Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
5 min
Distinguishing Tasawwur from Tasdiq
Author defines tasawwur and tasdiq and asserts the natural priority of tasawwur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasawwur (conceptualization) and tasdiq (assent) based on their objects.

Core Idea
Acquired knowledge splits into simple concepts and relational judgments.

Before you can construct or evaluate arguments, you must understand what kind of knowledge you are dealing with. The author begins by distinguishing between grasping a single meaning (tasawwur) and assenting to a relation (tasdiq). This is the foundational division of all acquired knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definitions
Find the lines in the Arabic passage where tasawwur and tasdiq are defined (lines 19-20).
2
Identify the genus and differentia
For tasawwur: genus is idrak (apprehension), differentia is mufrad (a single thing). For tasdiq: genus is idrak, differentia is nisba (relation).
Both are types of idrak, but differ in object.
3
Understand the natural priority
The author says tasawwur is prior by nature. Reflect on why a concept must precede a judgment.
Teaching order follows natural order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَنْواعُ العِلْمِ الحَادِثِ) (١٩) إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ : «تَصَوُّراً» عُلِمْ وَدَرْلُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ (٢٠) وَقَدِّمِ الأَوَّلَ عِنْدَ الوَضْعِ لأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّمَ بِالطَّبْعِ (۲۱) وَ(النَّظَرِي» : مَا احْتَاجَ لِلتَّأَمُّل وَعَكْسُهُ هُوَ الضَّرُورِيُّ» الجَلِي (۲۲) وَمَا بِهِ إِلَى تَصَوُّرٍ وُصِلْ يُدْعَى بِـ: «قَوْلِ شَارِحٍ فَلْتَبْتَهِلْ (۲۳) وَمَا لِتَصْدِيقِ بِهِ تُوُضِّلَا ب: «حُجَّةٍ» يُعْرَفُ عِنْدَ العُقَلَا
Types of acquired knowledge: (19) Apprehension of a single thing is known as 'tasawwur' (conceptualization), and apprehension of a relation is marked as 'tasdiq' (assent). (20) Present the first in teaching, for it is prior by nature. (21) 'Nadhari' (theoretical) is what requires reflection, and its opposite is the manifest 'dharuri' (necessary). (22) That by which one reaches a tasawwur is called 'qawl sharh' (explicative statement), so strive. (23) And that by which one reaches tasdiq is known as 'hujja' (argument) among the rational.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage classifies acquired knowledge. The author defines tasawwur as grasping a single concept (e.g., 'human') and tasdiq as judging a relation (e.g., 'human is rational'). Teaching should start with tasawwur because it is naturally prior. Knowledge is either nadhari (needs reflection) or dharuri (self-evident). The tool for tasawwur is qawl sharh (definition), and for tasdiq it is hujja (argument).

Key Terms
تصور
تصديق
نظري
ضروري
قول شارح
حجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the object of tasawwur?
A) A relation
B) A single thing
C) A judgment
D) An argument

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur is simple apprehension of a concept; tasdiq is relational apprehension (assent).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following as tasawwur or tasdiq: 'The world is created' (tasdiq), 'creation' (tasawwur), 'everything originated has a cause' (tasdiq).
?
Explain in one sentence why tasawwur is prior to tasdiq in teaching.

The Tools of Knowledge: Qawl Sharh and Hujja
Author distinguishes necessary from theoretical knowledge and names the tools for each type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between dharuri and nadhari knowledge, and identify qawl sharh and hujja as the respective tools for tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
Knowledge is either self-evident or inferred; each type requires its own tool: definition for concepts, argument for judgments.

After dividing knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, the author further splits knowledge into necessary (dharuri) and theoretical (nadhari). Moreover, he introduces the tools by which new tasawwur and tasdiq are acquired: qawl sharh (explicative statement) for tasawwur, and hujja (argument) for tasdiq. This provides the basic toolkit for expanding knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Find the dharuri/nadhari distinction
Look at line 21: 'Nadhari is what requires reflection; its opposite is the manifest dharuri.'
Dharuri knowledge is self-evident; nadhari needs reasoning.
2
Identify the criterion
The criterion is whether reflection (ta'ammul) is needed. Dharuri does not require it.
3
Locate the tools
Lines 22-23: 'That by which one reaches tasawwur is called qawl sharh... that by which one reaches tasdiq is called hujja.'
Qawl sharh includes definitions and descriptions; hujja includes syllogisms.
4
Connect tools to knowledge types
Qawl sharh produces new tasawwur; hujja produces new tasdiq.
Both tools are needed in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَنْواعُ العِلْمِ الحَادِثِ) (١٩) إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ : «تَصَوُّراً» عُلِمْ وَدَرْلُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ (٢٠) وَقَدِّمِ الأَوَّلَ عِنْدَ الوَضْعِ لأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّمَ بِالطَّبْعِ (۲۱) وَ(النَّظَرِي» : مَا احْتَاجَ لِلتَّأَمُّل وَعَكْسُهُ هُوَ الضَّرُورِيُّ» الجَلِي (۲۲) وَمَا بِهِ إِلَى تَصَوُّرٍ وُصِلْ يُدْعَى بِـ: «قَوْلِ شَارِحٍ فَلْتَبْتَهِلْ (۲۳) وَمَا لِتَصْدِيقِ بِهِ تُوُضِّلَا ب: «حُجَّةٍ» يُعْرَفُ عِنْدَ العُقَلَا
Types of acquired knowledge: (19) Apprehension of a single thing is known as 'tasawwur' (conceptualization), and apprehension of a relation is marked as 'tasdiq' (assent). (20) Present the first in teaching, for it is prior by nature. (21) 'Nadhari' (theoretical) is what requires reflection, and its opposite is the manifest 'dharuri' (necessary). (22) That by which one reaches a tasawwur is called 'qawl sharh' (explicative statement), so strive. (23) And that by which one reaches tasdiq is known as 'hujja' (argument) among the rational.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage classifies acquired knowledge. The author defines tasawwur as grasping a single concept (e.g., 'human') and tasdiq as judging a relation (e.g., 'human is rational'). Teaching should start with tasawwur because it is naturally prior. Knowledge is either nadhari (needs reflection) or dharuri (self-evident). The tool for tasawwur is qawl sharh (definition), and for tasdiq it is hujja (argument).

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
5 min
Subtypes of Tasawwur and Tasdiq
Tablawi explains that the plural 'tasawwurat' and 'tasdiqat' indicate multiple species within each category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the subtypes of tasawwur and tasdiq as classified by Tablawi and explain why the plural form is used.

Core Idea
The plural indicates multiple species within each category.

In the study of logic, we constantly encounter the terms tasawwur (conceptualization) and tasdiq (assent). But why are they sometimes written in the plural as tasawwurat and tasdiqat? The commentator Tablawi answers this by breaking down each into its distinct subtypes. Understanding this classification is key to grasping how knowledge is structured in the Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the puzzling usage
Notice that the base text uses the plurals 'التصورات' and 'التصديقات', even though the singular forms are verbal nouns. Why would the author do this? This is the starting point of Tablawi's explanation.
2
Extract the subtypes of tasawwur
Tablawi lists three subtypes: conceptualization of the subject (e.g., 'wajib al-wujud'), conceptualization of the predicate (e.g., 'existent'), and conceptualization of the relation between subject and predicate without assent (e.g., 'the world is created' without accepting it).
The third type is a conceptualization of a relation, not yet a judgment.
3
Extract the subtypes of tasdiq
Tablawi lists two subtypes: assent to a categorical proposition (e.g., 'the world is created' with acceptance) and assent to a conditional proposition (e.g., 'if the world is created, it has a creator' with acceptance). He adds 'and so on' hinting at further subdivisions.
The conditional subtype includes both conjunctive and disjunctive conditionals.
4
Connect to the reason for the plural
Because each term contains multiple distinct types (species), the plural is used even though they are masdars. The plural signals that we are referring to these various species collectively.
This is a common linguistic usage in Arabic when a generic term covers multiple categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (التَّصَوُّرَاتِ وَالتَّصْدِيقَاتِ) جمع التَّصور والتصديق مع أنَّهما مصدران؛ لاختلاف النَّوع؛ إذِ التَّصور: يكون تصور موضوع، ويكون تصور محمول، ويكون تصور نسبة بدون إذعان لها على ما سيأتي. والتصديق: يكون تصديقاً بنسبة قضيَّةٍ حملية، ويكون تصديقاً بنسبة قضيَّةٍ شرطيَّةٍ، إلى غير ذلك.
His statement: 'al-tasawwurat wa al-tasdiqat' is the plural of tasawwur and tasdiq despite both being masdars, due to difference of type. For tasawwur can be a conceptualization of a subject, a conceptualization of a predicate, or a conceptualization of a relation without assent, as will come. And tasdiq can be an assent to the relation of a categorical proposition, or an assent to the relation of a conditional proposition, and so on.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a commentary note by the super-commentator al-Tablawi on the phrase 'التصورات والتصديقات' in the main text. He addresses why the author used the plural form of two words that are normally singular masdars (verbal nouns). The reason is that each term encompasses multiple distinct types. For tasawwur (conceptualization), he identifies three types: conceptualization of the subject (e.g., 'wajib al-wujud'), conceptualization of the predicate (e.g., 'existent'), and conceptualization of the relation between subject and predicate without assent (e.g., 'the world is created' without accepting it as true). For tasdiq (assent), he lists two types: assent to the relation in a categorical proposition (e.g., 'the world is created' with acceptance) and assent to the relation in a conditional proposition (e.g., 'if the world is created, it has a creator' with acceptance). This classification is foundational for understanding the scope of knowledge in logic.

Key Terms
تصور
تصديق
قضية حملية
قضية شرطية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Tablawi, how many types of tasawwur (conceptualization) are there?
A) Two: subject and predicate
B) Three: subject, predicate, and relation
C) Four: subject, predicate, relation, and judgment
D) One: only the essence

Key Takeaway
The pluralization of tasawwur and tasdiq highlights the multiplicity of subtypes within each, a crucial insight for precise logical analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Provide your own example from Islamic jurisprudence (fiqh) for each of the three types of tasawwur: subject, predicate, and relation. For instance, think of the concept of 'riba' (usury) and its prohibition.
?
Determine whether the statement 'If a prayer is invalid, it must be repeated' is an instance of tasawwur or tasdiq. If tasdiq, is it categorical or conditional? Explain your reasoning using the classifications from this lesson.

Classification of Knowledge: Conceptual and Assertoric
Commentator defines 'نتائج الفكر' and distinguishes conceptual from assertoric knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conceptual (تصوري) and assertoric (تصديقي) knowledge and explain the commentator's specification of theoretical sciences.

Core Idea
Knowledge is either conceptual (simple apprehension) or assertoric (judgment); both require known premises to reach an unknown.

In this lesson, we examine how the commentator defines the key term 'نتائج الفكر' (results of thought) and establishes the fundamental classification of knowledge into conceptual and assertoric. Using concrete examples from logic and theology, you will learn to identify each type and understand why theoretical knowledge is the primary subject of praise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two known things
In both examples (definition of man and demonstration of world's temporality), the commentator describes two known things that are arranged. Identify what these two known things are in each case.
For the definition of man: genus and differentia. For the demonstration: the two premises.
2
Extract the unknown conclusion
The conclusion is the unknown that is reached by arranging the two known things. In the first example, it is the concept of man. In the second, it is the judgment that the world is temporal.
3
Distinguish conceptual vs assertoric
Notice that the first example yields a concept (what is man?), while the second yields a judgment (is the world temporal?). This is the core distinction between تصوري and تصديقي.
Conceptual knowledge is a simple apprehension; assertoric knowledge involves truth valuation.
4
Understand the objection and response
The imagined objection asks: why specify theoretical sciences when necessary sciences are also results of thought? The commentator answers that theoretical sciences are subject to dispute, so praise is more relevant. Also suggests a broader linguistic interpretation.
Necessary knowledge is directly from Allah and not acquired by effort, so it is even more deserving of praise.
5
Appreciate the linguistic interpretation
The commentator notes an alternative: 'نتائج الفكر' may be taken linguistically to include both necessary and theoretical sciences, as per al-Malawi. This shows flexibility in interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١) الحَمْدُ للهِ الَّذِي قَدْ أَخْرَجَا نَتَائِجَ الفِكْرِ لِأَرْبَابِ الحِـ
الباجوري
مَعْلُومَيْنِ لِيُتَوَصَّلَ بِهِمَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ (۱)؛ تَصَوُّريًّا كَانَ، أَوْ تَصْدِيقِيًّا». فَالأَوَّلُ كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الإِنْسَانِ»: «هُوَ : حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ، فَإِنَّ فِيهِ تَرْتِيبَ أَمْرَينِ مَعْلُومَيْنِ - وَهُمَا : الجِنْسُ وَالفَصْلُ - ؛ لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِهِمَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ تَصَوُّرِيٌّ - وَهُوَ الإِنْسَانُ» - وَالثَّانِي كَمَا فِي قَوْلِكَ فِي الِاسْتِدْلَالِ عَلَى حُدُوثِ العَالَمِ»: «العَالَمُ مُتَغِيِّرُ، وَكُلُّ مُتَغَيِّرٍ حَادِثُ، فَإِنَّ فِيهِ تَرْتِيبَ أَمْرَيْنِ مَعْلُومَيْنِ - وَهُمَا المُقَدِّمَتَانِ المَذْكُورَتَانِ - ؛ لِيَتَوَصَّلَ بِهِمَا إِلَى أَمْرٍ مَجْهُولٍ تَصْدِيقِيِّ - وَهُوَ : «ثُبُوتُ الحُدُوثِ لِلعَالَمِ» -.
فَإِنْ قِيلَ: لِمَ خَصَّ المُصَنِّفُ نَتَائِجَ الفِكْرِ» - الَّتِي هِيَ العُلُومُ النَّظَرِيَّةُ ـ بِالذِّكْرِ، مَعَ أَنَّ مِثْلُهَا - ذَلِكَ العُلُومَ الضَّرُورِيَّةَ؟
أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّ النَّظَرَيَّةَ مَحَلُّ الخِلَافِ بِخِلَافِ الضَّرُورِيَّةِ فَإِنَّهَا بِتَأْثِيرِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى اتِّفَاقاً، وَهُوَ بِصَدَدِ الرَّدُ، وَأَيْضاً : الضَّرُورِيَّةُ يُفْهَمُ الحَمْدُ عَلَيْهَا بِالأَوْلَى؛ إِذْ لَا كَسْبَ لِلعَبْدِ فِيهَا . عَلَى أَنَّهُ يُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّهُ أَرَادَ بِـ نَتَائِجَ الفِكْرِ» المَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيَّ، وَهُوَ : «مَا يَتَرَتَّبُ عَلَى حَرَكَةِ النَّفْسِ (۲) المَعْقُولَاتِ مِنَ العُلُومِ الضَّرُورِيَّةِ أَوِ النَّظَرِيَّةِ ؛ كَمَا أَفَادَهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ فِي كَبِيرِهِ (۳) .
The praise is to Allah who has produced the results of thought for the people of intellect. Two known things to arrive through them at an unknown thing, whether conceptual or assertoric. The first is like your saying in defining man: 'He is a rational animal,' for in it there is an arrangement of two known things – which are the genus and the differentia – to arrive through them at an unknown conceptual thing – which is man. And the second is like your saying in demonstrating the temporality of the world: 'The world is changing, and everything changing is temporal,' for in it there is an arrangement of two known things – which are the two mentioned premises – to arrive through them at an unknown assertoric thing – which is 'the affirmation of temporality for the world'. If it is said: Why did the author specify 'results of thought' – which are the theoretical sciences – in mention, while similar are the necessary sciences? The answer is: The theoretical is the subject of dispute, contrary to the necessary, for it is by the effect of Allah Almighty unanimously, and he is in a position of refutation. Also, the necessary are understood as praise more primarily since there is no acquisition for the servant in them. But it is possible that he intended by 'results of thought' the linguistic meaning, which is: 'what results from the movement of the soul in the intelligibles of necessary or theoretical sciences', as Shaykh al-Malawi conveyed in his major commentary.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that expands on the opening line of the matn, defining the term 'نتائج الفكر' (results of thought) and explaining the two types of knowledge: conceptual (تصوري) and assertoric (تصديقي). The commentator begins by clarifying the definition: knowledge is attained by arranging two known things (المعْلومين) to reach an unknown. He provides two examples: for conceptual knowledge, the definition of man as 'rational animal' uses the known genus and differentia to arrive at the concept of man. For assertoric knowledge, the demonstration of the world's temporality uses the known premises 'the world is changing' and 'everything changing is temporal' to conclude that the world is temporal. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: why does the author specify 'theoretical sciences' when necessary sciences are also results of thought? The answer is that theoretical sciences are matters of dispute, whereas necessary sciences are agreed upon and directly from Allah, so praise is more appropriate for theoretical knowledge. However, the commentator notes an alternative interpretation: 'نتائج الفكر' can be taken in a linguistic sense, meaning any knowledge resulting from intellectual movement, whether necessary or theoretical, as al-Malawi suggested.

Key Terms
نتائج الفكر
تصور
تصديق
علم نظري
علم ضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, what is the difference between conceptual (تصوري) and assertoric (تصديقي) knowledge?
A) Conceptual knowledge is certain, while assertoric knowledge is probable.
B) Conceptual knowledge is obtaining a concept (e.g., definition of man), while assertoric knowledge is a judgment (e.g., the world is temporal).
C) Conceptual knowledge is from the senses, assertoric from reason.
D) Conceptual knowledge is about objects, assertoric about actions.

Key Takeaway
The classification of knowledge into conceptual (تصوري) and assertoric (تصديقي) is essential for understanding how definitions and demonstrations function in Islamic logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether each of the following is conceptual or assertoric: (a) The definition of 'salat' as 'specific actions with intention'. (b) The judgment that 'salat is obligatory based on the Qur'an and Sunnah'.
?
Construct a conceptual definition of 'riba' using genus and differentia, and then an assertoric syllogism to prove that a specific transaction involves riba.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
5 min
The Relational Distinction Between Knowledge and the Known
Al-Anbabi on the epistemology of science naming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two views on the relationship between knowledge (ilm) and the known (ma'lum) and explain the consequence of each for the naming of sciences.

Core Idea
The distinction between knowledge and the known can be essential or relational; this affects how we define a science.

Al-Anbabi opens a subtle epistemological point: is knowledge separate from its object or do they coincide relationally? This distinction influences how we name sciences—are they proper names or generic? In this lesson, you will analyse the two positions and their implications for the discipline of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views on the difference between knowledge and known
Locate in the Arabic where Anbabi states 'mugheerat al-'ilm lil-ma'lum bi al-dhat' (essential difference) and then 'al-mughayara i'tibariyya' (relational difference). Understand that the first view sees them as separate in essence; the second sees them as the same thing considered relationally.
Relational difference means the same entity is called 'knowledge' when considered as an attribute and 'known' when considered as an object.
2
Understand the relational view's claim about mental existence
Anbabi notes that on the relational view, 'what exists in the mind is the very known, not the shadow or example.' This means the object of knowledge is directly present in the mind, not a representation.
3
Recognise the condition for the relational view to work
Anbabi says 'unless one is content with relational difference' — meaning the relational view is viable only if one accepts that the difference is not essential but merely conceptual.
He refers to his own hashiah on al-Sabban's treatise for more detail, indicating this is a refined position.
4
Apply the distinction to the naming of sciences
Consider how this distinction affects whether 'ilm al-mantiq' is a proper name (essential difference) or a descriptive term (relational difference). In the relational view, the science name refers to the same reality as the known subject matter.
This step connects the epistemological point to the broader topic of defining sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبابي بمغايرة العلم للمعلوم بالذات، أمَّا على أنَّ المغايرة اعتباريَّةٌ، وأنَّ الموجود في الذهن عين المعلوم لا الشَّبح والمثال فلا ؛ إلا أن يكتفي بالتَّغاير الاعتباري؛ أي: اعتبار كون الشَّيء معلوماً، وكونه علماً وإن أردت الزيادة، فعليك بحاشيتنا على رسالة الصَّبَّان البيانية . قوله : فَالمُرَادُ : أَنَّهُ يُرْقَى بِهِ لِمَا عَدَاهُ ... إلخ) هذا ظاهر على جعل التّركيب من باب التّصريحيَّة فقط، أو المكنية، مع جعل قرينتها استعارة تصريحيَّة تحقيقيَّة؛ لأنَّ السَّماء حينئذ المرقية بالسُّلَّم هي المسائل الصَّعبة، أمَّا على جعله من باب إضافة المشبه به إلى المشبَّه، أو المكنيَّة مع بقاء القرينة على حالها فلا؛ إذ المراد بعلم المنطق على هذا كله.
Al-Anbabi: Regarding the difference between knowledge and the known in essence. As for the view that the difference is relational and that what exists in the mind is the very known, not the image or example, then it does not [work?] unless one is content with relational difference, i.e., considering the thing as known and as knowledge. And if you want more, refer to our hashiah on al-Sabban's treatise on rhetoric. His statement: 'So the intended meaning is that it is ascended by it to what is other than it, etc.' This is apparent if the construct is taken as merely declarative (tasrihiyya) or as metaphorical (makniyya) with its qarina being a declarative investigative metaphor, because then the sky that is ascended by the ladder is the difficult issues. However, if it is taken as the addition of the analogized-to to the analogized, or as makniyya with the qarina remaining, then it is not [apparent], because the intended meaning of 'science of logic' in all this is [something else].
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary by al-Anbabi on the previous discussion. He first raises an epistemological point: the distinction between 'ilm (knowledge) and ma'lum (the known) is either essential or relational. If relational, then the object in the mind is the known itself, not a shadow. Then he comments on a statement (probably from Bajuri) that the intended meaning is that the book leads to other parts of logic. He analyzes the metaphor: if the construct 'sama' 'ilm al-mantiq' is taken as a declarative metaphor (tasrihiyya) or a makniyya with a declarative qarina, then the 'sky' represents the difficult issues of logic. But if it is taken as idafat al-mushabbah bihi ila al-mushabbah (as Bajuri interpreted), then the interpretation differs. This shows the layers of commentary in the Islamic logical tradition, where each generation refines the rhetorical analysis of the foundational texts.

Metaphor Analysis: The Sky of Logic as Difficult Issues
Al-Anbabi on the interpretation of the metaphor 'sky of logic'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the tasrihiyya and makniyya interpretations of the metaphor 'sama' 'ilm al-mantiq' and explain the consequence for understanding the purpose of logic.

Core Idea
The metaphor 'sky of logic' is interpreted differently depending on whether it is declarative or implicit, affecting what the 'sky' represents.

Anbabi analyzes the construct 'sama' ilm al-mantiq' (the sky of the science of logic). Depending on whether the metaphor is classified as tasrihiyya or makniyya, the 'sky' may represent either the difficult issues of logic or something else. This shows how rhetorical analysis refines our understanding of textbook metaphors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphor under discussion
Find the phrase 'sama' 'ilm al-mantiq' in the Arabic. It is a construct phrase where 'sama' (sky) is attributed to 'ilm al-mantiq' (the science of logic). Understand that this is a metaphor: logic is being likened to a sky.
The metaphor is part of a longer statement: 'it is ascended by it to what is other than it' — referring to the book of logic as a ladder.
2
Distinguish the two metaphorical interpretations
Anbabi presents two possible ways to interpret the construct: (1) as tasrihiyya (declarative metaphor) or as makniyya (implicit metaphor) with the qarina itself being a declarative metaphor; (2) as idafat al-mushabbah bihi ila al-mushabbah (addition of the analogized-to to the analogized) or as makniyya with the qarina remaining literal. In the first case, the 'sky' represents the difficult issues; in the second, it represents logic itself.
The qarina (قرينة) is the linguistic clue that indicates metaphor; here it is the word 'سُلَّم' (ladder).
3
Understand the implication of the first interpretation
If taken as tasrihiyya or makniyya with a declarative qarina, then 'the sky that is ascended by the ladder' refers to 'the difficult issues' (al-masa'il al-sa'ba). This means logic is a ladder to climb difficult problems.
This interpretation makes the metaphor consistent: a ladder ascends to a sky (difficult issues).
4
Understand the alternative interpretation
If taken as idafat al-mushabbah bihi ila al-mushabbah or as makniyya with qarina unchanged, then 'sky' is the analogized-to (the science of logic) and 'ladder' is the analogized (the book or method). In this case, the intended meaning is different: the book is a ladder to logic itself.
Anbabi says this interpretation is 'not apparent' (فلا), implying it does not fit the context.
5
Conclude which interpretation Anbabi favours
Anbabi's phrasing suggests that the first interpretation (tasrihiyya/makniyya with declarative qarina) is the apparent one (هذا ظاهر). The alternative is problematic because it changes what 'science of logic' refers to.
This shows how rhetorical classification determines the correct reading of a pedagogical metaphor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Ashʿari View on Knowledge and the Known
Anbabiy states the Ashʿari view that the difference between knowledge and its object is conventional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Ashʿari position that knowledge and the known are identical in essence and distinguish it from views positing essential difference or representationalism.

Core Idea
In Ashʿari epistemology, knowledge and the known are one; difference is conventional, not real.

This lesson clarifies a foundational point in Islamic epistemology: the relationship between knowledge (ʿilm) and its object (maʿlūm). The passage from al-Anbabiy presents the Ashʿari view that the mental existence of an object is identical to the object itself, not a mere representation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for navigating debates in kalām and logic about the nature of cognition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing views
Find in the passage the contrast between essential difference (al-mughāyara bi'adh-dhāt) and conventional difference (al-mughāyara iʿtibāriyya). The passage first rejects essential difference under Ashʿari assumptions.
The particle 'ammā indicates a conditional structure.
2
Understand the Ashʿari ontological commitment
Note the phrase 'al-mawjūdu fī adh-dhihn ʿayn al-maʿlūm'—what exists in the mind is the very same as the known object, not a shadow (shabah) or example (mithāl). This rejects representationalism.
3
Analyze the consequence for difference
If they are identical, no real difference exists. However, a conventional difference remains: the same entity can be considered as 'knowledge' (from the perspective of the soul) and as 'known' (from the perspective of its being apprehended).
The term iʿtibārī means a mental consideration without separate existence.
4
Relate to the broader kalām context
This position allows Ashʿaris to maintain a distinction in language without multiplying entities. It appears in definitions of knowledge, e.g., in al-Sanūsī's works.
The passage ends by directing to al-Anbabī's own ḥāshiya for deeper analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمغايرة العلم للمعلوم بالذات، أمَّا على أنَّ المغايرة اعتباريَّةٌ، وأنَّ الموجود في الذهن عين المعلوم لا الشَّبح والمثال فلا ؛ إلا أن يكتفي بالتَّغاير الاعتباري؛ أي: اعتبار كون الشَّيء معلوماً، وكونه علماً وإن أردت الزيادة، فعليك بحاشيتنا على رسالة الصَّبَّان البيانية.
Regarding the difference between knowledge and the known in essence: if the difference is considered conventional and that what exists in the mind is the same as the known, not a shadow or example, then no; unless one is satisfied with conventional difference, i.e., considering something as known and considering it as knowledge. And if you want more, refer to our hashiya on the Risāla al-Ṣabbān al-Bayāniyya.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This is a marginal note from al-Anbabiy clarifying the epistemological position of the Ashʿaris. The note addresses whether knowledge and the known are essentially distinct. Anbabiy states that if one holds the Ashʿari view that the difference is conventional (iʿtibārī) and that the mental form is exactly the known itself, not a mere representation (shabah) or example (mithāl), then there is no essential difference. However, one may still speak of a conventional difference: the same thing considered as 'knowledge' and considered as 'known'. This is sufficient for logic. Anbabiy then directs the reader to his own hashiya on al-Ṣabbān's work for further detail.

Key Terms

الموجود في الذهن
الشبح والمثال

D) When the mental form is a mere example.

Key Takeaway
In Ashʿari epistemology, knowledge and the known are identical in essence; their difference is merely conventional (iʿtibārī).

The Four Types of Acquired Knowledge
Author classifies knowledge into four types via two dichotomies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given piece of knowledge as a necessary concept, theoretical concept, necessary assent, or theoretical assent.

Core Idea
Knowledge divides into concept and assent, each either necessary or theoretical.

In this passage, al-Bajuri unpacks the classification of acquired knowledge. He shows that knowledge is first divided into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), and each of those is either necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari). This yields four distinct types. Understanding this grid is essential for analyzing the epistemological status of any claim in Islamic theology and logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary division
Notice that knowledge is first split into two categories: tasawwur (concept) and tasdiq (assent). A concept is mere apprehension without judgment, while assent includes a judgment of truth or falsehood.
For example, knowing the meaning of 'creator' is a concept; affirming that Allah is the creator is an assent.
2
Identify the secondary division
Each of these two is then divided into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari). Necessary knowledge is immediate and requires no reasoning; theoretical knowledge requires proof.
The examples given in the source: necessary knowledge is like knowing that the whole is greater than the part.
3
Construct the 2x2 grid
Combine the divisions: there are four types: necessary concept, theoretical concept, necessary assent, theoretical assent. This is the classification the author implies.
The grid helps locate any piece of knowledge precisely.
4
Apply to a theological example
Take a typical statement from Kalam: 'The world is temporally originated.' This is an assent (it affirms something). Is it necessary or theoretical? It is theoretical because it requires proof (the argument from contingency). So it is a theoretical assent.
Practice by classifying other knowledge claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (أَنْواعُ العِلْمِ الحَادِثِ) أَي : الَّتِي هِيَ أَرْبَعَةٌ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِنِ اسْتِقْصَاءِ كَلَامِهِ، وَذَلِكَ لأَنَّ العِلْمَ : إِمَّا تَصَوُّرٌ , وَإِمَّا تَصْدِيقٌ ; وَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا: إِمَّا ضَرُورِيٌّ، وَإِمَّا نَظَرِيٌّ. وَتَعَرَّضَ المُصَنِّفُ لِتَنْوِيعِ العِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَتَعَرَّضُ لِحَدِّهِ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الخِلَافِ، حَتَّى قَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِتَعَذُّرِهِ، وَقَالَ الإِمَامُ الرَّازِيُّ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِكَوْنِهِ ضَرُوريًّا. قوله : (حَتَّى قَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِتَعَذُّرِهِ) عبارة جمع الجوامع: والعِلمُ قَالَ الإِمَامُ : ضَرُورِيٌّ، ثُمَّ قَالَ : هُوَ حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ الجَازِمُ المُطَابِقُ لِمُوجِبٍ. وَقِيْلَ : هُوَ ضَرُورِيٌّ فَلَا يُحَدُّ . وَقَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ : عَسِرٌ ، فَالرَّأيُّ الإمْسَاكُ عَنْ تَعْرِيفِهِ.
His statement: (Types of acquired knowledge) means: the ones that are four, as is known from surveying his words. That is because knowledge is either a concept (tasawwur) or an assent (tasdiq); and each of them is either necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari). And the author undertook the classification of knowledge, but he did not undertake its definition due to the disagreement about it, to the extent that Imam al-Haramayn said: It cannot be defined because it is impossible, and al-Imam al-Razi said: It should not be defined because it is necessary. He said: (To the extent that Imam al-Haramayn said: It cannot be defined because it is impossible) is an expression from Jam' al-Jawami': Knowledge, al-Imam said, is necessary, then he said: It is the firm judgment of the mind corresponding to what necessitates it. And it was said: It is necessary, so it is not defined. And Imam al-Haramayn said: It is difficult, so the opinion is to refrain from defining it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's section heading 'Types of acquired knowledge' (anwa' al-'ilm al-hadith). The commentator, al-Bajuri, first explains that from a survey of the author's subsequent discussion, the types are four. This classification is based on a bipartite division: knowledge is either a concept (tasawwur) or an assent (tasdiq), and each of these is either necessary (daruri, known without inquiry) or theoretical (nazari, acquired through reasoning). This yields a 2x2 grid: necessary concept, theoretical concept, necessary assent, theoretical assent. Then the commentator notes that the author of the matn classified knowledge but deliberately avoided giving a definition (hadd) of knowledge itself, because there is disagreement among scholars on whether and how to define it. He cites two authorities: Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) held that it cannot be defined because it is inherently impossible (ta'addhur), and Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi held that it should not be defined because it is a necessary concept; attempting to define it is misguided. The Anbabi insertion, which is part of the lesson, clarifies further by quoting from Jam' al-Jawami': al-Imam (presumably al-Razi) initially said knowledge is necessary, but then he also gave a definition: 'the firm judgment of the mind corresponding to what necessitates it.' This shows some ambivalence. Then it repeats that some say it is necessary and thus undefinable, while al-Juwayni found it difficult and recommended refraining (imsak) from defining it. This passage thereby highlights the epistemological caution within the tradition regarding the first principles.

Key Terms
تصور
تصديق
ضروري
نظري

B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Acquired knowledge is exhaustively divided into four types: necessary concept, theoretical concept, necessary assent, and theoretical assent.

Why 'Ilm Cannot Be Defined: The Controversy
Author discusses the controversy over defining 'ilm, citing al-Juwayni and al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarize the arguments of Imam al-Haramayn and al-Imam al-Razi against defining 'ilm.

Core Idea
Defining knowledge is either impossible or unnecessary because knowledge is a necessary concept.

After noting that the matn author avoided defining 'ilm, al-Bajuri cites two prominent scholars who gave reasons for this avoidance. Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) held that defining 'ilm is inherently impossible, while Fakhr al-Din al-Razi argued that it is a necessary concept and therefore cannot—and should not—be defined. This debate reveals deep epistemological caution in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two authorities
Locate the names: Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and al-Imam al-Razi. They are invoked to justify why the author did not define 'ilm.
These are major figures in Ash'ari Kalam and Usul.
2
Extract al-Juwayni's reason
Al-Juwayni is quoted: 'It cannot be defined because it is impossible (ta'addhur).' This means that 'ilm is so fundamental that any definition would be circular or presuppose what it defines.
This position is based on the idea that definition requires prior knowledge of something simpler, but 'ilm is simple.
3
Extract al-Razi's reason
Al-Razi is quoted: 'It should not be defined because it is necessary (daruri).' That is, 'ilm is self-evident and immediately known, so attempting to define it is unnecessary and may lead to confusion.
Al-Razi's own definition in other works shows nuance: he says it is necessary but also gives a description.
4
Understand the nuance from Jam' al-Jawami'
The commentary then adds that al-Razi first said 'ilm is necessary, but then defined it as 'the firm judgment of the mind corresponding to what necessitates it.' This shows that even scholars who say it is necessary may still offer a definition, but they treat it as an explanation rather than a true definition (hadd).
This distinction is critical for advanced study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (أَنْواعُ العِلْمِ الحَادِثِ) أَي : الَّتِي هِيَ أَرْبَعَةٌ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِنِ اسْتِقْصَاءِ كَلَامِهِ، وَذَلِكَ لأَنَّ العِلْمَ : إِمَّا تَصَوُّرٌ , وَإِمَّا تَصْدِيقٌ ; وَكُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا: إِمَّا ضَرُورِيٌّ، وَإِمَّا نَظَرِيٌّ. وَتَعَرَّضَ المُصَنِّفُ لِتَنْوِيعِ العِلْمِ، وَلَمْ يَتَعَرَّضُ لِحَدِّهِ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الخِلَافِ، حَتَّى قَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِتَعَذُّرِهِ، وَقَالَ الإِمَامُ الرَّازِيُّ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِكَوْنِهِ ضَرُوريًّا. قوله : (حَتَّى قَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ: لَا يُحَدُّ لِتَعَذُّرِهِ) عبارة جمع الجوامع: والعِلمُ قَالَ الإِمَامُ : ضَرُورِيٌّ، ثُمَّ قَالَ : هُوَ حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ الجَازِمُ المُطَابِقُ لِمُوجِبٍ. وَقِيْلَ : هُوَ ضَرُورِيٌّ فَلَا يُحَدُّ . وَقَالَ إِمَامُ الحَرَمَيْنِ : عَسِرٌ ، فَالرَّأيُّ الإمْسَاكُ عَنْ تَعْرِيفِهِ.
His statement: (Types of acquired knowledge) means: the ones that are four, as is known from surveying his words. That is because knowledge is either a concept (tasawwur) or an assent (tasdiq); and each of them is either necessary (daruri) or theoretical (nazari). And the author undertook the classification of knowledge, but he did not undertake its definition due to the disagreement about it, to the extent that Imam al-Haramayn said: It cannot be defined because it is impossible, and al-Imam al-Razi said: It should not be defined because it is necessary. He said: (To the extent that Imam al-Haramayn said: It cannot be defined because it is impossible) is an expression from Jam' al-Jawami': Knowledge, al-Imam said, is necessary, then he said: It is the firm judgment of the mind corresponding to what necessitates it. And it was said: It is necessary, so it is not defined. And Imam al-Haramayn said: It is difficult, so the opinion is to refrain from defining it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's section heading 'Types of acquired knowledge' (anwa' al-'ilm al-hadith). The commentator, al-Bajuri, first explains that from a survey of the author's subsequent discussion, the types are four. This classification is based on a bipartite division: knowledge is either a concept (tasawwur) or an assent (tasdiq), and each of these is either necessary (daruri, known without inquiry) or theoretical (nazari, acquired through reasoning). This yields a 2x2 grid: necessary concept, theoretical concept, necessary assent, theoretical assent. Then the commentator notes that the author of the matn classified knowledge but deliberately avoided giving a definition (hadd) of knowledge itself, because there is disagreement among scholars on whether and how to define it. He cites two authorities: Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) held that it cannot be defined because it is inherently impossible (ta'addhur), and Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi held that it should not be defined because it is a necessary concept; attempting to define it is misguided. The Anbabi insertion, which is part of the lesson, clarifies further by quoting from Jam' al-Jawami': al-Imam (presumably al-Razi) initially said knowledge is necessary, but then he also gave a definition: 'the firm judgment of the mind corresponding to what necessitates it.' This shows some ambivalence. Then it repeats that some say it is necessary and thus undefinable, while al-Juwayni found it difficult and recommended refraining (imsak) from defining it. This passage thereby highlights the epistemological caution within the tradition regarding the first principles.

الإمام الرازي
تعذر
ضروري
تعريف

Key Takeaway
Two major Ash'ari scholars argued against defining 'ilm: al-Juwayni said it is impossible, al-Razi said it is necessary and thus undefinable.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
8 min
Why Allah's Knowledge Cannot Be Defined as Tasawwur or Tasdiq
Bajuri explains the chosen definition of knowledge and its restriction to the temporal realm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the theological reason why definitions of knowledge involving idrak (perception) cannot apply to Allah and identify the logical steps in this argument.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge is beyond human categories because those imply a body and soul.

In this passage, al-Bajuri presents the preferred definition of knowledge as absolute perception, but immediately guards against applying it to Allah. He shows that the very terms tasawwur and tasdiq are tied to a bodily process. This critical refinement demonstrates how logical definitions in Islamic sciences must be carefully circumscribed to preserve divine transcendence. Let us follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition being discussed
The author states the chosen definition is that knowledge is absolute perception (mutlaq al-idrak), not the more specific 'perception of the truth-bearing ratio'.
Note that the specificity matters: absolute perception is broader and can be divided into tasawwur and tasdiq later.
2
Note the qualifying term 'al-hadith'
The text explicitly restricts the definition to acquired/temporal knowledge, thereby excluding Allah's knowledge.
The adjective 'hadith' is crucial for theological precision.
3
Trace the reason for exclusion
Because tasawwur and tasdiq are defined as idrak, which is 'the soul's arrival at the full meaning', a property of bodies. Applying this to Allah would imply He has a body and soul.
Idrak is inherently linked to a soul that receives forms, which is a created attribute.
4
Consider the attempted reinterpretation
The author notes that even if one reinterprets tasawwur and tasdiq for Allah (as His knowledge of simples and relations), the terms still carry temporal implications because they are tied to idrak.
Al-Bajuri rejects this as insufficient; the linguistic and conceptual baggage remains.
5
Conclude the theological necessity
Thus, Allah's knowledge cannot be categorized under the human logical divisions without compromising tawhid.
This shows how logic must serve theology, not the reverse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَكِنَّ المُخْتَارَ : أَنَّهُ يُحَدُّ، فَحَدَّهُ بَعْضُ الأُصُولِيِّينَ بـ: «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ التَّصْدِيقِيَّةِ»، وَلَيْسَ مُرَاداً هُنَا، وَإِنَّمَا المُرَادُ بِهِ : مُطْلَقُ الإِدْرَاكِ ; بِدَلِيلِ التَّقْسِيمِ الآتي. وَاحْتَرَزَ بِقَوْلِهِ : الحَادِثِ عَنْ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى إِشْعَاراً بِأَنَّهُ لا يَتَّصِفُ بِكَوْنِهِ تَصَوُّراً أَوْ تَصْدِيقاً، وَلَا بِكَوْنِهِ نَظَرِيًّا أَوْ ضَرُورِيًّا ; لأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنَ التَّصَوُّرِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ مُفَسَّرٌ بِالإِدْرَاكِ، وَهُوَ : وُصُولُ النَّفْسِ إِلَى تَمَامِ المَعْنَى، وَذَلِكَ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الأَجْسَامِ، فَفِي وَصْفِ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى بِذَلِكَ إِيهَامُ أَنَّ لَهُ تَعَالَى جِسْماً وَنَفْساً تَنْطَبِعُ فِيهَا صُورَةُ المَعْلُومَاتِ، وَلِهَذَا يَمْتَنِعُ إِطْلَاقُ ذَلِكَ، وَلَوْ أُرِيدَ بِهِ مَعْنَىً صَحِيحٌ ; كَأَنْ يُرَادَ بِالتَّصَوُّرِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى : عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يُسَمَّى العِلْمُ بِهِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا تَصَوُّراً، وَهُوَ المُفْرَدُ كَـ : «زَيْدٍ»، وَبِالتَّصْدِيقِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى : عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يُسَمَّى العِلْمُ بِهِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا تَصْدِيقاً، وَهُوَ النِّسْبَةُ كَ: «نِسْبَةِ القِيَامِ لِزَيْدٍ». وَلِأَنَّ النَّظَرِيَّ مُفَسَّرٌ بِـ : مَا يَحْصُلُ عَنْ نَظَرٍ وَاسْتِدْلَالٍ، وَهُوَ يَقْتَضِي الحُدُوثَ ; لِكَوْنِهِ مَسْبُوقاً بِالنَّظَرِ وَالاسْتِدْلَالِ.
However, the chosen opinion is that it can be defined. Some usuliyyun defined it as: 'the perception of the truth-bearing ratio (al-nisbat al-tasdiqiyya)', but that is not intended here. What is intended here is absolute perception, as evidenced by the upcoming division. And by his saying 'al-hadith' (acquired/temporal), he excluded knowledge of Allah, indicating that it is not described as being a concept or an assent, nor as being theoretical or necessary. Because each of tasawwur and tasdiq is interpreted as perception, which is: the soul's arriving at the full meaning, and that is a property of bodies. Thus, describing Allah's knowledge as such implies that He has a body and a soul in which the forms of known things are imprinted. Therefore, it is prohibited to apply that. Even if a sound meaning were intended, such as intending by 'tasawwur' in His case: His knowledge of what is called, in relation to us, 'concept' (al-mufrad like 'Zayd'), and by 'tasdiq' in His case: His knowledge of what is called, in relation to us, 'assent' (the external relation like 'the relation of standing to Zayd'). And because the theoretical is interpreted as that which is obtained from reflection and inference, and it necessitates temporality because it is preceded by reflection and inference.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage from al-Bajuri presents the preferred opinion that knowledge can indeed be defined, contrary to the previous hesitation. It first notes that some usuliyyun (jurists) defined knowledge as 'perception of the truth-bearing ratio' (idrak al-nisbat al-tasdiqiyya), but al-Bajuri clarifies that in this context the intended meaning is simply 'absolute perception' (mutlaq al-idrak), not the ratio-specific definition. This is supported by the upcoming division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq, which would not be possible if knowledge were already defined as perception of a ratio. Then he explains the significance of the adjective 'al-hadith' (temporal/acquired) in the original text: it excludes Allah's knowledge. Why? Because tasawwur and tasdiq are both explained as 'perception' (idrak), defined as 'the soul's arriving at the full meaning'. This process implies a soul that receives forms, which is a property of physical bodies. Attributing such a process to Allah would imply that He has a body and a soul, which is unacceptable in Islamic theology. Therefore, these categories cannot be applied to Allah's knowledge. Even if one attempted to reinterpret them in a sound manner — e.g., tasawwur as His knowledge of simple concepts, and tasdiq as His knowledge of relations — the very terms carry implications of temporality and physicality. Moreover, the theoretical (nazari) is defined as that which results from reflection and inference, which implies being preceded by thought, hence temporality. Thus, Allah's knowledge is beyond these divisions.

حادث

Why the Qualifier 'al-Hadith' in the Division of Knowledge
Author explains why the qualifier 'al-hadith' is necessary and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the qualifier 'al-hadith' is necessary in the division of knowledge and evaluate the objection that it is redundant due to the word 'anwa' (types).

Core Idea
The qualifier 'al-hadith' safeguards divine transcendence by excluding God's knowledge from categories tied to physicality and temporality.

In this passage from al-Bajuri's hashiya, the commentator defends the author's addition of 'al-hadith' (temporal) in the division of knowledge into tasawwur/tasdiq and dharuri/nazari. He shows that without this qualifier, one might wrongly include divine knowledge, leading to serious theological errors. An objection that the word 'anwa' (types) already excludes divine knowledge is carefully refuted, revealing deeper issues about how logical divisions must respect Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem with Applying Division to Divine Knowledge
Read the passage and note why tasawwur and tasdiq cannot be applied to God. Both involve 'perception' (idrak), which requires a soul reaching the meaning—a property of bodies. Applying them to God falsely implies He has a body and soul.
2
Analyse the Problem with 'Nazari' and 'Dharuri'
Understand that 'nazari' (theoretical) entails temporality because it is preceded by reasoning, which cannot apply to God. 'Dharuri' (necessary) implies compulsion (darura), impossible for God. Even though the meaning of 'dharuri' as 'self-evident' could be correct, the term carries a false implication.
3
Examine the Objection: Is 'anwa' Sufficient?
The objection says that the qualifier is redundant because the word 'anwa' (types) already excludes divine knowledge, since God has no types. Identify this objection in the text.
4
Evaluate the First Answer: Multiple Knowledge in Type
The first answer is that the qualifier is needed on the view of some Sunni scholars who hold that God's knowledge multiplies with known objects. Without 'al-hadith', one might think this multiplication is by type, which would wrongly include divine knowledge. But actually, it is by individual, not type. So 'anwa' alone does not exclude it.
5
Consider the Better Answer: Authorial Clarity
The commentator offers a better answer: the author added the qualifier simply for explicit clarification, especially for those unaware that God's knowledge does not diversify by type. This shows a pedagogical motive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَكِنَّ المُخْتَارَ : أَنَّهُ يُحَدُّ، فَحَدَّهُ بَعْضُ الأُصُولِيِّينَ بـ: «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ التَّصْدِيقِيَّةِ»، وَلَيْسَ مُرَاداً هنا، وَإِنَّمَا المُرَادُ بِهِ : مُطْلَقُ الإِدْرَاكِ ؛ بِدَلِيلِ التَّقْسِيمِ الآتي. وَاحْتَرَزَ بِقَوْلِهِ : الحَادِثِ عَنْ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى إِشْعَاراً بِأَنَّهُ لا يَتَّصِفُ بِكَوْنِهِ تَصُوْراً أَوْ تَصْدِيقاً، وَلَا بِكَوْنِهِ نَظَرِيًّا أَوْ ضَرُورِيًّا : لأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنَ التَّصُوْرِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ مُفَسَّرٌ بِالإِدْرَاكِ، وَهُوَ : وُصُولُ النَّفْسِ إِلَى تَمَامِ المَعْنَى، وَذَلِكَ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الأَجْسَامِ ، فَفِي وَصْفِ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى بِذَلِكَ إِيهَامُ أَنَّ لَهُ تَعَالَى جِسْماً وَنَفْساً تَنْطَبِعُ فِيهَا صُورَةُ المَعْلُومَاتِ، وَلِهَذَا يَمْتَنِعُ إِطْلَاقُ ذَلِكَ، وَلَوْ أُرِيدَ بِهِ مَعْنَى صَحِيحٍ ; كَأَنْ يُرَادَ بِالتَّصَوُّرِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى : عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يُسَمَّى العِلْمُ بِهِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا تَصَوُّراً، وَهُوَ المُفْرَدُ كَـ: «زَيْدِ» ، وَبِالتَّصْدِيقِ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى : عِلْمُهُ بِمَا يُسَمَّى العِلْمُ بِهِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْنَا تَصْدِيقاً، وَهُوَ النِّسْبَةُ كَ: «نِسْبَةِ القِيَامِ لِزَيْدِ». - وَلِأَنَّ النَّظَرِيَّ مُفَسَّرُ بِـ : مَا يَحْصُلُ عَنْ نَظَرٍ وَاسْتِدْلَالٍ ، وَهُوَ يَقْتَضِي الحُدُوثَ ; لِكَوْنِهِ مَسْبُوقاً بِالنَّظَرِ وَالاسْتِدْلَالِ . - وَأَمَّا الضَّرُورِيُّ فَهُوَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعْنَاهُ - أَعْنِي : مَا لَمْ يَحْصُلْ عَنْ نَظَرٍ وَاسْتِدْلَالٍ - صَحِيحاً فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، لَكِنَّ إِطْلَاقَهُ عَلَى عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى فِيهِ إِيهَامُ مُقَارَنَتِهِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ؛ لِإِطْلَاقِ الضَّرُورِيِّ عَلَى مَا اقْتَضَتْهُ الضَّرُورَةُ، وَذَلِكَ مُسْتَحِيلٌ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى . فَإِنْ قِيلَ: لَا حَاجَةَ لِزِيَادَةِ المُصَنِّفِ لِهَذَا القَيْدِ؛ لِخُرُوجِ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى بِلَفْظِ الْأَنْوَاعِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا أَنْوَاعَ لَهُ. أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ قَيَّدَ بِذَلِكَ ، لِيُخْرِجَ عِلْمَهُ تَعَالَى حَتَّى عَلَى قَوْلِ بَعْضِ أَكَابِرِ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ : أَنَّ عِلْمَهُ تَعَالَى يَتَعَدَّدُ بِتَعَدُّدِ المَعْلُومِ. وَفِيهِ : أَنَّ هَذَا يَقْتَضِي أَنَّ القَائِلَ بِذَلِكَ يَقُولُ : بِأَنَّ تَعَدُّدَ العِلْمِ بِتَعَدُّدِ المَعْلُومِ تَعَدُّدٌ بِالنَّوْعِ، وَلَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ، بَلْ يَقُولُ : بِأَنَّ تَعَدُّدَهُ بِذَلِكَ تَعَدُّدٌ بِالشَّخْصِ فِي مَا يَظْهَرُ . فَالأَوْلَى الجَوَابُ : بِأَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ أَرَادَ الإِيضَاحَ، فَزَادَ القَيْدَ المَذْكُورَ تَصْرِيحاً بِالمَقْصُودِ لَا سِيَّمَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَعْلَمْ عَدَمَ تَنَوُّعِ عِلْمِهِ تَعَالَى، فَلْيُتَأمَّلْ .
But the chosen view is that it is defined. So some of the scholars of usul defined it as: 'It is the perception of the predicative relation.' But that is not intended here. Rather, what is intended by it is absolute perception, as evidenced by the coming division. And he guarded by his saying 'the temporal' against His knowledge, exalted is He, indicating that it is not described as being conceptualization or assent, nor as being theoretical or necessary. Because each of conceptualization and assent is interpreted as perception, and it is the soul's reaching the complete meaning, and that is from the properties of bodies. So in describing His knowledge, exalted is He, with that there is an implication that He, exalted is He, has a body and a soul in which the form of known things imprints. Therefore, the application of that is prohibited, even if a sound meaning is intended by it. For example, if by 'conceptualization' with respect to Him, exalted is He, is meant His knowledge of what is called with respect to us conceptualization, and it is the simple term like 'Zayd', and by 'assent' with respect to Him, exalted is He, is meant His knowledge of what is called with respect to us assent, and it is the relation like the relation of standing to Zayd. And because 'theoretical' is interpreted as what is obtained from investigation and inference, and it necessitates temporality, because it is preceded by investigation and inference. As for the necessary knowledge, although its meaning—I mean, what is not obtained from investigation and inference—is correct with respect to Him, exalted is He, but applying it to His knowledge, exalted is He, contains an implication of its being accompanied by compulsion, because 'necessary' is applied to what necessity requires, and that is impossible with respect to Him, exalted is He. For if it is said: There is no need for the author to add this qualification, because His knowledge, exalted is He, is excluded by the word 'types', since He has no types. The answer is: The author qualified with that to exclude His knowledge, exalted is He, even according to the statement of some prominent Ahl al-Sunnah that His knowledge, exalted is He, multiplies with the multiplicity of the known. And there is in it: That this requires that the one who says that says that the multiplicity of knowledge with the multiplicity of the known is a multiplicity in type, and it is not like that. Rather, he says that its multiplicity by that is a multiplicity in individual, as appears. So the better answer is: The author intended clarification, so he added the mentioned qualification as an explicit statement of the intended purpose, especially with respect to one who does not know the non-diversification of His knowledge, exalted is He. So let it be considered.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion from a hashiya on the Sullam al-Munawraq. It focuses on the need for the qualifier 'al-hadith' (temporal) in the division of knowledge. The author begins by stating the chosen view that knowledge is definable, and cites a definition from some usul scholars: 'It is the perception of the predicative relation.' However, he clarifies that this definition is not intended here; rather, by 'knowledge' is meant absolute perception, as evidenced by the upcoming division into tasawwur and tasdiq. Then he explains why the author of the matn used the term 'al-hadith' (temporal) to qualify 'knowledge': it is to exclude the knowledge of Allah (Exalted is He). The reason is that divine knowledge cannot be described as either tasawwur (conceptualization) or tasdiq (assent), nor as nazari (theoretical) or dharuri (necessary). Tasawwur and tasdiq are both defined as perception, which involves the soul's reaching the complete meaning of something, and that is a property of bodies (since it implies a receptive soul). Applying such terms to God would falsely imply that He has a body and a soul that receives forms. Even if one tries to reinterpret them in a sound manner (e.g., understanding tasawwur as God's knowledge of simple terms, and tasdiq as His knowledge of relations), the standard terms still carry undesired implications. Similarly, 'nazari' (theoretical) is defined as knowledge obtained through investigation and inference, which entails temporality (since it is preceded by reasoning). This cannot apply to God. As for 'dharuri' (necessary), although its meaning—knowledge not obtained from reasoning—is true of God, calling it 'dharuri' suggests that it is compelled by necessity, which is impossible for God. Next, an objection is raised: the qualifier 'al-hadith' seems redundant because the word 'types' (anwa') already excludes divine knowledge, since God's knowledge is not multiple in type. The answer is that the qualification is needed even on the view of some prominent Sunni scholars who hold that God's knowledge multiplies with the multiplicity of known things. One might think this multiplication is by type, but actually it is by individual (i.e., many individual instances, not distinct types). Therefore, 'anwa'' could be misinterpreted as restricting the division to types, not covering the individual multiplicity. Hence, adding 'al-hadith' clarifies that only temporal knowledge is being divided. A better answer, the commentator says, is that the author simply intended to be explicit, especially for those unaware that God's knowledge does not diversify in type. Thus, the qualifier serves as an explicit clarification.

Key Terms
العلم الحادث
التصور
التصديق
الضروري
النظري

D) To emphasize that all knowledge is temporal

Key Takeaway
The qualifier 'al-hadith' is essential in the division of knowledge to exclude divine knowledge, because applying terms like tasawwur, tasdiq, nazari, and dharuri to God would imply physicality, temporality, or compulsion, contradicting divine transcendence.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Definition of Tasawwur and Its Two Main Modes
Commentator defines tasawwur and explains its modes and types of internal relations, including a critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between non-relational and relational tasawwur and identify the three subtypes within each.

Core Idea
Tasawwur includes not only bare concepts but also certain internal relations without judgment.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the scope of tasawwur (conceptualization). He explains that it can be either completely free of any relation or involve a non-external (mental) relation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how logic divides knowledge into conceptualization and assent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining phrase
Locate the definition: 'idrak mufrad' (apprehension of a single concept). Note that 'single concept' means without a full propositional judgment.
2
Classify the two main cases
The passage divides tasawwur into two: (a) no relation at all, and (b) a relation that is non-external. Write them down.
3
Enumerate the three non-relational subtypes
List: (i) subject alone, (ii) predicate alone, (iii) both subject and predicate without the relation.
These are cases where there is no relation at all.
4
Enumerate the three relational subtypes
List: verbal relation (nisba kalāmiyya), relational relation (nisba iḍāfiyya), and explicatory relation (nisba tafsīliyya).
These are internal, mental relations.
5
Test with examples
Take the examples given (Zayd, standing, Zayd son of Amr, rational animal) and classify each as which type of tasawwur.

قَوْلُهُ : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ ... إلخ) المُرَادُ بِـ إِدْرَاكِ المُفْرَدِ : الإِدْرَاكُ الَّذِي لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقْ بِالنِّسْبَةِ الخَارِجِيَّةِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِنْعَانِ : - بِأَنْ لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِنِسْبَةٍ أَصْلًا ، وَذَلِكَ : إِدْرَاكُ المَوْضُوعِ وَحْدَهُ ، وَإِدْرَاكُ المَحْمُولِ وَحْدَهُ، وَإِدْرَاكُهُمَا دُونَ النِّسْبَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا. أَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِنِسْبَةٍ غَيْرِ خَارِجِيَّةٍ ، وَذَلِكَ : إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ ثُبُوتُ المَحْمُولِ لِلمَوْضُوعِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِثْبَاتِ فِي القَضِيَّةِ المُوجَبَةِ، وَعَلَى وَجْهِ النَّفْيِ فِي القَضِيَّةِ السَّالِبَةِ ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ أَوْ خَبَرِيَّةٌ، وَإِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ الإِضَافِيَّةِ كَالنِّسْبَةِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : زَيْدُ بْنُ عَمْرٍو وَهِيَ بُنُوَّةُ زَيْدٍ لِعَمْرِو، وَإِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ التَّفْسِيدِيَّةِ كَالنِّسْبَةِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ وَهِيَ كَوْنُ الثَّانِي صِفَةٌ لِلأَوَّلِ . قَالَ الْأَنْبَابِيُّ: قَوْلُهُ: (وَإِدْرَاكُهُمَا دُونَ النِّسْبَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا) فِيهِ: أَنَّ تَصَوُّرَهُمَا يَسْتَدْعِي تَصَوُّرَ النِّسْبَةِ؛ إِذْ مَتَى لُوحِظَ طَرَفَاهَا حَصَلَتْ. وَقَدْ يُقَالُ: لَا نُسَلِّمُ ذَلِكَ؛ إِذْ لَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ تَصَوُّرِ مَا صَدَقَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعِ كَـ«زَيْدٍ»، وَمَا صَدَقَاتِ الْمَحْمُولِ كَـ«قَائِمٍ»، وَلَا مِنْ تَصَوُّرِهِمَا مَعًا بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ ارْتِبَاطِ أَحَدِهِمَا بِالْآخَرِ تَصَوُّرُ النِّسْبَةِ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمُرَادُ، لَا مَا فَهِمَهُ.
His statement: 'Apprehension of a single concept... etc.' What is meant by 'apprehension of a single concept' is apprehension that is not related to an external relation in the mode of affirmation: i.e., either it is not related to any relation at all, and that is: apprehension of the subject alone, apprehension of the predicate alone, and apprehension of both without the relation between them; or it is related to a non-external relation, and that is: apprehension of the verbal relation which is the establishment of the predicate for the subject in the mode of affirmation in an affirmative proposition, and in the mode of negation in a negative proposition, whether they are performative or declarative; and apprehension of the relational relation, like the relation in your saying: Zayd son of Amr, which is the sonship of Zayd to Amr; and apprehension of the explicatory relation, like the relation in your saying: rational animal, which is the second being a description of the first. Al-Anbabi said: His statement: 'and apprehension of both without the relation between them' – there is an objection: that their conceptualization necessitates the conceptualization of the relation, since whenever its two ends are considered, it occurs. And it may be said: We do not accept that; for the conceptualization of the referents of the subject, like 'Zayd', and the referents of the predicate, like 'standing', nor the conceptualization of both together without considering the connection of one to the other, does not entail the conceptualization of the relation. This is what is meant, not what he understood.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage defines tasawwur (conceptualization) as the apprehension of a single concept (mufrad). The commentator first explains that 'apprehension of a single concept' means apprehension that either is completely free from any relation (external or internal) or is related only to a non-external, mental relation. The non-relational case includes three possibilities: apprehending the subject alone, the predicate alone, or both together without any relation between them. The relational case includes three types of internal relations: the verbal relation (nisba kalāmiyya), which is the affirmation or negation in a proposition; the relational relation (nisba iḍāfiyya), like the father-son relation in 'Zayd son of Amr'; and the explicatory relation (nisba tafsīliyya), like the description in 'rational animal' where 'rational' qualifies 'animal'. Then al-Anbābī raises a critical point: can we truly apprehend subject and predicate without the relation? He argues that whenever one considers both ends, the relation is inevitably grasped. A response follows, stating that the objection is not accepted, because one can conceive of 'Zayd' and 'standing' as mere referents without any relational link—that is precisely what 'without relation' means. The passage thus clarifies the scope of tasawwur, ensuring that it includes both simple term apprehension and the apprehension of certain internal relations, while excluding external relations and judgments.

Key Terms
تصوّر
إدراك مفرد
نسبة كلامية
نسبة إضافية
نسبة تفسيدية

B) Apprehending the concept 'mortality'.
C) Judging that 'man is mortal'.
D) Apprehending the relation of sonship in 'Zayd is son of Amr'.

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur is the apprehension of a single concept, whether without any relation or with a non-external relation, but never with a judgment.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Objection and Response on Apprehending Both Ends
Al-Anbabi criticizes the possibility of conceiving subject and predicate without the relation, and the commentator rebuts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Anbabi's objection and the response, and explain why the objection is rejected.

Core Idea
Apprehending subject and predicate together does not automatically entail the relation; one can think of them as separate.

Al-Anbabi objects that when you conceive of both subject and predicate, you inevitably conceive the relation. The response clarifies that you can conceive of the referents without linking them. This refines the definition of tasawwur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Al-Anbabi says: 'their conceptualization necessitates the conceptualization of the relation, since whenever its two ends are considered, it occurs.'
2
Identify the response
The commentator says: 'We do not accept that. You can conceive of the referents (e.g., Zayd and standing) without considering their connection.'
3
Analyze the reasoning
The objection relies on the assumption that considering both ends forces the relation. The response distinguishes between conceiving the terms as independent and conceiving them in relation.
4
Evaluate the outcome
The response is accepted; the definition of tasawwur includes the case of apprehending both ends without the relation.

قَوْلُهُ : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ ... إلخ) المُرَادُ بِـ إِدْرَاكِ المُفْرَدِ : الإِدْرَاكُ الَّذِي لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقْ بِالنِّسْبَةِ الخَارِجِيَّةِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِنْعَانِ : - بِأَنْ لَمْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِنِسْبَةٍ أَصْلًا ، وَذَلِكَ : إِدْرَاكُ المَوْضُوعِ وَحْدَهُ ، وَإِدْرَاكُ المَحْمُولِ وَحْدَهُ، وَإِدْرَاكُهُمَا دُونَ النِّسْبَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا. أَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِنِسْبَةٍ غَيْرِ خَارِجِيَّةٍ ، وَذَلِكَ : إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ ثُبُوتُ المَحْمُولِ لِلمَوْضُوعِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِثْبَاتِ فِي القَضِيَّةِ المُوجَبَةِ، وَعَلَى وَجْهِ النَّفْيِ فِي القَضِيَّةِ السَّالِبَةِ ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ إِنْشَائِيَّةٌ أَوْ خَبَرِيَّةٌ، وَإِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ الإِضَافِيَّةِ كَالنِّسْبَةِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : زَيْدُ بْنُ عَمْرٍو وَهِيَ بُنُوَّةُ زَيْدٍ لِعَمْرِو، وَإِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ التَّفْسِيدِيَّةِ كَالنِّسْبَةِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : حَيَوَانٌ نَاطِقٌ وَهِيَ كَوْنُ الثَّانِي صِفَةٌ لِلأَوَّلِ . قَالَ الْأَنْبَابِيُّ: قَوْلُهُ: (وَإِدْرَاكُهُمَا دُونَ النِّسْبَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا) فِيهِ: أَنَّ تَصَوُّرَهُمَا يَسْتَدْعِي تَصَوُّرَ النِّسْبَةِ؛ إِذْ مَتَى لُوحِظَ طَرَفَاهَا حَصَلَتْ. وَقَدْ يُقَالُ: لَا نُسَلِّمُ ذَلِكَ؛ إِذْ لَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ تَصَوُّرِ مَا صَدَقَاتِ الْمَوْضُوعِ كَـ«زَيْدٍ»، وَمَا صَدَقَاتِ الْمَحْمُولِ كَـ«قَائِمٍ»، وَلَا مِنْ تَصَوُّرِهِمَا مَعًا بِقَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنِ ارْتِبَاطِ أَحَدِهِمَا بِالْآخَرِ تَصَوُّرُ النِّسْبَةِ، وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمُرَادُ، لَا مَا فَهِمَهُ.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
5 min
Distinguishing Tasawwur and Tasdiq: The Two Types of Relation
Commentator defines tasawwur and tasdiq with explanatory notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish tasawwur from tasdiq by identifying whether the perceived relation is linguistic or external.

Core Idea
Tasawwur perceives a concept; tasdiq perceives a real connection with conviction.

The commentator explains the foundational division of knowledge. He clarifies that tasawwur is the perception of a singular concept, while tasdiq involves perceiving a relation in reality, but only when accompanied by assent. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the rest of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary divisions of knowledge in the matn.
The matn states: perception of an individual is tasawwur, perception of a relation is tasdiq.
2
Distinguish between the linguistic relation and the external relation.
The linguistic relation is the subject-predicate connection in speech; the external relation is its occurrence in reality.
The commentator clarifies that perception of the linguistic relation is also called tasawwur (a concept of a relation).
3
Map each perception to the correct type of knowledge.
Perception of the linguistic relation is tasawwur, while perception of the external relation is tasdiq only if accompanied by idh‘ān.
If the external relation is perceived without idh‘ān (e.g., with hesitation), it is still tasawwur.
4
Recognize that tasdiq requires idh‘ān.
Assent can be preponderant (opinion) or decisive but false (compound ignorance).
This broadens the scope of tasdiq beyond certainty.

إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ: «تَصَوُّراً» عُلِـمْ وَدَرْلُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ. أَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِنِسْبَةٍ خَارِجِيَّةٍ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِنْعَانِ؛ بِأَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَابِلاً وَمُسَلِّما لَهَا عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي تَفْسِيرِ الإِذْعَانِ. فَكُلُّ مَا ذُكِرَ دَاخِل فِي تَعْرِيفِ التَّصَوُّرِ ، وَقَدْ أَبْلَغَ بَعْضُهُمْ صُوَرَهُ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ صُورَةٌ. قَوْلُهُ : تَصَوُّراً) عُلِمٌ أَيْ : عُلِمَ بِالتَّصَوُّرِ ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ سُمِّيَ بِهِ ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ التَّصَرُّرَ بِهَذَا المَعْنَى قِسْمٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ، وَأَمَّا بِمَعْنَى : حُصُولِ صُورَةِ الشَّيْء فِي النَّفْسِ ، فَهُوَ مُرَادِفٌ لِلعِلْمِ الشَّامِلِ لِلتَّصَوُّرِ بِذَلِكَ المَعْنَى وَلِلتَّصْدِيقِ ؛ فَتَحَصَّلَ أَنَّ التَّصَوُّرَ لَهُ اسْتِعْمَالَانِ: أَحَدُهُمَا : اسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي المَعْنَى الأَخَصّ ، وَهُوَ الَّذِي ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ . وَالثَّاني : اسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي المَعْنَى الأَعَمِّ، وَهُوَ مَا تَقَدَّمَ، فَلَا تَغْفَلْ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَدَرْلُ نِسْبَةٍ ... إلخ) الدَّرْكُ : اسْمُ مَصْدَرٍ بِمَعْنَى الإِدْرَاكِ . وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ مِمَّا مَرَّ : أَنَّ النِّسْبَةَ الكَلَامِيَّةَ هِيَ : «ثُبُوتُ المَحْمُولِ لِلمَوْضُوعِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِثْبَاتِ أَوْ عَلَى وَجْهِ النَّفْيِ ، بِخِلَافِ النِّسْبَةِ الخَارِجِيَّةِ ، فَإِنَّهَا : «وُقُوعُ ذَلِكَ الثُّبُوتِ أَوْ عَدَمُ وُقُوعِهِ ، وَقَدْ تَقَدَّمَ : أَنَّ إِدْرَاكَ النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ يُسَمَّى : تَصَوُّراً». قوله : أَوْ تَعَلَّقَ بِنِسْبَةٍ خَارِجِيَّةٍ لَا عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِذْعَانِ) أي : بل على وجه التّردُّد باستواء، أو مرجوحيَّةٍ . قوله : (وَقَدْ أَبْلَغَ بَعْضُهُمْ صُوَرَهُ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ) هو المحقِّقُ الصَّبَّان. وَمِنْ هَذَا تَعْلَمُ : أَنَّ كَلَامَ المُصَنِّفِ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى النِّسْبَةِ الخَارِجِيَّةِ ؛ لِأَنَّ إِدْرَاكَهَا هُوَ الَّذِي يُسَمَّى : «تَصْدِيقاً»، وَهَذَا أَوْلَى مِمَّا صَنَعَهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ مِنْ حَمْلِ كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ عَلَى النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ مَعَ تَقْدِيرِ مُضَافٍ؛ حَيْثُ قَالَ : أَيْ: وَإِدْرَاكُ وُقُوعِ نِسْبَةٍ ... إلخ. وَمَحَلُّ تَسْمِيَةِ إِدْرَاكِ هَذِهِ النِّسْبَةِ : تَصْدِيقاً إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِنْعَانِ؛ بِحَيْثُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ التَّسْلِيمِ وَالقَبُولِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ الخَبِيْصِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ التَّهْذِيبِ، وَنَقَلَهُ عَنِ العَضُدِ وَالسَّعْدِ وَالسَّيِّدِ، وَهَذَا مَا ارْتَضَاهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلَّوِيُّ وَجَعَلَهُ التَّحْقِيقَ، وَنَقَلَ يَاسِينُ فِي حَاشِيَتِهِ عَلَى الخَبِيصِيِّ عَنِ العِصَامِ : أَنَّ الإِذْعَانَ الاعْتِقَادُ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ رَاجِحاً وَهُوَ الظَّنُّ، أَوْ جَازِماً غَيْرَ مُطَابِقٍ وَهُوَ الجَهْلُ المُرَكَّب.
Perception of an individual: it is called 'tasawwur,' and perception of a relation is called 'tasdiq,' or it pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent, i.e., not being accepting and submitting to it as will come in the interpretation of idh‘ān. So everything mentioned is included in the definition of tasawwur, and some have raised its forms to twenty-five forms. His statement: 'tasawwuran' it is known, i.e., known by tasawwur, meaning that it is named by it. It is not hidden that tasawwur in this sense is a division of knowledge. As for in the sense of obtaining the image of a thing in the soul, it is synonymous with knowledge encompassing tasawwur in that sense and tasdiq. So it is established that tasawwur has two usages: one is its usage in the more specific sense, which is what the author mentioned; the second is its usage in the more general sense, which is what preceded, so do not neglect. His statement: 'and perception of a relation... etc.' al-darak is a verbal noun meaning perception. And you have known from what passed that the linguistic relation is: 'the establishment of the predicate for the subject in the manner of affirmation or in the manner of negation,' contrary to the external relation, for it is: 'the occurrence of that establishment or its non-occurrence,' and it has preceded that perception of the linguistic relation is called 'tasawwur.' His statement: 'or pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent' meaning: rather in the manner of hesitation with equal probability or with less probability. His statement: 'and some have raised its forms to twenty-five' is the investigator al-Sabban. And from this you know that the author's speech is carried upon the external relation, because its perception is what is called 'tasdiq,' and this is more appropriate than what al-Mallawi did of carrying the author's speech upon the linguistic relation with an implied annexation, where he said: 'i.e., perception of the occurrence of a relation... etc.' And the place of naming the perception of this relation 'tasdiq' is when it is in the manner of assent, such that the name of submission and acceptance applies to it, as al-Khabisi said in Sharh al-Tahdhib, and he transmitted it from al-‘Adud, al-Sa‘d, and al-Sayyid, and this is what al-Mallawi approved and made the verification. And Yasin transmitted in his hashiyah on al-Khabisi from al-‘Isam that idh‘ān is belief, whether it is preponderant, which is opinion, or decisive without correspondence, which is compound ignorance.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the text's classification of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). It begins by restating the matn: perception of an individual is called 'tasawwur,' and perception of a relation is called 'tasdiq.' The commentator then clarifies the phrases. The line 'or pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent' explains that tasdiq involves a relation but without outright conviction—it could be hesitation (equal or less probable). This is a preliminary step before the full condition of idh‘ān (assent) is introduced. The commentator notes that all these cases fall under the definition of tasawwur, and some scholars (like al-Sabban) have enumerated twenty-five forms of tasawwur. Next, a crucial distinction is made: tasawwur has two meanings. The first is the specific sense used by the author—a division of knowledge opposite to tasdiq. The second is the general sense—the mere obtaining of an image in the mind, which is synonymous with knowledge itself and includes both tasawwur and tasdiq. This is a key point to avoid confusion. The commentary then explains the term 'darak' (perception) as a verbal noun. It distinguishes between the 'linguistic relation' (nisba kalamiyya), which is the relation of predicate to subject as affirmed or denied in speech, and the 'external relation' (nisba kharijiyya), which is the actual occurrence or non-occurrence of that relation in reality. The perception of the linguistic relation is tasawwur (since it is just a concept of the relation), while the perception of the external relation is tasdiq, but only when accompanied by idh‘ān. The commentator argues that the author's statement should be interpreted as referring to the external relation, because that is what is properly called tasdiq. This is preferred over al-Mallawi's interpretation that it refers to the linguistic relation with an implied annexation. Finally, the passage discusses the nature of idh‘ān: it is assent or belief, whether it is a preponderant belief (opinion) or a decisive belief that does not correspond to reality (compound ignorance). This follows al-Khabisi and others, and is the verification chosen by al-Mallawi.

التَّصْدِيق
الإِذْعَان
النِّسْبَةُ الكَلَامِيَّة
النِّسْبَةُ الخَارِجِيَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is TRUE about tasdiq?
A) It is always certain.
B) It can be preponderant opinion or compound ignorance.
C) It is synonymous with tasawwur.
D) It does not require a relation.

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur and tasdiq are distinguished by whether the perception is of an individual or of a relation, and tasdiq requires assent (idh‘an).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the following statement: 'The world is temporally originated.' Identify whether this is a tasawwur or a tasdiq, and which type of relation (linguistic or external) is being perceived.
?
Construct your own example of a tasawwur and a tasdiq from the field of Usul al-Fiqh, explaining the relation involved.
