Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
4 min
The Two Meanings of Tasawwur: Specific and General
Commentator clarifies the two senses of tasawwur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate between the specific and general meanings of tasawwur as used in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Tasawwur has two meanings: one specific (a division of knowledge) and one general (synonymous with all knowledge).

The commentator alerts readers that 'tasawwur' is used in two distinct ways. Understanding these two meanings is vital to avoid confusion when reading logic texts. This lesson will help you recognize which meaning is intended in a given context.

Guided Path
1
Locate the passage where the two meanings are discussed.
The commentator explicitly states that tasawwur has two usages.
2
Identify the first (specific) meaning.
Tasawwur as a division of knowledge opposite tasdiq, i.e., perception of an individual.
This is the meaning used by the author of the matn.
3
Identify the second (general) meaning.
Tasawwur as obtaining the image of a thing in the soul, synonymous with knowledge itself, including both tasawwur and tasdiq.
In this sense, it encompasses all knowledge.
4
Test the distinction with examples.
For example, 'perception of the concept of wine' is a specific tasawwur, while 'knowledge of the ruling of wine' includes both conception and assent.
The general meaning is broader.

النِّسْبَةِ : تَصْدِيقاً إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِنْعَانِ؛ بِحَيْثُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ التَّسْلِيمِ وَالقَبُولِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ الخَبِيْصِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ التَّهْذِيبِ، وَنَقَلَهُ عَنِ العَضُدِ وَالسَّعْدِ وَالسَّيِّدِ، وَهَذَا مَا ارْتَضَاهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلَّوِيُّ وَجَعَلَهُ التَّحْقِيقَ، وَنَقَلَ يَاسِينُ فِي حَاشِيَتِهِ عَلَى الخَبِيصِيِّ عَنِ العِصَامِ : أَنَّ الإِذْعَانَ الاعْتِقَادُ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ رَاجِحاً وَهُوَ الظَّنُّ، أَوْ جَازِماً غَيْرَ مُطَابِقٍ وَهُوَ الجَهْلُ المُرَكَّب.
Perception of an individual: it is called 'tasawwur,' and perception of a relation is called 'tasdiq,' or it pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent, i.e., not being accepting and submitting to it as will come in the interpretation of idh‘ān. So everything mentioned is included in the definition of tasawwur, and some have raised its forms to twenty-five forms. His statement: 'tasawwuran' it is known, i.e., known by tasawwur, meaning that it is named by it. It is not hidden that tasawwur in this sense is a division of knowledge. As for in the sense of obtaining the image of a thing in the soul, it is synonymous with knowledge encompassing tasawwur in that sense and tasdiq. So it is established that tasawwur has two usages: one is its usage in the more specific sense, which is what the author mentioned; the second is its usage in the more general sense, which is what preceded, so do not neglect. His statement: 'and perception of a relation... etc.' al-darak is a verbal noun meaning perception. And you have known from what passed that the linguistic relation is: 'the establishment of the predicate for the subject in the manner of affirmation or in the manner of negation,' contrary to the external relation, for it is: 'the occurrence of that establishment or its non-occurrence,' and it has preceded that perception of the linguistic relation is called 'tasawwur.' His statement: 'or pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent' meaning: rather in the manner of hesitation with equal probability or with less probability. His statement: 'and some have raised its forms to twenty-five' is the investigator al-Sabban. And from this you know that the author's speech is carried upon the external relation, because its perception is what is called 'tasdiq,' and this is more appropriate than what al-Mallawi did of carrying the author's speech upon the linguistic relation with an implied annexation, where he said: 'i.e., perception of the occurrence of a relation... etc.' And the place of naming the perception of this relation 'tasdiq' is when it is in the manner of assent, such that the name of submission and acceptance applies to it, as al-Khabisi said in Sharh al-Tahdhib, and he transmitted it from al-‘Adud, al-Sa‘d, and al-Sayyid, and this is what al-Mallawi approved and made the verification. And Yasin transmitted in his hashiyah on al-Khabisi from al-‘Isam that idh‘ān is belief, whether it is preponderant, which is opinion, or decisive without correspondence, which is compound ignorance.

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the text's classification of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). It begins by restating the matn: perception of an individual is called 'tasawwur,' and perception of a relation is called 'tasdiq.' The commentator then clarifies the phrases. The line 'or pertains to an external relation not in the manner of assent' explains that tasdiq involves a relation but without outright conviction—it could be hesitation (equal or less probable). This is a preliminary step before the full condition of idh‘ān (assent) is introduced. The commentator notes that all these cases fall under the definition of tasawwur, and some scholars (like al-Sabban) have enumerated twenty-five forms of tasawwur. Next, a crucial distinction is made: tasawwur has two meanings. The first is the specific sense used by the author—a division of knowledge opposite to tasdiq. The second is the general sense—the mere obtaining of an image in the mind, which is synonymous with knowledge itself and includes both tasawwur and tasdiq. This is a key point to avoid confusion. The commentary then explains the term 'darak' (perception) as a verbal noun. It distinguishes between the 'linguistic relation' (nisba kalamiyya), which is the relation of predicate to subject as affirmed or denied in speech, and the 'external relation' (nisba kharijiyya), which is the actual occurrence or non-occurrence of that relation in reality. The perception of the linguistic relation is tasawwur (since it is just a concept of the relation), while the perception of the external relation is tasdiq, but only when accompanied by idh‘ān. The commentator argues that the author's statement should be interpreted as referring to the external relation, because that is what is properly called tasdiq. This is preferred over al-Mallawi's interpretation that it refers to the linguistic relation with an implied annexation. Finally, the passage discusses the nature of idh‘ān: it is assent or belief, whether it is a preponderant belief (opinion) or a decisive belief that does not correspond to reality (compound ignorance). This follows al-Khabisi and others, and is the verification chosen by al-Mallawi.

Key Terms
التَّصَوُّر
العلم
المعنى الأخص
المعنى الأعم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about tasawwur?
A) It has only one meaning.
B) It has two meanings: specific and general.
C) It is the same as tasdiq.
D) It never includes tasdiq.

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur can mean either a specific division of knowledge (conception) or the general act of obtaining an image in the soul, which covers all knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Tasdiq: External vs. Linguistic Relation
Bajuri defines tasdiq and clarifies that the relation is external, not linguistic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the external relation (al-nisbah al-khārijiyya) and the linguistic relation (al-nisbah al-kalāmiyya) in the definition of tasdiq, and explain why Bajuri prefers the external relation.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is about real-world judgments, not mere linguistic statements.

In Islamic logic (mantiq), knowledge is divided into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). The standard definition of tasdiq is 'perception of a relation' (idrāk al-nisbah). But which relation? In this passage, Bajuri clarifies that the intended relation is the external relation—the actual state of affairs—and not the linguistic relation of subject-predicate combination. This distinction is crucial for understanding how tasdiq functions in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of tasdiq in the matn
Find the line: 'Perception of a singular: called tasawwur. And perception of a relation: called tasdiq.' This establishes tasdiq as perception of a relation.
2
Extract the two candidate interpretations of 'relation'
Bajuri introduces two possibilities: the external relation (al-nisbah al-khārijiyya), which is the actual occurrence in reality, and the linguistic relation (al-nisbah al-kalāmiyya), which is the grammatical connection in speech.
3
Analyze Bajuri's argument for the external relation
Bajuri states that perceiving the external relation is what is called tasdiq. He criticizes al-Mallawi's interpretation of the linguistic relation with an implied genitive, saying his own interpretation is more appropriate.
4
Understand the consequence
If tasdiq were about linguistic relations, then affirming a false statement would still be tasdiq because the linguistic relation exists. But since tasdiq requires correspondence to reality (external relation), false statements are not tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ: تَصَوُّراً عُلِـمْ وَدَرْكُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ. وَمِنْ هَذَا تَعْلَمُ : أَنَّ كَلَامَ المُصَنِّفِ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى النِّسْبَةِ الخَارِجِيَّةِ ; لِأَنَّ إِدْرَاكَهَا هُوَ الَّذِي يُسَمَّى : «تَصْدِيقاً»، وَهَذَا أَوْلَى مِمَّا صَنَعَهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلوِيُّ مِنْ حَمْلِ كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ عَلَى النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ مَعَ تَقْدِيرِ مُضَافٍ; حَيْثُ قَالَ : أَيْ: وَإِدْرَاكُ وُقُوعِ نِسْبَةٍ ... إلخ.
Perception of a singular: called 'tasawwur'. And perception of a relation: called 'tasdiq'. And from this you know that the author's words are predicated on the external relation, because perceiving it is what is called 'tasdiq'. And this is more appropriate than what al-Mallawi did, in interpreting the author's words as the linguistic relation, assuming a genitive construct, where he said: 'That is, perception of the occurrence of a relation...' etc.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary. The matn line states: 'Perception of a singular is called tasawwur, and perception of a relation is called tasdiq.' Bajuri then explains that the 'relation' referred to is the external relation (al-nisbah al-khārijiyya)—i.e., the actual occurrence of a judgment in reality, not the linguistic expression of it. He argues this interpretation is more appropriate than that of al-Mallawi, who took it as the linguistic relation (al-nisbah al-kalāmiyya), requiring an implied genitive. Bajuri's point is that tasdiq is about real-world judgments, not mere statements.

نسبة خارجية
نسبة كلامية

The definition of tasdiq as perception of a relation must be understood as the external relation in reality, not the linguistic one, to preserve its epistemological function.

The Four Types of Idh'ān (Assent) in Tasdiq
Bajuri enumerates the types of idh'ān that qualify perception as tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of idh'ān (assent) and classify any assent as zann, jahl murakkab, yaqīn, or taqlīd based on its decisiveness, correspondence, and firmness.

Core Idea
Assent ranges from opinion to certainty, and even includes false conviction.

This lesson unpacks the key condition for tasdiq: that it must be accompanied by idh'ān, a state of acceptance. But not every assent is the same. The classical logicians distinguished four types based on decisiveness, truth-correspondence, and stability. Understanding these distinctions is essential for evaluating the epistemic strength of beliefs in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for tasdiq
Read the first line: the perception of the relation is only called tasdiq when it is 'in the mode of idh'ān'. This means acceptance (i'tiqād) is required.
2
Extract the definition of idh'ān
From the transmission of al-'Isam, idh'ān is i'tiqād (belief). It can be preponderant (rājih) or decisive (jāzim), truthful or false.
3
List the four types
The passage names four: zann (preponderant belief), jahl murakkab (decisive false belief), yaqīn (certain truth), and taqlīd (firm but non-rationally grounded acceptance).
4
Classify on a 2x2 grid
Create a grid: decisive/jāzim vs. non-decisive, and corresponding (mutābiq) vs. non-corresponding. Place each type: zann (non-decisive, corresponding? Actually zann is rājih but not decisive; it may correspond or not? The passage says it is rājih, so not decisive; correspondence not specified, but it is not jāzim so it's in the non-decisive column; yaqīn is decisive + corresponding; jahl murakkab is decisive + non-corresponding; taqlīd is decisive + corresponding but not firm (rāsikh).
Taqlīd is decisive and corresponding but lacks firmness (rusūkh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَحَلُّ تَسْمِيَةِ إِدْرَاكِ هَذِهِ النِّسْبَةِ : تَصْدِيقاً إِذَا كَانَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الإِذْعَانِ؛ بِحَيْثُ يُطْلَقُ عَلَيْهِ اسْمُ التَّسْلِيمِ وَالقَبُولِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ الخَبِيْصِيُّ فِي شَرْحِ التَّهْذِيبِ، وَنَقَلَهُ عَنِ العَضُدِ وَالسَّعْدِ وَالسَّيِّدِ، وَهَذَا مَا ارْتَضَاهُ الشَّيْخُ المَلَّوِيُّ وَجَعَلَهُ التَّحْقِيقَ، وَنَقَلَ يَاسِينُ فِي حَاشِيَتِهِ عَلَى الخَبِيصِيِّ عَنِ العِصَامِ : أَنَّ الإِذْعَانَ الاعْتِقَادُ ; سَوَاءٌ كَانَ رَاجِحاً وَهُوَ الظَّنُّ، أَوْ جَازِماً غَيْرَ مُطَابِقٍ وَهُوَ الجَهْلُ المُرَكَّب، أَوْ مُطَابِقاً رَاسِخاً لَا يَعْرِضُ لَهُ الزَّوَالُ بِتَشْكِيكِ المُشَكْكِ وَهُوَ اليَقِينُ، أَوْ غَيْرَ رَاسِخِ وَهُوَ التَّقْلِيدُ.
The place where perceiving this relation is called 'tasdiq' is when it is in the mode of idh'ān (assent), such that the name 'taslīm and qabūl' can be applied, as al-Khabisi said in his commentary on al-Tahdhīb, and he transmitted it from al-'Adud, al-Sa'd, and al-Sayyid. This is what al-Mallawi preferred and made the verified position. And Yassin in his hashia on al-Khabisi transmitted from al-'Isam that idh'ān is belief (i'tiqād), whether it be preponderant (rājih), which is opinion (zann), or decisive and non-corresponding (jāzim ghayr muṭābiq), which is compound ignorance (jahl murakkab), or decisive and corresponding and firm (rāsikh), which is certainty (yaqīn), or non-firm, which is blind acceptance (taqlīd).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is definitional and enumerative. Bajuri explains that the perception of the external relation is only called tasdiq when it occurs with idh'ān (assent), which is a state of acceptance. He then categorizes idh'ān into four types: (1) preponderant but not certain (rājih) — this is zann (opinion); (2) decisive but not corresponding to reality — this is jahl murakkab (compound ignorance); (3) decisive, corresponding, and firm — this is yaqīn (certainty); (4) decisive and corresponding but not firm — this is taqlīd (blind acceptance). These categories show that tasdiq can range from mere opinion to true certainty.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is not just any perception; it requires assent (idh'ān), which can be of four types: zann, jahl murakkab, yaqīn, and taqlīd, each with different epistemic status.

The Meaning of Idh'ān: Logicians vs. Theologians
Bajuri reports a dispute on the meaning of idh'ān and gives his teacher's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two technical definitions of idh'ān and explain how scholars resolve terminological disputes.

Core Idea
A term's meaning shifts between disciplines; the scholar's task is to decide which usage is authoritative.

In this passage, Bajūrī reports a dispute over the technical meaning of idh'ān. Logicians and theologians use the term differently. Bajūrī then records his teacher's preference. This lesson will show you how to analyze such terminological conflicts and understand the method of preferring one definition over another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Find the two distinct definitions of idh'ān reported in the passage: one from the logicians and one from the theologians.
The logicians define it as idrāk (perception); the theologians define it as taslīm (submission) and qabūl (acceptance).
2
Note the preference of many shaykhs
Bajūrī states that many shaykhs preferred the theologians' definition. This shows a common scholarly inclination.
3
Identify the teacher's view
Bajūrī reports that his own teacher holds that the approved view (al-murḍā) is the first definition, i.e., the logicians' idrāk.
This indicates that despite the majority preference, the teacher's authority offers a different verdict.
4
Recognize the method of resolving disputes
Bajūrī advises to consult further and revise (falyurājaʿ wa līyuḥarrar). This shows that terminological disputes are resolved by careful reference to authoritative sources and scholarly revision.
In Islamic scholarship, defining terms precisely is critical to avoid confusion in arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي كَلَامِ غَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ أَنَّ الإِذْعَانَ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ بِمَعْنَى : الإِدْرَاكِ، وَعِنْدَ المُتَكَلِّمِينَ بِمَعْنَى : التَّسْلِيمِ وَالقَبُولِ»، وَرَبَّحَهُ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ الأَشْيَاحَ، كَذَا قَالَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ، لَكِنَّ الَّذِي قَالَهُ شَيْخُنَا : أَنَّ المَرْضِيَّ هُوَ الأَوَّلُ، فَلْيُرَاجَعْ وَلِيُحَرَّر .
And in the speech of more than one: that idh'ān, according to the logicians, means perception (idrāk), and according to the theologians, means submission (taslīm) and acceptance (qabūl). And many shaykhs preferred it. Thus said some investigators. But what our shaykh said is that the approved is the first. Let it be consulted and revised.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is dialectical. Bajuri reports that multiple scholars have noted a terminological difference: the logicians (manāṭiqa) define idh'ān as mere perception (idrāk), while the theologians (mutakallimūn) define it as submission and acceptance (taslīm wa qabūl). Bajuri adds that many shaykhs preferred the theologians' definition, but his own teacher (shaykhunā) holds that the approved view is the logicians' definition (idrāk). He advises the reader to consult further and revise.

Key Terms
إذعان (idh'ān): Here the term has two technical meanings: in mantiq it means perception (idrāk); in kalām it means submission (taslīm) and acceptance (qabūl). [Note: This semantic shift between disciplines is a known issue; in some later texts, idh'ān is used interchangeably with tasdiq.]

Key Takeaway
Idh'ān is defined differently by logicians (idrāk) and theologians (taslīm wa qabūl); scholarly preference may vary, but the distinction is essential for accurate reading.

The Two Definitions of Tasdiq: Philosophers vs. al-Razi
Bajuri contrasts the philosophers' definition of tasdiq with al-Razi's expanded definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the philosophers' definition of tasdiq (as pure judgment) with al-Razi's definition (including prior perceptions) and explain the difference between part and condition in defining assent.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is either the judgment alone or the judgment plus its building blocks.

The term tasdiq is central to Islamic logic. But is it merely the act of affirming or denying a relation, or does it also include the prior grasp of the terms and the relation itself? This passage from Bajuri's commentary presents two views: the dominant position of the philosophers, and the expanded definition of Imam al-Razi. Understanding this dispute reveals how definitions shape the study of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate in the Arabic where the philosophers' and al-Razi's definitions are stated. The philosophers hold that tasdiq is the perception of the judgment alone. Al-Razi holds it includes the three preceding perceptions.
The philosophers' view is introduced as 'madhab al-hukama'' and is deemed preponderant (al-rajih).
2
Extract the components of each definition
List what each definition includes. The philosophers: only the judgment (nisba hukmiyya). Al-Razi: the judgment plus perception of subject, predicate, and linguistic relation.
The three prior perceptions are idrak al-mawdu', idrak al-mahmul, and idrak al-nisba al-kalamiyya.
3
Distinguish 'part' vs 'condition'
In the philosophers' view, prior perceptions are conditions (shartiyya) external to tasdiq. In al-Razi's view, they are integral parts (shartiyya) of tasdiq itself. Understand the difference: a condition is prerequisite but not part of the essence; a part is constitutive.
The Arabic terms are shartiyya (part) and shartiyya (condition) – spelled identically but distinguished by context.
4
Determine the preponderant view
Bajuri states that the apparent meaning of al-Sullam's text supports the philosophers, and he himself considers it preponderant. Consider why the narrower definition might be preferred.
The broader definition could blur the line between conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq).
5
Reflect on implications
Think about how this definitional dispute affects the analysis of knowledge statements in Islamic sciences. For example, in usul al-fiqh, does assenting to a legal ruling require grasping the subject and predicate as part of the assent itself?
This debate reappears in discussions of the nature of knowledge (al-'ilm) and the categories of mental perception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (بِـ تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمٌ أَيْ : عُلِمَ بِالتَّصْدِيقِ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ سُمِّيَ بِذَلِكَ. وَالمُتَبَادِرُ مِنْ كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ : أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ اسْمٌ لِذَلِكَ الإِدْرَاكِ وَحْدَهُ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ الحُكَمَاءِ، وَهُوَ الرَّاجِحُ. وَذَهَبَ الإِمَامُ الرَّازِيُّ إِلَى أَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لَهُ مَعَ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ قَبْلَهُ؛ أَعْنِي : إِدْرَاكَ المَوْضُوع، وَإِدْرَاكَ المَحْمُولِ، وَإِدْرَاكَ النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ، فَهِيَ عِنْدَهُ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ فِي التَّصْدِيقِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الشَّطْرِيَّةِ. بِخِلَافِهَا عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ، فَإِنَّهَا مُعْتَبَرَةٌ فِيهِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الشَّرْطِيَّةِ.
His saying: 'Called tasdiq' means it was known as tasdiq, i.e., it was named that. And the obvious understanding from the author's words is that tasdiq is a name for that perception alone, and it is the doctrine of the philosophers (hukamā'), and it is the preponderant. Imam al-Razi held that it is a name for it together with the three perceptions preceding it: perception of the subject, perception of the predicate, and perception of the linguistic relation. So in his view, these are considered in tasdiq on the mode of being parts (shartiyya). Contrary to the first view, where they are considered on the mode of being conditions (shartiyya).
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is definitional. Bajuri explains that the matn's phrase 'called tasdiq' means that this perception (of the relation) is named tasdiq. He then notes that the apparent meaning of the author's (al-Sullam) words is that tasdiq is exclusively the perception of the judgment, which is the position of the philosophers (hukamā') and is preponderant. In contrast, Imam al-Razi holds that tasdiq includes not only the judgment but also the three prior perceptions: grasping the subject, the predicate, and the linguistic relation. In al-Razi's view, these are integral parts (ajzā') of tasdiq, whereas in the philosophers' view they are merely prerequisites (shurūṭ) external to the act of judgment.

شطرية
شرطية

D) They are subsequent to tasdiq.

Key Takeaway
The definition of tasdiq is contested: whether it is solely the judgment or includes its preparatory perceptions has implications for the foundational theory of knowledge in Islamic logic.

The Two Types of Acquired Knowledge: Tasawwur and Tasdiq
Defines acquired knowledge as tasawwur or tasdiq, and subdivides tasdiq into yaqin and taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasawwur and tasdiq, and identify whether a given judgment is yaqin or taqlid based on the criteria of firmness.

Core Idea
Acquired knowledge is either a simple concept (tasawwur) or a judgment (tasdiq); the latter is certain only if unshakable.

In logic, acquired knowledge is divided into two fundamental types: perception of a singular concept (tasawwur) and perception of a relation (tasdiq). The commentator al-Bajuri further explains that tasdiq can be either firmly established (yaqin) or not (taqlid). Understanding this classification is essential for evaluating the certitude of any claim in Islamic sciences, such as in Kalam or Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary types
Look at the first line of the passage: acquired knowledge is either perception of a singular or perception of a relation. These are called tasawwur and tasdiq respectively.
2
Understand the definitions
Tasawwur is grasping a concept without any judgment about its existence or relation. Tasdiq involves affirming or denying a relationship between concepts, e.g., 'the world is created'.
3
Examine the subdivision of tasdiq
Al-Bajuri divides tasdiq into yaqin (certainty) which is a firm matching judgment immune to doubt, and taqlid (blind following) which lacks firmness.
4
Apply the criteria
For any statement, first decide if it is a concept (tasawwur) or a judgment (tasdiq). If it is a judgment, then check whether it is so firm that no doubt can shake it – that would be yaqin; otherwise it is taqlid.
Even if a taqlid judgment happens to be true, it is not considered certain knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنواع العلم الحادث (19) إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ: تَصَوُّراً عُلِم وَدَرْكُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ الباجوري أَوْ مُطَابِقاً رَاسِخاً لَا يَعْرِضُ لَهُ الزَّوَالُ بِتَشْكِيكِ المُشَكْكِ وَهُوَ اليَقِينُ، أَوْ غَيْرَ رَاسِخِ وَهُوَ التَّقْلِيدُ. [اهـ].
Types of acquired knowledge (19): Perception of a singular is called 'tasawwur', and perception of a relation is labeled 'tasdiq'. [Al-Bajuri:] Or [it is] matching and firmly established, not subject to removal by the skeptic's doubt, and that is certainty; or not firmly established, and that is blind following. [End].
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage defines the two primary types of acquired knowledge (al-ilm al-hadith): tasawwur (concept) and tasdiq (assent). The text then subdivides tasdiq into two categories: yaqin (certainty), which is a firm and unshakable judgment, and taqlid (blind following), which is a judgment lacking firmness. The commentator (al-Bajuri) explains that yaqin is immune to doubt, while taqlid is not, even if it happens to be true. This classification is foundational in logic, as it distinguishes between certain knowledge and mere acceptance without proof.

D) Necessary and Acquired

Key Takeaway
Acquired knowledge is exhaustively divided into conceptual knowledge (tasawwur) and propositional knowledge (tasdiq), with the latter having a spectrum from certain (yaqin) to mere acceptance (taqlid).

Tasdiq: Logicians vs. Theologians
Defining tasdiq: logicians vs. theologians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the logicians' and theologians' definitions of tasdiq and identify the dominant position.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is either perception of a relation (logicians) or submission (theologians); the logicians' view is preferred.

This passage clarifies that the term 'tasdiq' has different technical meanings. The logicians define it as perception (idrak) of a relation, while the theologians define it as submission and acceptance (taslim wa qabul). The commentator notes that many scholars, including the author's shaykh, consider the logicians' definition as the approved one. Understanding this distinction is crucial because the same term appears across Islamic disciplines with nuanced differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate in the Arabic where tasdiq is defined for logicians (المَنَاطِقَة) and theologians (المُتَكَلِّمِينَ). Notice the key terms: إدراك (perception) vs. تسليم (submission).
2
Note the preferred view
The commentator states that many shaykhs preferred the logicians' definition, and the author's shaykh confirms that the first meaning (perception) is the approved one.
The approval does not invalidate the theologians' usage; it indicates technical priority in logic.
3
Understand the reason for the difference
Consider why logicians focus on perception (judgment) while theologians emphasize submission (acceptance with certainty). The contexts differ: logic deals with the structure of arguments, while theology deals with faith.
4
Dissect the definition of tasdiq as perception
Using definition_dissector: The genus is 'perception' and the differentia is 'of a relation'. This distinguishes it from simple concept formation.
Complete hadd: tasdiq is perception of the truth of a relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي كَلَامِ غَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ عِنْدَ المَنَاطِقَةِ بِمَعْنَى : الإِدْرَاكِ، وَعِنْدَ المُتَكَلِّمِينَ بِمَعْنَى : التَّسْلِيمِ وَالقَبُولِ، وَرَبَّحَهُ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ الأَشْيَاحَ، كَذَا قَالَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ، لَكِنَّ الَّذِي قَالَهُ شَيْخُنَا : أَنَّ المَرْضِيَّ هُوَ الأَوَّلُ، فَلْيُرَاجَعْ وَلِيُحَرَّر . قَوْلُهُ : (بِـ تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمٌ أَيْ : عُلِمَ بِالتَّصْدِيقِ؛ بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ سُمِّيَ بِذَلِكَ. وَالمُتَبَادِرُ مِنْ كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ : أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ اسْمٌ لِذَلِكَ الإِدْرَاكِ وَحْدَهُ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ الحُكَمَاءِ، وَهُوَ الرَّاجِعُ وَذَهَبَ الإِمَامُ الرَّازِيُّ إِلَى أَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لَهُ مَعَ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ قَبْلَهُ؛ أَعْنِي : إِدْرَاكَ المَوْضُوع، وَإِدْرَاكَ المَحْمُولِ، وَإِدْرَاكَ النِّسْبَةِ الكَلَامِيَّةِ ، فَهِيَ عِنْدَهُ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ فِي التَّصْدِيقِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الشَّطْرِيَّةِ. بِخِلَافِهَا عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ، فَإِنَّهَا مُعْتَبَرَةٌ فِيهِ عَلَى وَجْهِ الشَّرْطِيَّةِ. الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَالمُتَبَادِرُ مِنْ كَلَامِ المُصَنِّفِ : أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ اسْمٌ لِذَلِكَ الإِدْرَاكِ وَحْدَهُ) إنَّما جعله متبادراً، ولم يجعله متعيّناً؛ لاحتمال كلام المصنف لمذهب الرَّازي ؛ بأن يقال : وَدَرْكُ نِسْبَةٍ وَبَقِيَّةِ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ بِتَصْدِيقٍ وُسِمْ»، ففيه حذف الواو مع ما عطفت، لكنه خلاف المتبادر . ويترتَّبُ على هذا الخلاف الذي بين الحكماء والرَّازي : أنَّ التصديق المتعلق بالنسبة الخارجيَّة إذا كان ضروريا يسمى : علماً ضروريا عند الحكماء، ولو كان إدراك الأجزاء الثَّلَاثة نظريًّا، بخلافه عند الرّازي، فإنَّه لا يسمَّى التَّصديقُ : «ضروريا»؛ إلَّا إذا كانت الأجزاء ضروريَّةٌ . اهـ مِنَ الصَّبَّان» بالمعنى . جميع
And in the speech of more than one author: that 'tasdiq' according to the logicians means 'perception', and according to the theologians means 'submission and acceptance'. Many of the shaykhs preferred this, as stated by some verificators. However, what our shaykh said is that the approved view is the first, so let it be reviewed and corrected. His statement: ('by tasdiq it is known') means: it is known by tasdiq, i.e., it is named by that. The apparent meaning from the author's speech is that 'tasdiq' is a name for that perception alone, and that is the doctrine of the philosophers, and it is the preponderant. And Imam al-Razi held that it is a name for it along with the three perceptions before it: namely, perception of the subject, perception of the predicate, and perception of the linguistic relation. So according to him, these are considered in tasdiq in the manner of part-whole. Contrary to the first view, they are considered in it in the manner of condition. [Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'The apparent meaning from the author's speech is that tasdiq is a name for that perception alone' – he made it apparent, not definite, because of the possibility that the author's speech accommodates al-Razi's doctrine, by saying: 'And perception of a relation and the remaining three perceptions by tasdiq it is known', so there is omission of the conjunction with what it coordinates, but it is contrary to what is apparent. And upon this disagreement between the philosophers and al-Razi arises the consequence: that tasdiq related to the external relation, if it is necessary, is called 'necessary knowledge' according to the philosophers, even if the perception of the three parts is theoretical; contrary to al-Razi, for he does not call tasdiq 'necessary' unless the parts are necessary. End from al-Sabban, paraphrased.]
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage refines the definition of tasdiq by highlighting a disagreement between logicians (manatiqa) and theologians (mutakallimun). For logicians, tasdiq is simply 'perception' (idrak) of a relation; for theologians, it is 'submission and acceptance' (taslim wa qabul). The commentator notes that many scholars preferred the logicians' view, and the author's shaykh confirms that the first meaning is the approved one. The text then discusses a deeper disagreement between the philosophers (hukama') and Imam al-Razi. The philosophers hold that tasdiq is merely the perception of the relation itself, whereas al-Razi argues that it includes the perceptions of the subject, the predicate, and the linguistic relation (the three prior acts) as parts (shartiyya). Al-Shirshimi explains that the author's phrasing is ambiguous but the apparent meaning favors the philosophers. He further notes a practical consequence: for the philosophers, if the judgment (tasdiq) about an external relation is immediate, it is called necessary knowledge even if the concepts are theoretical; for al-Razi, the whole must be immediate for the tasdiq to be considered necessary.

تصديق
إدراك
تسليم

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq has two technical meanings: perception (logicians) and submission (theologians); the logicians' definition is preferred in the context of logic.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Tasdiq: Philosophers vs. Al-Razi
Debate on the composition of tasdiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Razi's additive definition of tasdiq and its consequence for the classification of knowledge as necessary or theoretical.

Core Idea
Al-Razi includes the three prior perceptions as parts of tasdiq; philosophers treat them as mere conditions, altering when knowledge is deemed necessary.

This passage delves deeper into a disagreement within the logical tradition. The philosophers (hukama') restrict tasdiq to the judgment alone, while Imam al-Razi argues that it includes the perceptions of the subject, predicate, and the linguistic relation. The commentator, al-Shirshimi, highlights that this distinction has a real consequence: for the philosophers, a judgment can be necessary even if its component concepts are theoretical, whereas al-Razi requires all parts to be necessary for the whole to be called necessary. Understanding this nuance is essential for analyzing epistemic claims in Islamic theology and jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find in the Arabic where the philosophers' view is stated: tasdiq is perception alone. Then al-Razi's view: tasdiq includes the three prior perceptions as parts.
The three perceptions: subject, predicate, linguistic relation.
2
Understand the part-whole vs. condition distinction
Note the terms: 'ala wajh al-shartiyya (as parts) vs. 'ala wajh al-shartiyya (as conditions). Al-Razi views the three perceptions as integral parts; the philosophers view them as external conditions for the judgment to occur.
This is a metaphysical distinction about the nature of mental acts.
3
Extract the consequence regarding necessary knowledge
Read al-Shirshimi's commentary: for philosophers, if the tasdiq (judgment) itself is immediate, it is called necessary knowledge even if the concepts are theoretical. For al-Razi, the entire composite must be immediate for the tasdiq to be necessary.
This affects how we classify premises in theological proofs.
4
Dissect both definitions
Use definition_dissector to compare: both have same genus (perception), but different differentia. Philosophers: perception of relation alone. Al-Razi: perception of relation plus perceptions of subject, predicate, and linguistic relation.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate

Why 'Tasdiq' Is Named After Truth: The Principle of Taghlib
Explains the naming of tasdiq via taghlib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of taghlib (predominance) in the naming of 'tasdiq' and identify applications of this principle in Islamic legal terminology.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is named after truth because the most honorable aspect predominates.

Have you ever wondered why a false judgment is still called 'tasdiq' (confirmation)? The answer lies in a powerful linguistic principle: taghlib. This lesson unpacks how the Islamic logical tradition justifies this naming, using the predominance of truth over falsehood. We'll dissect the passage from al-Bajuri's commentary, guided by al-Shirshimi's elucidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Locate the question that prompted this discussion: since 'tasdiq' can be either true or false, why is it named after truth? Al-Shirshimi states that sometimes the perception is true (e.g., the temporality of the world) and sometimes false (e.g., the philosopher's belief in its eternity), yet the term 'tasdiq' is used universally.
The objector assumes that naming should reflect all possibilities equally.
2
Extract the principle of taghlib
Notice that the passage answers with taghlib (تغليب): giving precedence to the more honorable or common aspect. The word 'tasdiq' is derived from 'sidq' (truth), so truth is the primary connotation. Falsehood is only a rational possibility (احتمال عقلي) not indicated by the speech.
Taghlib is a standard linguistic device in Arabic, e.g., 'the two parents' (al-walidan) refers to father and mother, but the word derives from 'father' alone.
3
Apply the principle to the term tasdiq
Understand that linguistically, 'tasdiq' means 'attribution to truth' (النسبة إلى الصدق). Even when the content is false, the act of affirming it is still named after truth because the statement's intended meaning is truth. Falsehood is a coincidental possibility, not part of the definition.
Al-Sa'd al-Taftazani is cited as supporting that falsehood is only a rational possibility.
4
Contrast with the alternative view
Al-Shirshimi mentions that some scholars accept pure taghlib without the linguistic derivation: even if every connotation could be contested, the term tasdiq is used predominantly for truth. This shows the flexibility of the principle.
The passage ends by clarifying that the relation (al-nisba) is always a connection (thubut), whether affirmed or negated – this reinforces that tasdiq is about affirming that relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ ذَلِكَ : «تَصْدِيقاً» ، [تَغْلِيباً لِأَشْرَفِ احْتِمَالَيْهِ وَهُوَ الصِّدْقُ]؛ لِأَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ لُغَةٌ : النِّسْبَةُ إِلَى الصِّدْقِ، وَالخَبَرُ وَإِنِ احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ وَالكَذِبَ ، لَكِنْ مَدْلُولَهُ الصِّدْقُ لَيْسَ إِلَّا ، وَأَمَّا الكَذِبُ فَاحْتِمَالُ عَقْلِيُّ، كَمَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ السَّعْدُ . الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَإِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ ذَلِكَ : تَصْدِيقاً هذا جواب عن سؤال حاصله : أنَّ هذا الإدراك تارة يكون صادقاً إذا أدرك النسبة على ما هي عليه في نفس الأمر ك: إدراك حدوث العالم، وتارة يكون كاذباً إذا أدركها على ما ليست عليه ك: «إدراك الفلسفي قدمه»، فكلُّ كلام يحتمل الصدق والكذب بهذا الاعتبار. فأجاب المحنِّي : بأنَّ التصديق»: النسبة إلى «الصدق»، وهو: «مطابقة الخبر للواقع»، في تصديقك للخبر» : نسبتُكَ إيَّاه إلى الصدق إلى مطابقة الواقع، والخبر ليس إلا مدلول الصدق؛ لأنَّ مدلوله ما فُهِمَ منه ، ولم يُفهم منه إلَّا الصدق، فإذا اعتقدت حصول ذلك المفهوم، كان ذلك الاعتقاد تصديقاً له، وأما إدراكك خلاف مفهومه فهو احتمال جوزه عقلك، ولا يدلُّ عليه الكلام؛ لأنَّه ضدُّ مفهومه، فكيف يدلُّ عليه . وقال بعضهم : على تسليم أنَّ كلَّ مدلول يكون تسميته تصديقاً ؛ تغليباً لأشرف احتماليه وهو الصدق . واعلم أنَّ النِّسبة دائماً الثبوت ; أي: الارتباط والتَّعلُّق ؛ سواء كان في القضيَّة الموجبة أو السالبة، فيكون ذلك الارتباط تارة مثبتاً وتارةً منفيا .
And it is only called 'tasdiq' because of the predominance of its more honorable possibility, which is truth; because 'tasdiq' linguistically is attribution to truth. The statement, even if it admits truth and falsehood, its indication is nothing but truth. As for falsehood, it is a rational possibility, as al-Sa'd explicitly stated. [Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'And it is only called tasdiq' this is a response to a question whose gist is: that this perception is sometimes truthful if it perceives the relation as it is in itself, like perceiving the temporality of the world; and sometimes false if it perceives it otherwise, like the philosopher's perception of its eternity. So every speech admits truth and falsehood in this respect. The author answered that 'tasdiq' is attribution to 'truth', which is the correspondence of the statement to reality. In your 'tasdiq' of the statement, you attribute it to truth, to correspondence with reality. And the statement indicates nothing but truth, because what is understood from it is only truth. So when you believe in that understood meaning, that belief is a tasdiq of it. As for your perceiving the opposite of its meaning, that is a possibility your mind allows, but the speech does not indicate it, because it is the opposite of its meaning, so how could it indicate it? And some said: granting that every connotation, its naming 'tasdiq' is due to the predominance of its more honorable possibility, which is truth. And know that the relation is always one of affirmation, i.e., connection and attachment, whether in affirmative or negative propositions. So that connection is sometimes affirmed and sometimes negated.]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage explains why the perception of a relation is called 'tasdiq' (confirmation) even though it can be false. The reason is 'taghlib al-ashraf' – giving predominance to the more honorable aspect, which is truth (sidq). Linguistically, 'tasdiq' derives from 'sidq' (truth), and although a statement (khabar) can be true or false, its primary meaning is truth; falsehood is only a rational possibility, not part of the intended meaning. Al-Shirshimi elaborates: the objection is that tasdiq can be true or false (e.g., 'the world is created' is true, while 'the world is eternal' is false), so why call it confirmation? The answer: the word 'khabar' inherently denotes truth; falsehood is a later possibility. Therefore, when you affirm the content, it is confirmed as true. The alternative view, also cited, is that it is purely due to taghlib. The passage also clarifies that the relation in a proposition is always a connection (thubut), whether the proposition is affirmative or negative; in negatives, the connection is negated.

Key Terms
تصديق (tasdiq): Perception of a relation; named due to attribution to truth (sidq) by predominance of the true aspect.
تغليب (taghlib): Predominance; giving precedence to the more honorable or more common aspect in naming.
صدق (sidq): Truth, correspondence of the statement to reality; the basis for the term 'tasdiq'.
احتمال عقلي (ihtimal 'aqli): Rational possibility; falsehood is a possibility entertained by the mind, not indicated by the speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a false statement (e.g., 'the world is eternal') still called 'tasdiq' according to the passage?
A) Because falsehood is impossible in speech.
B) Because the term is derived from 'truth' and falsehood is only a rational possibility, not the intended meaning.
C) Because logicians ignore truth conditions.
D) Because 'tasdiq' means submission, not truth.

Key Takeaway
The naming of tasdiq is based on taghlib, prioritizing the truthful aspect over the false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In usul al-fiqh, the term 'nahy' (prohibition) is primarily understood as forbidding (tahrim) even though it can be for dislike (karahah). Explain the role of taghlib in this naming, using the principle from the passage.

Basic Definitions of Nazari and Dharuri
Bajuri defines nazari and dharuri in their first sense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish nazari from dharuri knowledge based on the need for reflection.

Core Idea
Nazari requires reflection; dharuri does not.

This lesson introduces the foundational distinction between knowledge that demands deliberate thought (nazari) and knowledge that is self-evident or necessary (dharuri). The passage from Bajuri's commentary on the matn defines these terms clearly, setting the stage for more nuanced discussions in later lessons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the terms being defined: 'al-nazari' and 'al-dharuri' in the Arabic.
They are opposites: each is defined in terms of the other.
2
Extract the core definitions
Nazari: what requires reflection (tamamul). Dharuri: what does not require reflection (its opposite).
The adjective 'jali' (clear) is added to emphasize that dharuri is manifestly necessary.
3
Understand the scope of dharuri in the first sense
In the first sense (opposed to nazari), dharuri includes all knowledge that is not acquired through reasoning, including sense perception and intuition.
This is the broader sense.
4
Apply the definition to an example
Consider the knowledge that 'the whole is greater than the part.' Is it nazari or dharuri? It is dharuri because it is immediately evident without reflection.
Islamic kalam uses such examples for self-evident truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢١) وَ(النَّظَرِي»: مَا احْتَاجَ لِلتَّأَمُّلِ وَعَكْسُهُ هُوَ الضَّرُورِيُّ الجَلِي
وَأَمَّا عَلَى القَوْلِ بِأَنَّهُ مَا لَا يَحْتَاجِ لِشَيْءٍ أَصْلاً ، فَيَكُونُ أَخَصَّ مِنْهُ؛ لِانْفِرَادِ الضَّرُورِيِّ عَلَى هَذَا بِالحَدَسِيَّاتِ وَالتَّجْرِبِيَّاتِ ؛ لِتَوَقُفِهِمَا عَلَى الحَدْسِ وَالتَّجْرِبَةِ .
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الضَّرُورِيَّ كَمَا يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ النَّظَرِي ، وَيُفَسَّرُ بِمَا ذُكِرَ كَمَا هُنَا ، يُسْتَعْمَلُ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ الاكْتِسَابِي وَيُفَسَّرُ بِـ : مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْعَبْدِ فِيهِ اكْتِسَابٌ ، وَهُوَ بِهَذَا المَعْنَى أَخَصُّ مِنْهُ بِالمَعْنَى الأَوَّلِ ؛ لانْفِرَادِهِ فِي العِلْمِ الحَاصِلِ بِالأَبْصَارِ المَقْصُودِ مِمَّنْ كَانَ مُعْمِضاً عَيْنَيْهِ فَفَتَحَهُمَا قَصْداً، فَإِنَّهُ ضَرُورِيٌّ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ دُونَ الثَّانِي ؛ لِأَنَّهُ مُكْتَسَبٌ لِلعَبْدِ بِفَتْحِ عَيْنَيْهِ؛ أَفَادَهُ المَلَّوِيُّ فِي كَبِيرِهِ. قَوْلُهُ : (الجَلِي) أي : الوَاضِحُ ، وَهُوَ وَصْفٌ كَاشِفٌ لِـ «الضَّرُورِيِّ».
(21) And 'al-nazari' is what requires reflection, and its opposite is 'al-dharuri al-jali'. And as for the view that it is what does not need anything at all, then it is more specific than it; because the dharuri on this view is unique to the intuitive and experiential, since they depend on intuition and experience. And know that 'al-dharuri' is used in opposition to 'al-nazari', and is interpreted as mentioned here, and is used in opposition to 'al-iktisabi' and is interpreted as: what the servant has no acquisition in, and it is in this sense more specific than the first meaning; because it is unique to the knowledge obtained by sight intended from one who was closing his eyes and then opened them intentionally, for it is dharuri in the first sense but not the second; because it is acquired by the servant by opening his eyes; al-Malawi informed us in his large work. His statement: 'al-jali' means 'al-wadih' (clear), and it is a descriptive attribute revealing 'al-dharuri'.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage defines the terms 'nazari' and 'dharuri' as types of knowledge. The author begins by citing the matn verse: 'Al-nazari is what requires reflection, and its opposite is al-dharuri al-jali.' Then he expands on the definition of dharuri, noting a second interpretation: that dharuri is what does not need anything at all. On this view, dharuri is more specific because it excludes intuitive and experiential knowledge, which depend on prior mental acts. He then explains that dharuri has two usages: one opposed to nazari (as defined here) and one opposed to iktisabi (acquired). In the second usage, it is more specific, excluding knowledge gained by deliberate action (e.g., opening one's eyes intentionally). He concludes by clarifying that the adjective 'jali' means 'clear' and simply describes dharuri.

Key Terms
النَّظَرِي
الضَّرُورِي
الجَلِي

A) It is acquired through effort.
B) It does not require reflection.
C) It is limited to intuitive knowledge.
D) It is always sensory.

Key Takeaway
Nazari knowledge requires reflection; dharuri knowledge does not.

Two Senses of Dharuri: Broader and Narrower
Bajuri expands on the two usages of 'dharuri'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two uses of 'dharuri' (opposed to nazari vs. opposed to iktisabi) and classify examples accordingly.

Core Idea
Dharuri has two meanings: broader (no reflection) and narrower (no acquisition by the servant).

Bajuri expands the discussion by noting that the term 'dharuri' is used in two distinct senses. The first, already encountered, opposes dharuri to nazari. The second, more specific, opposes dharuri to iktisabi (acquired). Understanding this nuance is crucial for accurately applying these terms in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Recall the first meaning of dharuri
Dharuri1: knowledge that does not require reflection, encompassing all necessary truths including intuition and experience.
This is the broader sense.
2
Introduce the second meaning
Dharuri2: knowledge in which the servant has no acquisition (iktisab). It excludes knowledge gained through deliberate action, such as opening one's eyes intentionally.
This is the narrower sense.
3
Compare the two meanings
Dharuri2 is more specific because it excludes knowledge that, while not requiring reflection, nevertheless involves an act of the servant (e.g., intentional sense perception).
The example given: one who intentionally opens eyes gains visual knowledge; it is dharuri1 but not dharuri2.
4
Apply the distinction to a new example
Consider the knowledge that 'fire is hot' gained by intentionally touching fire. Is it dharuri1? Yes, no reflection needed. Is it dharuri2? No, because it involves an act of acquisition.
This shows the narrower sense excludes volitional experiences.

The Condition of Consideration in Signification Definitions
Bajuri adds the condition of 'min haythu' to prevent overlap among the three types of signification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition 'min haythu' to correctly distinguish among the three types of signification (مطابقة, تضمن, التزام) and resolve cases of apparent overlap.

Core Idea
Without the 'min haythu' condition, the three significations collapse into one.

In defining the three types of word signification—agreement, inclusiveness, and commitment—the classical logicians faced a problem: the same utterance could satisfy multiple definitions. Al-Bajuri clarifies that a subtle condition, 'insofar as it is' (من حيث), must be appended to each definition to prevent overlap. This lesson will walk through the problem and its resolution using the homonymous example of 'sun'.

Guided Path
1
Review the bare definitions without the condition
Without the condition, signification of agreement (مطابقة) is when the word signifies its whole meaning; inclusiveness (تضمن) is when it signifies a part; commitment (التزام) is when it signifies an external necessary concomitant.
These definitions seem clear, but they overlap when a word is homonymous.
2
Identify the overlap using the homonymous example of 'شمس'
Assume 'شمس' is coined for three meanings: body alone, light alone, and the composite of body and light. If the word is coined for the composite, then signifying the body alone is تضمن (part of the composite). Yet the definition of مطابقة also applies because the word does correspond to the body when considered as a separate coinage. Thus, the same act of signification falls under two definitions.
The coinage considered matters; without 'min haythu', we cannot distinguish which aspect is intended.
3
Introduce the condition 'min haythu' as a fix
For مطابقة: the word signifies its meaning 'insofar as it is its meaning'. For تضمن: 'insofar as it is part of its meaning'. For التزام: 'insofar as it is a necessary concomitant'. This restricts each definition to the specific aspect of the coinage.
The condition 'min haythu' specifies the perspective from which the signification is considered.
4
Apply the condition to the problematic cases
If 'شمس' is coined for the composite, then it signifies the body alone not 'insofar as it is its meaning' (since the meaning is the composite), but 'insofar as it is part of its meaning'. So it is تضمن, not مطابقة. Similarly, if coined for the body alone, it signifies the light alone 'insofar as it is a necessary concomitant', i.e., التزام.
The condition elegantly resolves the overlap.

وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ قَيْدَ الحَيْنِيَّةِ مُعْتَبَرُ هُنَا، وَكَذَا فِي كُلِّ مِنْ دَلَالَةِ التَّضَمُّنِ وَالِالْتِزامِ، كَمَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ بَعْضُهُمْ حَيْثُ قَالَ فِي دَلَالَةِ المُطَابَقَةِ : مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَعْنَاهُ، وَفِي دَلَالَةِ التَّضَمُّنِ : مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ جُزْءُ مَعْنَاهُ»، وَفِي دَلَالَةِ الاِلْتِزامِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ لَازِمُ مَعْنَاهُ. وَالغَرَضُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ : الفَرَارُ مِنِ انْتِقَاضِ كُلِّ مِنَ الدَّلَالَاتِ الثَّلَاثِ بِالأُخْرَيَيْنِ، فِيمَا إِذَا فَرَضْنَا أَنَّ لَفْظَ الشَّمْسِ مَثَلاً مُشْتَرَكْ بَيْنَ : الجِرْمِ وَحْدَهُ، وَالضَّوءِ وَحْدَهُ، وَالمَجْمُوعِ - لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا نُظِرَ إِلَى وَضْعِهِ لِلمَجْمُوعِ، تَكُونُ دَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى كُلِّ مِنَ الجِرْمِ وَحْدَهُ، وَالضَّوْءِ وَحْدَهُ : دَلَالَةَ تَضَمُّنٍ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا تَعْرِيفُ دَلَالَةِ المُطَابَقَةِ؛ لأنَّ اللَّفْظَ قَدْ دَلَّ عَلَى مَا وَافَقَهُ بِالنَّظَرِ لِوَضْعِهِ لِكُلِّ مِنْهُمَا عَلَى حِدَّتِهِ. وَإِذَا نَظَرَ لِوَضْعِهِ لِلجِرْمِ وَحْدَهُ، تَكُونُ دَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى الضَّوْءِ وَحْدَهُ: «دَلَالَةَ التِزامِ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا تَعْرِيفُ دَلَالَةِ المُطَابَقَةِ؛ لأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ قَدْ دَلَّ عَلَى مَا وَافَقَهُ بِالنَّظَرِ لِوَضْعِهِ لِلضَّوءِ وَحْدَهُ. فَبِقَيْدِ الحَيْنِيَّةِ المَذْكُورَةِ يَخْرُجُ مَا ذُكِرَ عَنْ تَعْرِيفِ دَلَالَةِ المُطَابَقَةِ؛ لِأَنَّ دَلَالَةَ لَفْظِ الشَّمْسِ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ لَيْسَتْ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ مَعْنَاهُ، بَلْ مِنْ حِيْثُ إِنَّهُ جُزْءُ مَعْنَاهُ عَلَى الأَوَّلِ، وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهُ لَازِمُ مَعْنَاهُ عَلَى الثَّانِي. - وَلِأَنَّهُ إِذَا نُظِرَ لِوَضْعِهِ لِلجِرْمِ وَحْدَهُ، تَكُونُ دَلَالَتُهُ عَلَيْهِ : دَلَالَةَ مُطَابَقَةٍ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا تَعْرِيفُ دَلَالَةِ التَّضَمُّنِ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ قَدْ دَلَّ عَلَى جُزْءِ مَعْنَاهُ بِالنَّظَرِ لِوَضْعِهِ لِلمَجْمُوعِ. وَتَكُونُ دَلَالَتُهُ عَلَى الضَّوْءِ وَحْدَهُ: دَلَالَةَ التِزامِ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهَا تَعْرِيفُ دَلَالَةِ التَّضَمُّنِ؛ لأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ قَدْ دَلَّ عَلَى جُزْءِ مَعْنَاهُ بِالنَّظَرِ لِذَلِكَ.
Know that the condition of consideration is observed here, and likewise in each of the significations of inclusiveness and commitment, as some of them made explicit when they said concerning signification of agreement: 'insofar as it is its meaning', and concerning signification of inclusiveness: 'insofar as it is part of its meaning', and concerning signification of commitment: 'insofar as it is a necessary concomitant of its meaning'. The purpose of that is to avoid the infringement of each of the three significations by the other two, in the case where we suppose that the word 'sun', for example, is homonymous between the body alone, the light alone, and the composite - because if one considers its coinage for the composite, its signification of each of the body alone and the light alone is signification of inclusiveness, while the definition of signification of agreement applies to it, because the word has signified what corresponds to it by virtue of its coinage for each of them individually. And if one considers its coinage for the body alone, its signification of the light alone is signification of commitment, while the definition of signification of agreement applies to it, because the word has signified what corresponds to it by virtue of its coinage for the light alone. So by the condition of consideration mentioned, what was mentioned exits from the definition of signification of agreement; because the signification of the word 'sun' of what was mentioned is not insofar as it is its meaning, but insofar as it is part of its meaning in the first case, and insofar as it is a necessary concomitant of its meaning in the second case. And because if one considers its coinage for the body alone, its signification of it is signification of agreement, while the definition of signification of inclusiveness applies to it; because the word has signified a part of its meaning by virtue of its coinage for the composite. And its signification of the light alone is signification of commitment, while the definition of signification of inclusiveness applies to it; because the word has signified a part of its meaning by virtue of that.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the definitions of the three types of signification (دلالة المطابقة، دلالة التضمن، دلالة الالتزام). The commentator, al-Bajuri, emphasizes that a condition (قيد) must be added to each definition: the word must signify the meaning 'insofar as it is its meaning' for مطابقة, 'insofar as it is part of its meaning' for تضمن, and 'insofar as it is a necessary concomitant of its meaning' for التزام. Without this condition, the definitions overlap, which he demonstrates using the example of the word 'شمس' (sun) when it is homonymous among three meanings: the sun's body alone, the light alone, and the composite of body and light. For instance, if the word is coined for the composite, then when it signifies the body alone, it is technically a case of تضمن (part-whole), yet the definition of مطابقة would also apply because the word does correspond to that meaning individually. Similarly, if the word is coined for the body alone, then signifying the light alone is التزام (necessary concomitant), but the definition of مطابقة also applies because the word corresponds to the light. By adding the condition 'min haythu', we exclude these cases from the definition of مطابقة because in the first case the signification is 'insofar as it is a part', not 'insofar as it is the meaning'. The same logic applies to the other definitions. This refinement guards against a common misunderstanding where one might think the definitions are sufficient without the consideration of the aspect from which the signification is taken.

دلالة التضمن
دلالة الالتزام

Checkpoint
Consider the word 'خمر' (wine) which is understood to mean an intoxicating drink. If someone uses the word 'خمر' but means only its intoxicating property (not the liquid), which type of signification is it? According to the condition of consideration, what would we say?
A) It is signification of agreement (مطابقة) because the word corresponds to the intended meaning.
B) It is signification of inclusiveness (تضمن) because intoxication is a part of the meaning of khamr.
C) It is signification of commitment (التزام) because intoxication necessarily accompanies wine, and it is signified insofar as it is a necessary concomitant.
D) It is not a valid signification because the word 'khamr' is not coined for intoxication alone.

Key Takeaway
The condition 'min haythu' is essential to prevent overlap among the three types of signification by specifying the respect in which the word signifies its meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the Arabic word 'كتاب' (book) which can refer to the physical object, its content, or both. If someone uses 'كتاب' to mean only the content, classify the signification using the condition 'min haythu'. Explain your reasoning.
?
Take a real example from fiqh: the word 'بيع' (sale) is defined as an exchange of property. If a jurist says 'بيع signifies the offer and acceptance', would that be مطابقة or تضمن? Apply the condition.

Mufrad, Murakkab, Mu'allaf: The Classification of Expressions
Author defines and classifies expressions into simple, compound, and composite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Arabic expression as mufrad, murakkab, or mu'allaf based on whether its parts indicate parts of its meaning.

Core Idea
An expression's logical status depends on whether its parts contribute to its meaning.

In Islamic logic, before analyzing terms in a proposition, we must know how an expression conveys meaning. The logicians divide expressions into simple (mufrad) and compound (murakkab), with a third category (mu'allaf) in some systems. This lesson teaches you the criterion: does the part of an expression indicate any part of its overall meaning? Mastering this division is the first step to understanding definitions and syllogisms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entire expression
Determine the expression you want to classify (e.g., a single word, a phrase, a sentence).
The expression must be a unit; e.g., 'Zayd' or 'Zayd qa'im'.
2
Break the expression into parts
Divide the expression into its smallest meaningful units (words or morphemes). In Arabic, consider if the parts are nouns, verbs, or particles.
For 'Abdullah' as a name, the parts are 'Abd' and 'Allah', but they are combined as a single label.
3
Apply the criterion
Ask: Does any part indicate a part of the overall meaning? If no part does, it is mufrad (e.g., 'Zayd' – the letters do not indicate any part of the meaning of Zayd). If a part does indicate a part of the meaning, it is murakkab (or mu'allaf in the ternary view).
The criterion is about indication of meaning, not mere composition.
4
Determine the subtype if compound
If compound, identify the type: additive (idafi) like 'ghulam Zayd', restrictive (taqyidi) like 'hayawan natiq', or predicative (isnadi) like 'Zayd qa'im'. In the binary view, all are murakkab; in the ternary, predicative is mu'allaf.
The passage confirms that in the binary division, compound and composite are synonymous.
5
Practice with examples
Use examples from Islamic sciences: e.g., 'kitab Allah' (idafi), 'hayy an-natiq' (taqyidi), 'al-'alam hadith' (isnadi), or 'al-ibadah' (mufrad).
Notice that proper nouns like 'Abdullah' are treated as mufrad in logic even though they consist of two words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ
مستعمل الألفاظ حيث يوجد إما مركب وإما مفرد فأول: ما دل جزؤه على جزء معناه بعكس ما تلا.
قال الباجوري: قوله: (حيث يوجد) أي: في أي تركيب يوجد ذلك فيه، فهي حيثية إطلاق.
قوله: (إما مركب وإما مفرد) يعني أنه لا يخرج عنهما، وهذا مبني على أن القسمة ثنائية. وجعلها بعضهم ثلاثية:
(1) - مفرد، وهو: «ما لا يدل جزؤه على شيء أصلاً».
(2) - ومركب، وهو: ما يدل جزؤه على معنى ليس جزء معناه.
(3) - ومؤلف، وهو: ما يدل جزؤه على جزء معناه، والحق الأول.
ودخل تحت المركب: المركب الإضافي: غلام زيد، والتقييدي كـ: «حيوان ناطق»، والإسنادي كـ: زيد قائم». وتحت المفرد: الاسم، والفعل، والحرف.
قال الأنبابي: قوله: (ثنائية) وعلى هذه الطريقة فالمركب والمؤلف مترادفان.
قوله: (مفرد) كـ: زيد.
قوله: (ومركب) كـ «عبد الله» علماً، على ما فيه.
قوله: (ومؤلف) كـ: زيد قائم.
Chapter on topics of expressions. The used expressions wherever found are either compound or simple. So the first: that whose part indicates a part of its meaning, contrary to what follows. Al-Bajuri said: His statement: (wherever found) meaning: in any composition that is found, so it is a 'whereness' of absoluteness. His statement: (either compound or simple) means that it does not go beyond them, and this is based on the division being binary. Some made it ternary: (1) simple, which is: 'that whose part does not indicate anything at all.' (2) Compound, which is: that whose part indicates a meaning that is not part of its meaning. (3) Composite, which is: that whose part indicates a part of its meaning, and the correct is the first. Included under compound: additive compound: Ghulam Zayd, and restrictive like 'rational animal', and predicative like 'Zayd is standing'. And under simple: noun, verb, and particle. Al-Anbabi said: His statement: (binary) and according to this method, compound and composite are synonymous. His statement: (simple) like 'Zayd'. His statement: (and compound) like 'Abdullah' as a proper noun, with what is in it. His statement: (and composite) like 'Zayd is standing'.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage defines the classification of expressions (al-alfaz) into simple (mufrad) and compound (murakkab). The matn (core text) states that wherever expressions are used, they are either compound or simple. Then it defines the first type (which is compound) positively: its part indicates a part of its meaning. The second type (simple) is defined by negation: its part does not indicate part of its meaning. The commentator al-Bajuri expands: the division is binary (murakkab vs mufrad). Some scholars add a third type, mu'allaf (composite), defined as a compound where the part indicates a part of the meaning (which is actually the same as the matn's definition of murakkab). Al-Bajuri says the correct is the binary division. Al-Anbabi clarifies that in the binary view, murakkab and mu'allaf are synonyms. The passage then subdivides compound into three: 1) additive (al-murakkab al-idafi), e.g., 'ghulam Zayd' (Zayd's slave); 2) restrictive (al-taqyidi), e.g., 'hayawan natiq' (rational animal); 3) predicative (al-isnadi), e.g., 'Zayd qa'im' (Zayd is standing). Simple expressions are further divided into noun, verb, and particle. Examples from al-Anbabi: mufrad like 'Zayd' (a single word), murakkab like 'Abdullah' as a proper noun (which is a compound word but considered a single unit in meaning), and mu'allaf like 'Zayd qa'im' (a full sentence). The key logical point: the classification is based on whether the parts indicate the parts of the meaning. For example, in 'bayt' (house), the letters do not indicate any part of the meaning of 'house', so it is mufrad. In 'ghulam Zayd', the parts 'ghulam' and 'Zayd' each indicate part of the overall meaning (slave and ownership), so it is murakkab. In a predicative sentence like 'Zayd qa'im', the parts indicate the subject and predicate, which are parts of the meaning, so it is mu'allaf/composite. In the binary view, the predicative compound is simply a type of murakkab.

مركب
مؤلف

D) 'Zayd qa'im' (زيد قائم)

Key Takeaway
The classification of expressions into mufrad, murakkab, and mu'allaf depends on whether the parts of the expression indicate parts of the meaning; this distinction is foundational for logical analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Universal and Particular: Definitions and Key Distinctions
Author defines universal and particular, clarifying the division of the singular.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a universal and a particular concept according to Islamic logicians, and explain why universality is a property of meanings, not words.

Core Idea
A universal is a meaning predicable of many; a particular is not. The division is about meanings, not words.

The author begins by stating the two fundamental types of singular terms: universal and particular. But he immediately clarifies a crucial point: this division is primarily about meanings (ma‘ānī), not about words (alfāẓ). Universality and particularity are truly attributes of concepts, while applying them to words is metaphorical. Understanding this will prevent confusion when logicians discuss definitions and syllogisms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
The author states that the singular (mufrad) is divided into two: kullī and juz'ī. Note that this division applies wherever the singular term occurs.
This is a binary classification fundamental to logic.
2
Recognize the true subject of the division
The division is with respect to the meaning, not the word. Why? Because it is the meaning that is truly described as universal or particular. Describing the word as such is metaphorical.
This parallels the distinction between lafẓ and ma'nā.
3
Understand the reciprocal relation
Every universal is a part of its particular, and every particular is a whole for its universal. For example, 'human' is a part of 'Zaid', and 'Zaid' is a whole containing 'human' plus an individual determinant.
This relation helps in analyzing definitions.
4
Analyze the formal definition
The universal is defined as 'that which indicates sharing' (mufhim ishtirāk). The particular is its opposite. Check why this definition does not apply to a proper name like 'Zaid' even if many share it – because predication is different from mere common usage.
Mufhim ishtirāk means the concept can be truly said of each individual.
