وَهُوَ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ - أَعْنِي : المُفْرَدَا - كُلِّيَّ، اَوْ جُزْنِيُّ حَيْثُ وُجِدَا. وَهَذَا التَّقْسِمُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِاعْتِبَارِ كُلِّيَّةِ المَعْنَى وَجُزْنِيَّتِهِ ; لأَنَّهُ هُوَ الَّذِي يَتَّصِفُ بِالكُلِّيَّةِ وَالجُزْئِيَّةِ حَقِيقَةٌ، وَأَمَّا وَصْفُ اللَّفْظِ بِهِمَا فَهُوَ مَجَازٌ مِنْ وَصْفِ الدَّالّ بِمَا لِلمَدْلُولِ، كَمَا أَنَّ التَّرْكِيبَ وَالإِفْرَادَ وَصْفَانِ لِلَّفْظِ حَقِيقَةٌ، وَأَمَّا وَصْفُ المَعْنَى بِهِمَا فَهُوَ مَجَازٌ مِنْ وَصْفِ المَدْلُولِ بِمَا لِلدَّالٌ، فَتَأَمَّلْ . قَوْلُهُ : (أَعْنِي : المُفْرَدَا) هَذَا المَقَامُ لَيْسَ لِلعِنَايَةِ ; لأَنَّهُ لَا يُؤتَى بِهَا إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ هُنَاكَ خَفَاءُ، وَمَا هُنَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ ; لأَنَّ رُجُوعَ الضَّمِيرِ لِـ مَا تَلَا الَّذِي هُوَ المُفْرَدُ مَعْلُومٌ مِنْ قَاعِدَةِ أَنَّ الضَّمِيرَ يَرْجِعُ لِأَقْرَبَ مَذْكُورٍ ، كَذَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ كَلَامِ بَعْضِ المُحَقِّقِينَ. وَقَدْ يُقَالُ : لَمَّا كَانَ قَدْ يُتَوَهَّمُ أَنَّ الصَّمِيرَ عَائِدٌ لِلمُرَكَّب، لأَنَّهُ هُوَ المُحَدَّثُ عَنْهُ فِي قَوْلِهِ : «فَأَوَّلُ ... إلخ»، أَتَى المُصَنِّفُ بِالعِنَايَةِ لِمَا فِي المَقَام مِنَ الخَفَاءِ بِهَذَا الاِعْتِبَارِ . قَوْلُهُ : (كُلِّيٌّ ، أَوْ جُزْنِيُّ بِإِسْقَاطِ الهَمْزَةِ بَعْدَ نَقْلِ حَرَكَتِهَا لِلسَّاكِنِ قَبْلَهَا الَّذِي هُوَ التَّنْوِينُ، وَبِمَنْعِ صَرْفِ جُزْئِي لِلوَزْنِ. وَالكُلِّي نِسْبَةٌ لِلْكُلِّ الَّذِي هُوَ الجُزْنِيُّ، وَالجُزْنِيُّ نِسْبَةٌ لِلْجُزْءِ الَّذِي هُوَ الكُلِّيُّ، وَذَلِكَ لأَنَّ القَاعِدَةَ: «أَنَّ كُلَّ كُلِّيّ جُزْءٌ مِنْ جُزْنِيهِ، وَكُلَّ جُزْنِي كُلٌّ لِكُلِّيِّهِ» ; لِأَنَّ حَقِيقَةَ الجُزْنِي مُرَكَّبَةٌ مِنَ الكُلِّي وَمِنَ الشَّخْصِ، فَالجُزْنِيُّ كُلٌّ لِلْكُلّي، وَالكُلّيُّ جُزْءٌ لِلْجُزْنِي . فَصْلٌ فِي مَبَاحِثِ الأَلْفَاظِ - (٢٨) وَهُوَ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ - أَعْنِي : المُفْرَدًا : كُلِّيَّ، أَوْ جُزْنِيُّ حَيْثُ وُجِدَا (٢٩) فَمُفْهِمُ اشْتِرَاكِ الكُلْيُّ» كَـ: «أَسَدٍ، وَعَكْسُهُ: «الجُزْنِيُّ». مَثَلاً : حَقِيقَةُ زَيْدِ» مُرَكَّبَةٌ مِنَ الإِنْسَانِ وَالشَّخْصِ، فَـ الإِنْسَانُ، كُلّي، وَهُوَ جُزْءٌ مِنْ جُزْنِيهِ گـ: «زَيْدٍ، وَزَيْدُ جُزْئِيٌّ ، وَهُوَ كُلٌّ لِكُلِّيهِ ، فَلْيُتَامَلْ. قَوْلُهُ : حَيْثُ وُجِدَا أَيْ: فِي أَيِّ تَرْكِيبٍ وُجِدَ فِيهِ المُفْرَدُ ، فَهِيَ حَيْثِيَّةُ إِطْلَاقٍ كَمَا مَرَّ فِي نَظِيرِهِ، وَالأَلِفُ فِيهِ لِلإطلاقِ . قَوْلُهُ : (فَمُفْهِمُ اشْتِرَاكِ ... إلخ) «الفَاءُ لِلإِنْصَاحِ ; لِأَنَّهَا أَفْصَحَتْ عَنْ شَيْءٍ مَحْذُوفٍ; وَالتَّقْدِيرُ : «إِذَا أَرَدْتَ بَيَانَ كُلِّ مِنَ الكُلِّي وَالجُزْئِي، فَمُفْهِمُ اشْتِرَاكِ ... إلخ». وَمُفْهِمُ اشْتِرَاكِ» : خَبَرٌ مُقَدَّمٌ ، وَالكُلّيُّ» : مُبْتَدَاْ مُؤَخَرٌ، وَيَجُوزُ العَكْسُ ، لَكِنَّ الأَوَّلَ أَوْلَى; لأَنَّ «الكُلّيّ» هُوَ المُعَرَّفُ وَمُفْهِمُ اشْتِرَاكِ هُوَ التَّعْرِيفُ، وَاللَّائِقُ حَمْلُ التَّعْرِيفِ عَلَى المُعَرَّفِ لَا العَكْسُ ; وَمِثْلُ ذَلِكَ يَجْرِي فِي قَوْلِهِ : وَعَكْسُهُ الجُزْنِيُّ . لَا يُقَالُ: «مُفْهِمُ الاِشْتِرَاكِ» عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ المُشْتَرَكِ ، فَكَأَنَّهُ قَالَ : فَالكُلّيُّ هُوَ المُشْتَرَكُ، وَحِينَئِذٍ يَصْدُقُ بِـ زَيْدِ الَّذِي اشْتَرَكَ فِيهِ بَنُوهُ مَثَلاً ، لأَنَّهُ مُشْتَرَكْ بَيْنَهُمْ مِنْ حَيْثُ أُبُوَّتِهِ لَهُمْ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ جُزْنِيٌّ ، فَيَكُونُ التَّعْرِيفُ غَيْرَ مَانِعِ . لأَنَّا نَقُولُ : المُرَادُ بِـ (المُشْتَرَكِ»: مَا جَرَى عَلَيْهِ اصْطِلاحُ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَهُوَ : مَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى كَثِيرِينَ»; بِمَعْنَى : أَنَّهُ يَصِحُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَيْهَا ، وَمَا ذَكَرَ لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ; لِأَنَّهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُشْتَرَكاً بَيْنَ بَنِيهِ باعْتِبَارِ أُبُوَّتِهِ لَهُمْ ، لَكِنْ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِمْ بِالمَعْنَى المَذْكُورِ.
And it (the singular) is of two types: universal or particular, wherever they are found. This division is only with respect to the universality and particularity of the meaning, because it is the meaning that is truly described by universality and particularity. As for describing the word by them, it is metaphorical, by describing the signifier with what belongs to the signified, just as composition and simplicity are true descriptions of the word, while describing the meaning by them is metaphorical, by describing the signified with what belongs to the signifier. So reflect. His statement: 'I mean: the singular' — this context does not require explanatory insertion, because it is only brought when there is obscurity, and there is none here, because the pronoun's reference to what follows, namely the singular, is known from the rule that the pronoun refers to the nearest antecedent. This is taken from the words of some verifiers. And it may be said: Since it might be imagined that the pronoun refers to the compound, because it is what is being spoken about in his statement 'the first... etc.', the author brought the explanatory insertion due to the obscurity in the context with this consideration. His statement: 'universal or particular' with dropping of the hamza after transferring its vowel to the preceding silent letter which is the tanwin, and by preventing the declension of juz’i due to the meter. And al-kulli is a relation to the whole which is the particular, and al-juz’i is a relation to the part which is the universal. This is because the rule is: 'Every universal is a part of its particular, and every particular is a whole for its universal', because the reality of the particular is composed of the universal and the individual. So the particular is a whole for the universal, and the universal is a part of the particular. A section on topics of words. (28) And it is of two types—I mean the singular: universal or particular wherever they are found. (29) So 'indicator of sharing' is the universal, like 'lion', and its opposite is the particular. For example, the reality of 'Zaid' is composed of 'human' and the individual. So 'human' is universal, and it is a part of its particular like 'Zaid', and 'Zaid' is particular, and it is a whole for its universal. So ponder. His statement: 'wherever they are found' means: in any composition in which the singular is found, it is a conditional for absolute application, as passed in its counterpart, and the alif is for absolute application. His statement: 'So indicator of sharing... etc.' The fa is for clarification, because it clarifies an omitted thing; the estimation is: 'When you want to explain each of the universal and the particular, the indicator of sharing ... etc.' And 'indicator of sharing' is a predicate fronted, and 'the universal' is a subject delayed, and the reverse is permissible, but the first is better because the universal is the defined thing and 'indicator of sharing' is the definition, and it is appropriate to predicate the definition of the defined, not the opposite. And the same applies to his statement: 'and its opposite is the particular'. It should not be said: 'indicator of sharing' is an expression for the shared thing, so it is as if he said: the universal is the shared thing. In that case, it would apply to 'Zaid' whom his sons share, for example, because he is shared among them by virtue of his fatherhood to them, while he is particular, so the definition would not be exclusive. Because we say: By 'shared' is meant what is in the terminology of the logicians, namely, what is true of many, meaning that it can be predicated of them. And what you mentioned is not like that, because although he is shared among his sons by virtue of his fatherhood to them, yet he is not true of them in the mentioned sense.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a definitional section from the commentary on al-Sullam al-Munawraq, explaining the division of the singular (mufrad) into universal (kullī) and particular (juz'ī). The author begins by stating that the singular is divided into two: universal and particular, wherever they occur. He then clarifies that this division is primarily about meanings (ma‘ānī), not words (alfāẓ). Universality and particularity are truly attributes of meanings, while describing words as universal or particular is metaphorical—transferring the attribute from the signified to the signifier. This is parallel to the division of words into simple and compound, which are truly attributes of words, and metaphorically applied to meanings. The commentary then discusses the phrasing of the matn, explaining why the author included the clarifying phrase 'I mean the singular' (a‘nī al-mufradā). Some might think it unnecessary because the pronoun clearly refers to the nearest antecedent, which is 'the singular'. However, another view holds that the pronoun might be imagined to refer to 'the compound' (murakkab) mentioned earlier, so the clarification removes that potential ambiguity. Next, he explains the pronunciation of 'kulliyyun aw juz'iyyun' with a dropped hamza and the rationale for preventing declension of juz'ī. He then gives a reciprocal definition: the universal is related to the whole (kull) which is the particular, and the particular is related to the part (juz') which is the universal. This is based on the rule that every universal is a part of its particular, and every particular is a whole for its universal, because the reality of a particular is composed of a universal and an individual. For example, 'human' (insān) is universal and is a part of the particular 'Zaid', while 'Zaid' is particular and is a whole containing 'human' plus an individual determinant. The passage then repeats the division and provides a formal definition: the universal is 'that which indicates sharing' (mufhim ishtirāk) — meaning its concept applies to many — like the word 'lion' applying to many individual lions. Its opposite, the particular, does not apply to many. The commentary analyzes the syntax: 'mufhim ishtirāk' is a fronted predicate, 'al-kulliyyu' is a delayed subject, and the reverse is also possible but the given order is better because the universal is the defined and 'mufhim ishtirāk' is the definition. An important objection is raised: if 'mufhim ishtirāk' (indicator of sharing) means the same as 'al-mushtarak' (the shared thing), then the definition would apply to a proper noun like 'Zaid' that is shared by his sons (all are called Zaid's sons). But 'Zaid' is particular, so the definition would not exclude particulars. The answer is that 'mushtarak' in logical terminology means not just that many share in the word, but that the concept is predicable of many — i.e., it can be truly said of each. 'Zaid' is not predicable of his sons; we do not say 'this son is Zaid' in a literal predication. Thus the definition is exclusive.

Checkpoint
According to the logicians, which of the following is a universal (kullī)?
A) The word 'Zaid' when many people are named Zaid
B) The concept 'human' which can be said of Zaid and Amr
C) A proper noun like 'Makkah'
D) A phrase like 'the father of Zaid'

Key Takeaway
Universality is a property of meanings that can be predicated of many; particularity applies to meanings predicable of only one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Take the following concepts and classify them as universal or particular: 'human', 'Zaid', 'book', 'this book on the table'. Explain your reasoning using the definition from this lesson.
?
2. Explain why the statement 'The word "lion" is a universal' is actually metaphorical, citing the author's distinction between meaning and word.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
8 min
Categorizing the Five Word-Meaning Relations into Four Types
Classifying the five nisab into four relational categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the five relations between expressions and meanings into four categories based on what is being related.

Core Idea
The five word-meaning relations differ by what is related: meaning-to-individuals, meaning-to-meaning, word-to-meaning, or word-to-word.

In logic, expressions and meanings have various types of relations. The classical text lists five, but the commentator shows they fall into four categories depending on whether the relation is between meaning and its individuals, meaning and another meaning, an expression and its own meaning, or between two expressions. This classification is fundamental for understanding definitions, ambiguity, and synonymy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five nisab
The matn states that the relation of expressions to meanings is five divisions. List them: tawatu', tashkik, tabayun, ishtirak, taraduf.
2
Understand the commentator's four categories
The commentator groups these five into four types based on what entities are being compared. He specifies which nisba belongs to which category.
The categories are: (1) between meaning and individuals, (2) between meaning and meaning, (3) between expression and meaning, (4) between expression and expression.
3
Map each nisba to its category
Assign tawatu' and tashkik to category 1; tabayun to category 2; ishtirak to category 3; taraduf to category 4.
Note that tabayun is between meanings, not just words.
4
Analyze the objection about the matn's wording
The commentator points out that the matn's phrase 'relation of expressions to meanings' literally only covers ishtirak. He presents two resolutions: either the phrase is concise and implies other relations, or interpret 'to' as 'with' to include all.
This shows how commentators defend the comprehensiveness of the matn.

فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي
(۳۳) وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ بِلَا نُقْصَانِ
الباجوري
(فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي)
قَوْلُهُ : (فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي) اعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَا ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ مِنَ النِّسَبِ الخَمْسَةِ : (١) - مِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى اللَّفْظِ وَأَفْرَادِهِ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ : التَّوَاطِؤُ»، وَ: «النَّشَاكُكُ». (٢) - وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى لَفْظُ وَمَعْنَى لَفْظ آخَرَ ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ : «التَّبَايُنُ»، وَمَا قَدْ يَقَعُ مِنَ الحُكْمِ بِالتَّبايُنِ بَيْنَ الْأَلْفَاظِ فَهُوَ بِالنَّظَرِ لِمَعَانِيهَا .
(۳) - وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرُ بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ : الاشْتِرَاكُ) .
(٤) - وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتبر بَيْنَ لَفْظ وَلَفْظ آخَرَ ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ : التَّرَادِفُ».
وَظَاهِرُ قَوْلِ المُصَنِّفِ : وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلمَعَانِي لَا يَفِي إِلَّا بِالَّذِي بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ الِاشْتِرَاكُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ فَكَيْفَ يُخْبِرُ عَنْهُ بِقَوْلِهِ : خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ»؟ وَأَجَابَ بَعْضُهُمْ : بِأَنَّ فِي كَلَام المُصَنِّفِ اكْتِفَاءُ ؛ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ : وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلمَعَانِي وَلِلأَلْفَاظِ، وَنِسْبَةُ المَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلأَفْرَادِ. وَجَعَلَ الشَّيْخُ المَلَّوِيُّ اللَّامَ فِي قَوْلِهِ : لِلْمَعَانِي بِمَعْنَى مَعَ»، وَجَعَلَ المُرَادَ مِنَ المَعَانِي» مَا يَشْمَلُ الأَفْرَادَ ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَيَصِيرُ كَلَامَ المُصَنِّفِ هَكَذَا : وَنِسْبَةُ الأَلْفَاظِ مَعَ نِسْبَةِ المَعَانِي وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّ هَذَا يَصْدُقُ بِنِسْبَةِ الأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلأَلْفَاظِ وَنِسْبَةِ المَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي إِمَّا حَقِيقَةٌ أَوْ بِمَعْنَى الأَفْرَادِ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
SECTION: ON EXPLAINING THE RELATION OF EXPRESSIONS TO MEANINGS.
(33) And the relation of expressions to meanings is five divisions without deficiency.
al-Bajuri.
(Section on explaining the relation of expressions to meanings.)
His saying: (Section on explaining the relation of expressions to meanings). Know that what the author mentioned of the five relations: (1) Among them is what is considered between the meaning of the expression and its individuals, and that is al-tawatu' and al-tashkuk. (2) And among them is what is considered between the meaning of an expression and the meaning of another expression, and that is al-tabayun, and whatever judgment of difference occurs between expressions is with respect to their meanings. (3) And among them is what is considered between the expression and its meaning, and that is al-ishtirak. (4) And among them is what is considered between an expression and another expression, and that is al-taraduf.
And the apparent meaning of the author's saying: 'And the relation of expressions to meanings' does not cover except that which is between the expression and its meaning, which is al-ishtirak. If that is the case, how does he inform about it with his saying: 'five divisions'? And some of them answered: that in the author's speech there is conciseness; and the implied meaning is: the relation of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and the relation of meanings to meanings and to individuals. And al-Shaykh al-Mallawi made the letter lam in his saying: 'to meanings' in the sense of 'with', and he made the intended meaning of 'meanings' that which includes individuals. According to this, the author's speech becomes: the relation of expressions with the relation of meanings. And there is no doubt that this applies to the relation of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and the relation of meanings to meanings, either really or in the sense of individuals. So let it be considered.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage begins with the matn line stating that the relation of expressions to meanings has five divisions. The commentator then explains that these five relations are of four types based on what is being related: (1) Relations between the meaning of an expression and its individuals (tawatu' and tashkuk), (2) Relations between the meaning of one expression and the meaning of another (tabayun), (3) Relations between the expression and its own meaning (ishtirak), (4) Relations between one expression and another expression (taraduf). The commentator then raises an objection: the matn's wording 'relation of expressions to meanings' only covers the third type (ishtirak), so how can it refer to five? Two answers are given: first, the phrasing is concise and implies other relations; second, al-Mallawi interprets the 'lam' as 'with', so it includes all relations between expressions and meanings in a broad sense. This shows the sophistication of the commentary, as it defends the matn's comprehensiveness.

Key Terms
التَّوَاطُؤُ
النَّشَاكُكُ
التَّبَايُنُ
الاشْتِرَاكُ
التَّرَادُفُ
نِسْبَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, which of the five nisab is considered between the meaning of one expression and the meaning of another expression?
A) al-tawāṭu'
B) al-tashkīk
C) al-tabāyun
D) al-ishtirāk

Key Takeaway
The five nisab can be grouped into four categories based on what entities are being related: meaning to individuals, meaning to meaning, expression to meaning, and expression to expression.

Which Relations Are Specific to Universals?
The commentator clarifies which relations are restricted to universals and which also apply to particulars, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which of the five relations (nisab) are restricted to universal terms and which also apply to particulars, using examples from proper names.

Core Idea
Tawāṭu' and tashkīk require universals; tabāyun, ishtirāk, and tarāduf work for particulars too.

In classical Islamic logic, the five relations between terms are not all on the same footing. Some, like tawāṭu' (univocal) and tashkīk (analogical), only make sense when the terms are universal — because they involve a single meaning shared across multiple individuals. The others — tabāyun (opposition), ishtirāk (homonymy), and tarāduf (synonymy) — can also connect particular terms, as the commentator illustrates with proper names. This lesson will break down which is which and why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five relations
List the five nisab: tawāṭu', tashkīk, tabāyun, ishtirāk, tarāduf. Note that the passage discusses all five.
2
Separate universal-specific from general
The passage states that tawāṭu' and tashkīk are specific to universals because they involve a single meaning applying to multiple individuals. The other three can occur between particulars.
For example, 'human' is a universal that applies to many individuals; 'Zayd' is a particular that refers to one person.
3
Examine the examples for particulars
Tabāyun: 'Zayd' and 'Wāshiq' are two different proper names with no overlap. Ishtirāk: the name 'Zayd' is given to two different people. Tarāduf: one person is called both 'Zayd' and 'Abū 'Abdillāh'.
These show that particulars can be related via ishtirāk and tarāduf, not just tabāyun.
4
Refute the misconception
Some claimed that all particulars are mutabāyin (completely different). The passage refutes this by showing particulars can share a name (ishtirāk) or refer to the same individual by different names (tarāduf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعْلَمْ أَنَّ بَعْضَ هَذِهِ النِّسَبِ يَخْتَصُّ بِالكُلّي، وَهُوَ التَّوَاطُؤُ وَالنَّشَاكُكُ؛ كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرُ. وَأَمَّا البَاقِي فَهُوَ غَيْرُ مُخْتَصّ بِهِ، بَلْ يَكُونُ فِي الجُزْئِي أَيْضاً، وَمِثَالُ التَّبَايُنِ فِيهِ: «زَيْدُ، وَوَاشِقٌ»، وَمِثَالُ الاشْتِرَاكِ فِيهِ: زَيْدٌ - اسْماً لابْنِ عَمْرِو -، وَزَيْدٌ - اسْماً لابْنِ بَكْرٍ، وَمِثَالُ التَّرَادُفِ فِيهِ: زَيْدُ، وَأَبُو عَبْدِ اللهِ، وَبِهَذَا التَّحْقِيقِ يُعْلَمُ رَدُّ مَا قِيلَ مِنْ أَنَّ الجُزْئِيَّ مِنْ قَبِيلِ المُتَبَايَنِ، فَافْهَمْ.
Know that some of these relations are specific to the universal, namely al-tawāṭu' and al-tashkīk, as is apparent. As for the rest, they are not specific to it, but rather occur in the particular as well. An example of al-tabāyun in it: 'Zayd' and 'Wāshiq'. An example of al-ishtirāk in it: Zayd as a name for the son of 'Amr, and Zayd as a name for the son of Bakr. An example of al-tarāduf in it: 'Zayd' and 'Abū 'Abdillāh'. And by this verification, the refutation of what was said—that the particular is of the type of al-mutabāyin—is known. So understand.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage clarifies which of the five nisab are restricted to universal terms. Tawāṭu' and tashkīk require a universal because they involve a single meaning applying to multiple individuals (e.g., 'human' applies to many humans). The other three—tabāyun, ishtirāk, and tarāduf—can also involve particular terms. Examples are given: tabāyun between two proper names 'Zayd' and 'Wāshiq' (the latter being a dog's name); ishtirāk when the same name 'Zayd' refers to two different individuals; tarāduf when one person is called both 'Zayd' and 'Abū 'Abdillāh'. The passage then refutes a mistaken claim that all particulars are necessarily mutabāyin (completely different). This shows that a single particular can be related to another via ishtirāk or tarāduf.

Key Terms
الكُلِّي
الجُزْئِي
وَاشِق
المُتَبَايَن

Key Takeaway
Tawāṭu' and tashkīk are restricted to universals; tabāyun, ishtirāk, and tarāduf also occur between particulars.

Three Additional Relations in Term Logic: Musāwī, 'Umūm wa Khuṣūṣ
Definition of three additional relations and critique of subsumption under original five

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three additional relations between terms and evaluate whether they can be subsumed under the original five relations using the definitions and critique provided in the text.

Core Idea
The original five relations can be extended to eight, but subsumption is contested, especially for absolute general-specific.

The matn's five relations are not exhaustive; the commentator adds three more: musāwī, 'umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh, and 'umūm wa khuṣūṣ bi al-iṭlāq. Some investigators argue these can be folded into the original five by broadening definitions, but later commentators like al-Anbābī object. This lesson unpacks the definitions and the refinement debate.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three additional relations
In the Arabic text, find the names: al-musāwī, al-'umūm wa al-khuṣūṣ min wajh, and al-'umūm wa al-khuṣūṣ bi al-iṭlāq. Write down their definitions as given.
Use the key terms for reference.
2
Understand the extension vs intension distinction
For each relation, note whether the terms agree or differ in extension (ṣadaq) and intension (mafhūm). This is critical: musāwī agrees in extension but differs in intension; the other two involve partial or complete inclusion.
Extension: what the term applies to; Intension: its meaning.
3
Analyze the subsumption argument
The investigator (ba'd al-muḥaqqiqīn) suggests musāwī can be included under tarāduf, and the other two under tabāyun, by broadening definitions. Understand his reasoning: relaxing conditions allows extension.
This is a critical refinement to maximize the matn's completeness.
4
Evaluate the critique by al-Anbābī
Al-Anbābī objects that the third relation cannot be classified under tabāyun because the specific is not completely different from the general; rather, it is included. Tabāyun implies no overlap, but here there is full inclusion.
Shows the importance of precise classification in the commentary tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ) بَقِيَ عَلَيْهِ ثَلَاثَةٌ، وَهِيَ : الْمُسَاوِي، وَالْعُمُومُ وَالْخُصُوصُ مِنْ وَجْهِ، وَالْعُمُومُ وَالْخُصُوصُ بِالْإِطْلَاقِ. فَضَابِطُ الْأَوَّلِ : أَنْ يَتَّحِدَا صَادَقًا وَيَخْتَلِفًا مَفْهُومًا؛ كَمَا فِي: «الْكَاتِبِ، وَالضَّاحِكِ». وَضَابِطُ الثَّانِي: «أَنْ يَجْتَمِعَا فِي مَادَّةٍ، وَيَنْفَرِدُ كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا فِي مَادَّةٍ أُخْرَى»؛ كَمَا فِي : الْإِنْسَانِ، وَالْأَبْيَضِ. وَضَابِطُ الثَّالِثِ: «أَنْ يَجْتَمِعَا فِي مَادَّةٍ، وَيَنْفَرِدُ أَحَدُهُمَا فِي مَادَّةٍ أُخْرَى»؛ كَمَا فِي : الْإِنْسَانِ، وَالْحَيَوَانِ». قَالَ بَعْضُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ: وَيُمْكِنُ إِدْرَاجُ الْأَوَّلِ فِي التَّرَادُفِ»؛ بِأَنْ يُرَادَ بِهِ مَا يَشْمَلُ مَا لَوْ كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا الِاتِّحَادُ صَادَقًا فَقَطْ - وَإِدْرَاجُ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثِ فِي التَّبَايُنِ»؛ بِأَنْ يُرَادَ بِهِ مَا يَشْمَلُ التَّبَايُنَ الْجُزْئِيَ. اهـ بِتَصَرُّفٍ)، وَعَلَيْهِ فَكَلَامُ الْمُصَنِّفِ مُسْتَوْفٍ لِجُمْلَةِ النِّسَبِ الثَّمَانِيَةِ. الأنبابي: قوله : (وَإِدْرَاجُ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثِ ... إلخ) غَيْرُ ظَاهِرٍ فِي الثَّالِثِ؛ لِأَنَّ الْخَاصَّ لَا يُبَايِنُ الْعَامَّ. اهـ عَطَّار.
His saying: (Five divisions) – there remain three [relations] beyond it: al-musāwī (equality), and generality-specificity from one aspect, and generality-specificity absolutely. The rule of the first: that they agree in extension and differ in intension, as in 'the writer' and 'the laugher'. The rule of the second: 'that they meet in one matter, and each of them is unique in another matter', as in 'human' and 'white'. The rule of the third: 'that they meet in one matter, and one of them is unique in another matter', as in 'human' and 'animal'. Some investigators said: It is possible to include the first under al-tarāduf, by intending by it that which includes when there is agreement in extension only; and to include the second and third under al-tabāyun, by intending by it that which includes partial difference. End (with modification). According to this, the author's speech covers all eight relations. al-Anbābī: His saying: (And including the second and third… etc.) is not apparent regarding the third, because the specific does not differ [completely] from the general. End (from al-'Attār).
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage addresses the completeness of the matn's enumeration. The commentator notes that three additional relations are not explicitly mentioned: (1) musāwī (equality) – two terms that are co-extensive but differ in meaning, e.g., 'writer' and 'laugher' (all writers laugh? Actually the example is from the text). (2) 'umūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh' (general and specific from one aspect) – two terms that overlap partially, e.g., 'human' and 'white' (some humans are white, some not; some white things are human, some not). (3) 'umūm wa khuṣūṣ bi al-iṭlāq' (absolute general and specific) – one term includes the other entirely, e.g., 'human' and 'animal' (all humans are animals, but not vice versa). Some investigators argue that these three can be subsumed under the original five: musāwī under tarāduf (since both have same extension), and the other two under tabāyun (as partial difference). This would make the matn's five cover all eight relations. However, al-Anbābī objects that the third (absolute general-specific) cannot be placed under tabāyun because the specific does not differ completely from the general; rather, it is included under it. This shows ongoing critical refinement in the commentary tradition.

Key Terms
الْمُسَاوِي (al-musāwī): A relation between two terms that have the same extension (ṣadaq) but different intension (mafhūm), e.g., 'the writer' and 'the laugher'. [Note: Sometimes called 'al-'āmm wa al-khāṣṣ min wajh'? No, this is distinct.]
الْعُمُومُ وَالْخُصُوصُ مِنْ وَجْهٍ (al-'umūm wa al-khuṣūṣ min wajh): A relation where two terms partially overlap – each has some instances not shared by the other, e.g., 'human' and 'white'. [Note: Stable term in logic.]
الْعُمُومُ وَالْخُصُوصُ بِالْإِطْلَاقِ (al-'umūm wa al-khuṣūṣ bi al-iṭlāq): A relation where one term is completely inclusive of the other, i.e., the 'āmm (general) and khāṣṣ (specific), e.g., 'animal' and 'human'. [Note: Stable term.]
التَّبَايُنُ الْجُزْئِيُّ (al-tabāyun al-juz'ī): Partial difference; used here to include both partial overlap (min wajh) and absolute inclusion under tabāyun broadly. [Note: This is a specific usage by the investigator; not standard.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three additional relations expand the original five, but their subsumption under tarāduf and tabāyun is contested, particularly for the absolute general-specific relation.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner
5 min
The Core Definition: What is a Proposition?
Author defines what can be true/false and lists its various names based on perspective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the essential definition of a proposition (qadiyya/khabar) and explain why the two terms are synonymous yet differ in aspect.

Core Idea
A single proposition has many names, each reflecting a different perspective on its role.

This passage introduces the foundational element of logic: the proposition. It defines what can be true or false and explains that the same entity is called 'qadiyya' from the aspect of containing a judgment and 'khabar' from the aspect of being truth-apt. Understanding this unity under multiple names is crucial for following later discussions of premises, conclusions, and scientific problems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
What entity is being defined? Find the phrase 'what admits truth for its own essence' (ما احتمل الصدق لذاته).
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus is 'what admits truth' (ما احتمل الصدق). The differentia is 'for its own essence' (لذاته), distinguishing it from statements that are truth-apt only derivatively.
3
Distinguish the two primary names
The same entity is called 'qadiyya' when emphasizing the judgment it contains, and 'khabar' when emphasizing its capacity for truth or falsity. How does the aspect change the name but not the essence?
4
Test the definition's completeness
Does this definition include all propositions (e.g., 'The world is created')? Does it exclude non-propositions like commands or questions?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا احْتَمَلَ الصَّدْقَ لِذَاتِهِ جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ: «قَضِيَّةٌ» و«خَبَرَا»
قَوْلُهُ : جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ ... إلخ) عُلِمَ مِنْهُ : أَنَّ القَضِيَّةَ وَالخَبَرَ بِمَعْنَى وَاحِدٍ، وَهُوَ : مَا احْتَمَلَ ... إلخ ، لَكِنْ تَسْمِيَّتُهُ: «قَضِيَّةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ اشْتِمَالِهِ عَلَى الحُكْمِ، وَتَسْمِيَّتُهُ : خَبَراً» مِنْ حَيْثُ احْتِمَالِهِ الصِّدْقَ .
وَفِي التَّلْوِيحِ»: أَنَّهُ يُسَمَّى: «إِخْبَاراً مِنْ حَيْثُ إِفَادَتِهِ الحُكْمَ، وَ: «مُقَدِّمَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ جُزْءاً مِنَ الدَّلِيلِ، وَ : «مَظْلُوباً » مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ يُطْلَبُ بِالدَّلِيلِ، وَ نَتِيجَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ نَتِيجَةَ الدَّلِيلِ، وَ: «مَسْأَلَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ يُسْأَلُ عَنْهُ فِي العِلْم ؛ قَالَ : فَالذَّاتُ وَاحِدَةٌ، وَاخْتِلَافُ العِبَارَاتِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الاعْتِبَارَاتِ . اهـ
قوله : (وَ): «مَسْأَلَةٌ» . . . إلخ) أي : و «دعوى»: من حيث افتقارها لدليل، و«مبحث» مِن حيث إنَّها محلُّ البحث .
What admits truth for its own essence is called 'qadiyya' and 'khabar' interchangeably. His statement: 'interchangeable...' It is known from this that qadiyya and khabar are the same meaning, i.e., what admits truth... etc. However, it is called 'qadiyya' due to its inclusion of judgment, and 'khabar' due to its admitting truth. And in al-Talwih: it is called 'ikhbar' due to its conveying judgment, and 'muqaddima' due to its being part of a proof, and 'matlub' due to its being sought by proof, and 'natija' due to its being the result of a proof, and 'mas'ala' due to its being asked about in a science. He said: the essence is one, and the difference of expressions is due to difference of considerations. End. His statement: (and 'mas'ala'... etc.) i.e., and 'da'wa' due to its need for proof, and 'mabhath' due to its being the subject of investigation.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'proposition' or 'report' and clarifies its various names. The author begins by stating that what can be true or false in itself is called both 'qadiyya' and 'khabar' interchangeably. The commentator explains that the two terms are synonymous in meaning: they both refer to that which admits truth or falsity. However, the difference lies in the aspect considered: 'qadiyya' emphasizes the inclusion of a judgment (hukm), while 'khabar' emphasizes the possibility of truth or falsity. The passage then cites al-Talwih, which adds more names: 'ikhbar' (informing) from the aspect of conveying judgment, 'muqaddima' (premise) as part of a proof, 'matlub' (sought) as that which is sought through proof, 'natija' (conclusion) as the result of a proof, and 'mas'ala' (problem) as what is asked about in a science. The commentator notes that all these names refer to the same essence; the multiplicity of names arises from different perspectives. The super-commentator al-Annababi adds that it is also called 'da'wa' (claim) because it requires proof, and 'mabhath' (topic) because it is the subject of investigation. This passage teaches the student that a single logical entity can be viewed from multiple angles, and each perspective gives it a different technical name.

Key Terms
قضية
خبر
مقدمة
مطلوب
نتيجة
مسألة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

The Many Names of the Proposition: Perspective is Everything
Author defines what can be true/false and lists its various names based on perspective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the different names of a single proposition based on its role in a proof or discipline, and explain how perspective drives terminology.

Core Idea
A single proposition can be called premise, conclusion, claim, problem, or topic — each name captures a different role.

The passage from al-Talwih expands the list of names for the same truth-bearing entity. Depending on whether it is part of a proof, sought after, the result, or the subject of a science, it receives a different technical term. This shows that logical terminology is functional, not arbitrary.

Guided Path
1
Find the list of names in al-Talwih
Locate the names: ikhbar, muqaddima, matlub, natija, mas'ala. What aspect does each name highlight?
e.g., ikhbar focuses on conveying judgment, muqaddima on being a premise.
2
Add the super-commentator's additions
Al-Annababi adds 'da'wa' and 'mabhath'. What roles do these emphasize?
da'wa emphasizes need for proof, mabhath emphasizes being a subject of investigation.
3
Understand the principle
The essence is one; differences in expressions are due to differences in considerations. Why is this principle important for avoiding confusion?
4
Apply to a real example
Take a single proposition from fiqh: 'Wine is forbidden.' How would it be referred to in different logical contexts?
e.g., as a muqaddima in a syllogism, as a matlub if seeking to prove it, as a mas'ala in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا احْتَمَلَ الصَّدْقَ لِذَاتِهِ جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ: «قَضِيَّةٌ» و«خَبَرَا»
قَوْلُهُ : جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ ... إلخ) عُلِمَ مِنْهُ : أَنَّ القَضِيَّةَ وَالخَبَرَ بِمَعْنَى وَاحِدٍ، وَهُوَ : مَا احْتَمَلَ ... إلخ ، لَكِنْ تَسْمِيَّتُهُ: «قَضِيَّةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ اشْتِمَالِهِ عَلَى الحُكْمِ، وَتَسْمِيَّتُهُ : خَبَراً» مِنْ حَيْثُ احْتِمَالِهِ الصِّدْقَ .
وَفِي التَّلْوِيحِ»: أَنَّهُ يُسَمَّى: «إِخْبَاراً مِنْ حَيْثُ إِفَادَتِهِ الحُكْمَ، وَ: «مُقَدِّمَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ جُزْءاً مِنَ الدَّلِيلِ، وَ : «مَظْلُوباً » مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ يُطْلَبُ بِالدَّلِيلِ، وَ نَتِيجَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ نَتِيجَةَ الدَّلِيلِ، وَ: «مَسْأَلَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ يُسْأَلُ عَنْهُ فِي العِلْم ؛ قَالَ : فَالذَّاتُ وَاحِدَةٌ، وَاخْتِلَافُ العِبَارَاتِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الاعْتِبَارَاتِ . اهـ
قوله : (وَ): «مَسْأَلَةٌ» . . . إلخ) أي : و «دعوى»: من حيث افتقارها لدليل، و«مبحث» مِن حيث إنَّها محلُّ البحث .
What admits truth for its own essence is called 'qadiyya' and 'khabar' interchangeably. His statement: 'interchangeable...' It is known from this that qadiyya and khabar are the same meaning, i.e., what admits truth... etc. However, it is called 'qadiyya' due to its inclusion of judgment, and 'khabar' due to its admitting truth. And in al-Talwih: it is called 'ikhbar' due to its conveying judgment, and 'muqaddima' due to its being part of a proof, and 'matlub' due to its being sought by proof, and 'natija' due to its being the result of a proof, and 'mas'ala' due to its being asked about in a science. He said: the essence is one, and the difference of expressions is due to difference of considerations. End. His statement: (and 'mas'ala'... etc.) i.e., and 'da'wa' due to its need for proof, and 'mabhath' due to its being the subject of investigation.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'proposition' or 'report' and clarifies its various names. The author begins by stating that what can be true or false in itself is called both 'qadiyya' and 'khabar' interchangeably. The commentator explains that the two terms are synonymous in meaning: they both refer to that which admits truth or falsity. However, the difference lies in the aspect considered: 'qadiyya' emphasizes the inclusion of a judgment (hukm), while 'khabar' emphasizes the possibility of truth or falsity. The passage then cites al-Talwih, which adds more names: 'ikhbar' (informing) from the aspect of conveying judgment, 'muqaddima' (premise) as part of a proof, 'matlub' (sought) as that which is sought through proof, 'natija' (conclusion) as the result of a proof, and 'mas'ala' (problem) as what is asked about in a science. The commentator notes that all these names refer to the same essence; the multiplicity of names arises from different perspectives. The super-commentator al-Annababi adds that it is also called 'da'wa' (claim) because it requires proof, and 'mabhath' (topic) because it is the subject of investigation. This passage teaches the student that a single logical entity can be viewed from multiple angles, and each perspective gives it a different technical name.

مطلوب

A single proposition can be called by many names, each highlighting a different role or perspective; the essence remains the same.

Is 'al-hamdu lillah' a Performative or Informative Sentence?
Author discusses whether 'al-hamdu lillah' is originally khabar and became 'urfiyya in insha', with rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khabar and insha' sentences and apply the principle of 'asl 'adam al-naql' to determine the default nature of 'al-hamdu lillah'.

Core Idea
Informing about Allah's praise is itself praising; the default is no transfer.

In this passage, the author presents two competing analyses of the famous phrase 'al-hamdu lillah'. One view considers it a performative utterance (insha') that has become customary, while the other insists it remains a declarative sentence (khabar) whose informing function already constitutes praise. Understanding this debate reveals the importance of linguistic defaults in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Find the two views presented: the 'mukhtar' (chosen) view that the sentence is a customary reality in insha', and the 'sawab' (correct) view that it is khabar.
2
Examine the argument for the mukhtar view
The mukhtar view argues that the sentence has been transferred from its original khabar meaning to a performative one, and because it is now a customary reality, it conveys performativity without need for context.
3
Examine the rebuttal's argument
The rebuttal argues that the default state of language is no transfer ('al-asl 'adam al-naql'); informing that praise is due to Allah is itself an act of praise, as proven by analogy with informing about a person's knowledge.
4
Apply the principle of default no transfer
Consider whether evidence justifies departure from the original meaning. The rebuttal denies such evidence.
5
Evaluate the strength of each position
Based on the passage, which view is more consistent with linguistic principles and the nature of praising?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأَوَّلُ : المُخْتَارُ أَنَّ جُمْلَةَ الحَمْدِ اللَّهِ حَقِيقَةٌ عُرْفِيَّةٌ فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، نُقِلَتْ إِلَيْهِ نْ (١) أَصْلِهَا الَّذِي هُوَ الخَبَرُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا : «إِنْشَاءُ الثَّنَاءِ بِمَضْمُونِهَا»، لَا : «إِنْشَاءُ مَضْمُونِهَا كَمَا تُوهَمَ لِاقْتِضَائِهِ حُدُوثَ اسْتِحْقَاقِهِ تَعَالَى لِلوَصْفِ بِالجَمِيلِ، وَهُوَ بَاطِلٌ؛ وَلِكَوْنِهَا حَقِيقَةٌ لَمْ يَحْتَجْ فِي إِفَادَتِهَا الإِنْشَاءَ إِلَى قَرِينَةٍ، وَلَا إِلَى نِيَّةِ إِخْرَاجِهَا عَنْ أَصْلِهَا ؛ لِأَنَّهُ هُجِرَ وَصَارَ نَسِيًّا (٢) عليه قوله : (المُخْتَارُ أَنَّ جُمْلَةَ الحَمْدِ اللهِ») تبع في هذا المختار الهلالي في شرح القادرية»، والصَّوابُ : القولُ بأنَّها خبريَّةٌ ؛ لأنَّ الأصل عدمُ النَّقل ؛ لأنَّ المخبِرَ بثبوت الحمد لله تعالى مثن وحامد له، وإن لم ينشئ ذلك ؛ ضرورةً أنَّ المخبر عن زيد بـ : «أنَّه عالم مثن عليه بالعلم، فكذلك ما هنا ؛ إذ بإخباره يكون مقرا لله تعالى بالأوصاف الجميلة، وكما يقال لمن قال: «الله واحدٌ» : «إنَّه مُوَحّدٌ» ؛ لإقراره بمقتضى خبرها . قال البقاعي في حواشيه على السَّعد» جمله الحمد خبريَّةٌ لانطباق حدّ المركب الثام المحتمل للصدق والكذب عليها، فإنَّ مدلولها ثابت مع قطع النظر عن لفظ اللافظ واعتبار المعتبر،
The first: The chosen view is that the sentence 'al-hamdu lillah' is a customary reality in performative speech, having been transferred to it from its original which is informative, and what is meant by it is: 'the performative act of praise with its content', not: 'the performative act of its content' as was imagined because it would necessitate the occurrence of His, exalted, deserving of beautiful description, and that is false; and because it is a reality, it did not need, in conveying performative speech, a contextual indicator, nor an intention of removing it from its original; because that original has been abandoned and become forgotten. Then [the commentator says]: His saying: 'The chosen view that the sentence of al-hamdu lillah' – he followed in this chosen view al-Hilali in his commentary on al-Qadiriyya, and the correct view is to say it is informative, because the original is no transfer; because the informant of the establishment of praise to Allah, Exalted, is a praiser and a praise-giver for Him, even if he does not perform that; necessarily, the informant about Zayd that 'he is knowledgeable' is a praiser of him for knowledge, so likewise here; since by his informing he becomes an acknowledgeer to Allah, Exalted, of beautiful attributes, and just as it is said to the one who says 'Allah is one': 'He is a monotheist' because of his acknowledgment of the implication of its content. Al-Baqa'i said in his glosses on al-Sa'd: The sentence 'al-hamdu' is informative because the definition of the declarative composite, which is susceptible to truth and falsehood, applies to it, for its meaning is established regardless of the utterance of the speaker and the consideration of the considerer.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about the nature of the sentence 'al-hamdu lillah'. The author first presents the chosen view (المختار) that the phrase is a 'urfiyya haqiqa (customary reality) in insha' (performative speech), having been transferred from its original khabar (informative) usage. The intended meaning is that uttering this phrase constitutes a performative act of praising its content, not that it originates or creates the praiseworthiness of Allah. The latter would falsely imply that Allah's deserving praise is contingent upon human speech. The author then notes that because it is a customary reality, it does not require a contextual indicator or intention of transfer to convey performativity. Then, a rebuttal is introduced: the correct view is that it remains a khabar. The rebuttal argues that the default state of language is no transfer (from its original meaning). When one informs that 'Praise is due to Allah', he is intrinsically praising and acknowledging Him, just as informing that Zayd is knowledgeable is praising him for knowledge. Thus, the sentence is fundamentally informative; its performative aspect is incidental, not its primary nature. The rebuttal cites al-Baqa'i, who states that the sentence is informative because it satisfies the definition of a declarative sentence (المركب الثام المحتمل للصدق والكذب) – its truth value is independent of the speaker's utterance.

Key Terms
جملة الحمد لله (jumlat al-hamdu lillah): The phrase 'Praise be to Allah', analyzed as a sentence that may be declarative or performative. [Note: In logic texts, this phrase is often analyzed for its categorical/propositional form; here it is about speech act theory.]
حقيقة عرفية (haqiqa 'urfiyya): A word used in its customary transferred sense, established by convention, not originally literal but now the default. [Note: Contrasts with haqiqa lughawiyya (literal) and haqiqa shar'iyya (legal); this term is stable in Arabic rhetoric and logic.]
إنشاء (insha'): Performative speech – an utterance that effects a change in reality or creates a state, as opposed to reporting. [Note: In logic, insha' is not a proposition; it cannot be true/false. This usage is from Arabic rhetoric (balagha).]
خبر (khabar): Informative/declarative sentence that can be true or false, reporting a state of affairs. [Note: In logic, khabar is the primary type of qadiyya; in Arabic grammar, it is the predicate of a nominal sentence.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because informing that praise is due to Allah is itself praising, and the default state is no transfer.
C) Because the phrase is used customarily for performative speech.
D) Because it cannot be true or false.

Key Takeaway
The debate about 'al-hamdu lillah' shows that linguistic classification (khabar vs insha') is not merely grammatical but carries epistemological implications for how we understand praise and divine attributes.

The Subject Matter of Logic: Conception and Assent
Author derives the subject of logic as conceptual and verificational knowledge from the discussion of accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the subject matter of logic as defined in the text and explain the reasoning from essential accidents that justifies it.

Core Idea
Logic's subject is not syllogisms — it is all conceptual and verificational knowledge.

In this passage the author culminates a discussion of accidents to pinpoint the subject matter of logic. He asserts that logic studies conceptual and verificational knowledge because it investigates the essential accidents of these types of knowledge. Understanding this foundation is crucial: it defines the scope and purpose of logic within the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conclusion
Read the first sentence: the author states that the subject of logic is 'al-ma‘lūmāt al-taṣawwuriyya wa al-taṣdīqiyya' (conceptual and verificational knowledges). This is the claim we must understand.
2
Find the premise
The author gives a reason: 'because the logician only investigates their essential accidents'. The premise is that logic deals with essential accidents of these knowledges.
3
Understand the criterion for a scientific subject
The author then states a general principle: 'that which is investigated in a science regarding its essential accidents is the subject of the science.' Apply this: since logic investigates the essential accidents of conceptual and verificational knowledges, they must be its subject.
4
Connect to the broader framework
The passage ends by directing the reader to Ibn Sīnā's *Kitāb al-Burhān* for a deeper treatment. This shows that the definition is not isolated but ties into the larger project of demonstration (burhān).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ تمهد هذا عَلِمت أنَّ موضوع المنطق : المعلوماتُ التَّصوريَّة والتصديقيَّة؛ لأنَّ المنطقي إنَّما يبحث عن أعراضها الذاتية، وما يُبحث في العِلم عن أعراضه الذاتية هو موضوع العِلم، ومَن رام تحقيق مباحث الموضوع فعليه بكتاب البرهان من منطق الشَّفاء».
Since this is established, you know that the subject of logic is the conceptual and verificational knowledges, because the logician only investigates their essential accidents, and that which is investigated in a science regarding its essential accidents is the subject of the science. And whoever desires to verify the investigations of the subject should consult the Book of Demonstration from the Logic of al-Shifā’.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage concludes from the previous classification of accidents that the subject matter of logic is the two types of knowledge: taṣawwur (conception) and taṣdīq (assent). The author argues that logic investigates the essential accidents of these knowledges. He then directs the reader to Ibn Sīnā's Kitāb al-Burhān for a deeper treatment.

Key Terms
موضوع المنطق (mawḍū‘ al-manṭiq): The subject matter of logic: the conceptual and verificational knowledges. [Note: Stable definition across the tradition.]
المعلومات التصورية والتصديقية (al-ma‘lūmāt al-taṣawwuriyya wa al-taṣdīqiyya): Knowledges that are either concepts (taṣawwur) or judgments (taṣdīq). [Note: Central terms in Islamic logic; stable.]

The Meaning of Istimdad in Logic
Author defines the term istimdad and narrows its meaning for logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two senses of istimdad and identify which one applies to the science of logic.

Core Idea
Istimdad in logic means its terminological principles, not borrowing from other sciences.

The author begins by explaining what he means by istimdad (derivation) in the context of logic. He clarifies that it refers to the foundational principles upon which logic is built, and then divides them into conceptual and assent-based matters. But first, we must understand the term itself, as it has another common meaning that could mislead us.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the Arabic phrase that defines istimdad in the context of logic. The passage states 'المراد به مبادئه الاصطلاحية'.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The definition has genus 'مبادئ' (principles) and differentia 'اصطلاحية' (terminological).
3
Note the alternative meaning
The commentary mentions a second meaning: taking from another science, e.g., borrowing from eloquence.
4
Determine why the first is correct for logic
The author says the first meaning is more in accordance with the objectives of the masters of the scale. Logic derives its principles from itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما استمداده، فالمراد به مبادئه الاصطلاحية، وهي ما يبنى عليه من الفن من أمور تصورية وأمور تصديقية. فالتصورية : حدود الأشياء التي تستعمل فيه، ويكثر دورها فيه كـ: حدود الكلي وأقسامه، والجزئي، والقضية، والموضوع والمحمول، والمقدم والتالي، ونحو ذلك. والتصديقية منها كقولنا : النقيضان لا يجتمعان، ولا يرتفعان، و: نفي الأعم يستلزم نفي الأخص، و: ثبوت الأخص يوجب ثبوت الأعم، و: الكل أعظم من الجزء، ونحو ذلك من البديهيات. وفائدة معرفة الاستمداد : الرجوع إليه عند قصد تحقيق مسألة من الفن. قوله : (وأما استمداده) الاستمداد يطلق : ١ - ويُراد به : مبادئ العلم الاصطلاحية، كما ذكر هذا الشارح. ٢ - وقد يُراد به الأخذ؛ أي: أخذ العلم من غيره؛ كاستمداد علم البيان من البلغاء. لكنَّ الأوَّل أوفق بمقاصد أرباب الميزان.
As for its derivation, what is meant by it is its terminological principles, and they are what the art is built upon from conceptual matters and assent-based matters. The conceptual matters: definitions of things used in it, which recur frequently, such as the definitions of the universal and its divisions, the particular, the proposition, the subject and predicate, the antecedent and consequent, and the like. The assent-based matters include our saying: 'The two contradictories cannot coexist nor be removed,' and 'The negation of the more general entails the negation of the more specific,' and 'The establishment of the more specific necessitates the establishment of the more general,' and 'The whole is greater than the part,' and similar self-evident truths. The benefit of knowing the derivation: to refer back to it when intending to verify an issue of the art. His saying: (As for its derivation) — derivation is used in two senses: 1. It is meant to be the terminological principles of the science, as this commentator mentioned. 2. It may also mean taking, i.e., taking the science from another, like the derivation of the science of eloquence from the eloquent. But the first is more in accordance with the objectives of the masters of the scale.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage defines the 'istimdad' (derivation) of the science of logic, which refers to its terminological principles. These principles are divided into two types: tasawwuriyyat (conceptual matters) and tasdiqiyyat (assent-based matters). The conceptual matters are definitions of frequently used terms such as universal, particular, proposition, subject, predicate, etc. The assent-based matters are self-evident propositions (badihiyyat) like the law of non-contradiction, the entailment relations between general and specific, and the whole being greater than the part. The benefit of knowing these principles is to refer back to them when verifying any issue of the science. The commentary clarifies that 'istimdad' can also mean taking from another science, but here it means terminological principles, which is more appropriate for logic. All examples are from the foundational logical axioms.

Istimdad in logic refers to its terminological principles, not to borrowing from other sciences.

Conceptual and Assent-Based Principles in Logic
Author divides terminological principles into conceptual and assent-based categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize given logical principles as either conceptual (tasawwuriyyat) or assent-based (tasdiqiyyat) and provide an example of each from the passage.

Core Idea
Logic's principles are either definitions of terms or self-evident propositions.

After defining istimdad, the author divides the terminological principles into two categories: conceptual matters and assent-based matters. Conceptual matters are the definitions of frequently used terms, while assent-based matters are self-evident truths that serve as axioms. Understanding this division helps us see the foundation upon which logical reasoning is built.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage explicitly mentions 'tasawwuriyyat' and 'tasdiqiyyat'. Conceptual matters are about definitions; assent-based matters are about propositions accepted without proof.
2
Extract examples of conceptual matters
The passage lists: definitions of universal, particular, proposition, subject, predicate, antecedent, consequent, etc.
3
Extract examples of assent-based matters
The passage lists: the two contradictories cannot coexist nor be removed, negation of the more general entails negation of the more specific, establishment of the more specific necessitates the more general, the whole is greater than the part, and similar self-evident truths.
4
Understand the benefit
The benefit of knowing these principles is to refer back to them when verifying an issue of logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما استمداده، فالمراد به مبادئه الاصطلاحية، وهي ما يبنى عليه من الفن من أمور تصورية وأمور تصديقية. فالتصورية : حدود الأشياء التي تستعمل فيه، ويكثر دورها فيه كـ: حدود الكلي وأقسامه، والجزئي، والقضية، والموضوع والمحمول، والمقدم والتالي، ونحو ذلك. والتصديقية منها كقولنا : النقيضان لا يجتمعان، ولا يرتفعان، و: نفي الأعم يستلزم نفي الأخص، و: ثبوت الأخص يوجب ثبوت الأعم، و: الكل أعظم من الجزء، ونحو ذلك من البديهيات. وفائدة معرفة الاستمداد : الرجوع إليه عند قصد تحقيق مسألة من الفن. قوله : (وأما استمداده) الاستمداد يطلق : ١ - ويُراد به : مبادئ العلم الاصطلاحية، كما ذكر هذا الشارح. ٢ - وقد يُراد به الأخذ؛ أي: أخذ العلم من غيره؛ كاستمداد علم البيان من البلغاء. لكنَّ الأوَّل أوفق بمقاصد أرباب الميزان.
As for its derivation, what is meant by it is its terminological principles, and they are what the art is built upon from conceptual matters and assent-based matters. The conceptual matters: definitions of things used in it, which recur frequently, such as the definitions of the universal and its divisions, the particular, the proposition, the subject and predicate, the antecedent and consequent, and the like. The assent-based matters include our saying: 'The two contradictories cannot coexist nor be removed,' and 'The negation of the more general entails the negation of the more specific,' and 'The establishment of the more specific necessitates the establishment of the more general,' and 'The whole is greater than the part,' and similar self-evident truths. The benefit of knowing the derivation: to refer back to it when intending to verify an issue of the art. His saying: (As for its derivation) — derivation is used in two senses: 1. It is meant to be the terminological principles of the science, as this commentator mentioned. 2. It may also mean taking, i.e., taking the science from another, like the derivation of the science of eloquence from the eloquent. But the first is more in accordance with the objectives of the masters of the scale.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Defining Tasawwur: The Foundation of Knowledge
Author defines tasawwur and distinguishes it from tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the definition of tasawwur as given in this passage and distinguish it from tasdiq.

Core Idea
Knowledge is divided into concept and assent; tasawwur is the unjudged perception of a meaning.

This passage opens the discussion of the two fundamental cognitive acts: tasawwur and tasdiq. The author first announces this division, then provides a precise definition of tasawwur that will guide our understanding of all subsequent logical operations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the division of knowledge
The matn states: 'Perception of a single expression: as a concept it is known, and perception of a relation is marked as assent.' Notice that knowledge is divided into two types: tasawwur (concept) and tasdiq (assent).
This division is foundational in Islamic logic.
2
Extract the definition of tasawwur
The commentator says: 'He interpreted concept as: it is perception of a single expression.' The Arabic is 'إدراك مفرد'. Write down this definition.
Tasawwur is defined by its object: a single expression (mufrad).
3
Understand the definition of 'mufrad'
The commentator further defines mufrad as 'what is other than the occurrence of the complete relation or its non-occurrence'. This means any cognition that does not involve a full judgment (affirmation or negation).
A proposition (qadhiyya) involves a relation; a mufrad does not.
4
Apply the definition to examples
The commentator gives the example: in 'The human is a writer', both 'human' and 'writer' are mufrad because they are perceived without the relation of being. The complete relation 'is a writer' is what makes it tasdiq.
Thus tasawwur includes both subject and predicate separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (۱۹) إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ: تَصَوُّراً عُلِمَ وَدَرْكُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسِمْ قَسَّم «العِلْمَ» المَذْكُورَ إِلَى : تَصَوُّرٍ، وَتَصْدِيقٍ .
وَفَسَّرَ النَّصُورَ بِـ : «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ»، وَالمُفْرَدُ (۳) : «مَا سِوَى وُقُوعِ النِّسْبَةِ التَّامَّةِ أَوْ لَا وُقُوعِهَا » :
- فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ : المَحْكُومُ عَلَيْهِ وَالمَحْكُومُ بِهِ كَـ الإِنْسَانِ، وَالكَاتِبِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : الإِنْسَانُ كَاتِبٌ».
His statement: (19) 'Perception of a single expression: as a concept it is known, and perception of a relation is marked as 'assent'' — he divided the mentioned knowledge into concept and assent. And he interpreted 'concept' as: 'it is perception of a single expression', and 'single expression' (3) is: 'what is other than the occurrence of the complete relation or its non-occurrence'. So it includes: the subject and predicate, such as 'human' and 'writer' in your statement: 'The human is a writer'.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defining 'tasawwur' (concept) as part of the division of knowledge into concept and assent. The matn (from al-Sullam) says: 'Perception of a single expression: as a concept it is known, and perception of a relation is marked as assent.' The commentator explains that the author of the matn divided knowledge into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). Then he interprets 'concept' as 'perception of a single expression'. He then defines 'single expression' (مفرد) as: 'what is other than the occurrence of the complete relation or its non-occurrence'. This means that a single expression is any cognition that does not involve a complete judgment (whether affirmative or negative). So it includes the subject and the predicate individually. For example, in the proposition 'The human is a writer', 'human' and 'writer' are each single concepts. The commentator clarifies that 'perception of a single expression' encompasses both the subject and predicate of a proposition, not just isolated words. This is important because it shows that tasawwur is not limited to simple terms but includes any mental grasp of a meaning without asserting a relation.

المفرد
التصديق

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur is the unjudged perception of a single meaning; it is the building block of all propositions.

What Counts as a Single Expression: The Definition of Mufrad
Commentator defines the term 'mufrad' used in the definition of tasawwur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the definition of mufrad to determine whether a given cognitive content is a concept or a proposition.

Core Idea
A mufrad is any cognition that does not involve a complete relation — even complex concepts like 'writer' are mufrad until judged.

The commentator provides a precise definition of mufrad (single expression) to clarify the scope of tasawwur. This definition is crucial because it tells us exactly which mental contents count as concepts and which are propositions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of mufrad
The passage states: 'المفرد: ما سوى وقوع النسبة التامة أو لا وقوعها' — 'the single expression is what is other than the occurrence of the complete relation or its non-occurrence.' Write this definition.
This definition is given in the commentary, not the matn.
2
Break down the definition
The definition excludes anything that involves a 'complete relation' (نسبة تامة). A complete relation is an affirmative or negative judgment, i.e., a proposition. So mufrad includes everything else: simple concepts (human), compound concepts (writer), and even questions or commands if not judged as true/false.
In logic, only propositions have truth value.
3
Test with examples
Consider 'human' (simple) and 'writer' (complex). Both are mufrad because you can think of them without affirming or denying anything. Now consider 'the human is a writer' — that involves a relation (is), so it is not mufrad.
The same word can be mufrad in one context and part of a proposition in another.
4
Recognize that complex concepts are still mufrad
The example 'writer' shows that mufrad is not limited to single words; it includes any meaningful unit that does not assert a relation. 'The writer of the book' is still a mufrad because it does not claim anything.
This corrects a common misunderstanding that mufrad equals 'simple term'.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
beginner

Definitions of Tasawwur and Tasdiq
Author defines tasawwur and tasdiq with extensive commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given mental act is a conception or an assent based on the presence or absence of judgment.

Core Idea
Conception grasps meaning; assent grasps truth.

In Islamic logic, knowledge is divided into two fundamental types: conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). This passage from the commentary on al-Bannani's logic defines these terms precisely, explaining that conception is the apprehension of a single object without any judgment, while assent is the apprehension of a relation with judgment. Understanding this distinction is the first step in mastering logical reasoning, as it underpins all subsequent analysis of definitions and arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Find where the author divides knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq. This is the starting point for the entire discussion.
2
Understand the definition of tasawwur
Tasawwur is defined as 'apprehension of a single object (mufrad)'. Grasp what mufrad means: anything that is not the occurrence or non-occurrence of a complete relation. This includes terms, incomplete relations, etc., as long as no judgment is made.
Examples include understanding 'human' as animality and rationality, or understanding the relation 'book of Zaid' without affirming or denying.
3
Understand the definition of tasdiq
Tasdiq is defined as 'apprehension of the relation (nisba) with judgment (hukm)'. This means knowing that a relation occurs or does not occur. The commentator clarifies that this includes belief (even conjecture) but excludes pure doubt or illusion.
The relation here is the judgmental relation that can be true or false.
4
Compare the two definitions
The key difference is the presence of judgment (hukm). In tasawwur, the relation may be understood but not judged; in tasdiq, a judgment is made. For example, a doubter who understands 'The world is created' but does not affirm or deny it is having a conception, not an assent.
The commentator stresses that even the judgmental relation, when considered without actual judgment, falls under tasawwur.
5
Apply to examples from the commentary
Use the examples given: the subject and predicate in 'Human is a writer' (conception), the relation in a construct like 'book of Zaid' (conception), a performative like 'Pray!' (conception), and the belief that 'The world is created' (assent).
Test yourself by identifying whether each example involves a judgment or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (۱۹) إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ: تَصَوُّراً عُلِمَ وَدَرْكُ نِسْبَةٍ بِـ «تَصْدِيقِ وُسْمِ
قَسَّم «العِلْمَ» المَذْكُورَ إِلَى : تَصَوُّرٍ، وَتَصْدِيقٍ .
وَفَسَّرَ النَّصُورَ بِـ : «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ»، وَالمُفْرَدُ : «مَا سِوَى وُقُوعِ النِّسْبَةِ التَّامَّةِ أَوْ لَا وُقُوعِهَا » :
- فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ : المَحْكُومُ عَلَيْهِ وَالمَحْكُومُ بِهِ كَـ الإِنْسَانِ، وَالكَاتِبِ فِي قَوْلِكَ : الإِنْسَانُ كَاتِبٌ.
معاً، وتارة الذات فقط كـ «ضارب»، فأطلق المعلوم هنا وأريد الشَّيء؛ إذ لفظ «المعلوم» يدلُّ على شيءٍ متّصف بالمعلوميَّة، فألغي ذلك الوصف العنوانيُّ الَّذي هو المعلوميَّة، ورُوعي الشَّيء فقط .
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ) أي: إدراك العقل المعنى المفرد ; أي: وصول النَّفس إلى المعنى بتمامه : كـ إدراك معنى الإنسان) وهي : الحَيَوَانيَّة والنَّاطقيَّة يسمَّى في الاصطلاح «تصوراً».
- وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ : النِّسْبَةُ الحُكْمِيَّةُ الَّتِي هِيَ مَوْرِدُ الإِيجَابِ وَالسَّلْبِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اعْتِبَارِ الحُكْمِ، كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاكُ .
- وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ أَيْضاً : النِّسْبَةُ النَّاقِصَةُ كَنِسْبَةِ المُضَافِ إِلَى المُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ، وَالنَّعْتِ إِلَى المَنْعُوتِ، وَالنِّسْبَةُ الإِنْشَائِيَّةُ وَالمَشْكُولُ فِيهَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ، وَغَيْرُ المَقْصُودَةِ كَنِسْبَةِ الجُمْلَةِ الوَاقِعَةِ صِلَةٌ أَوْ خَبَراً، فَإِدْرَاكُ كُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الأَشْيَاءِ تَصَوُّرٌ.
وَأَمَّا التَّصْدِيقُ فَفَسَّرَهُ بِـ : «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ»، وَأَرَادَ بِهَا : الحُكْمَ؛ لِيُطَابِقَ قَوْلَ جُمْهُورِ الحُكَمَاءِ : أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ هُوَ : إِدْرَاكُ وُقُوع النِّسْبَةِ أَوْ لَا وُقُوعِهَا»، وَهُوَ مُرَادِفٌ لِلْحُكْمِ ; أَي : العِلْمُ بِتُبُوتِ أَمْرٍ لِأَمْرِ أَوِ انْتِفَاءِ أَمْرٍ عَنْ أَمْرِ.
قوله : (كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاك) أي : يتصوّر المحكوم عليه والمحكوم به ومعنى النسبة، ويشكُ في وقوعها أو لا وقوعها ، فلو لم يتصور النِّسبة لم يمكنه أن يشكّ فيها هل هي واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؟ قوله : ( وَالنِّسْبَةُ الإِنْشَائِيَّةُ أي : لأنَّها لا تحتمل صدقاً ولا كذباً.
قوله : (وَالمَشْكُولُ فِيهَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ) تبع في هذا الهلالي، وفيه نظر; إذ هو مكرَّر مع قوله قبل : وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ النِّسْبَةُ الحُكْمِيَّةُ ... كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاك.
قوله : وَأَرَادَ بِهَا : الحُكْمَ) أي : فهو من باب استعمال اللفظ في غير ما وُضِعَ له وحمله على هذا التّجوز عدم وجدان قول بكون مسمى التصديق النسبة فقط .
قوله : (هُوَ : إِدْرَاكُ وُقُوع النِّسْبَةِ) معنى قولهم : إدراك وقوع النسبة... إلخ»; أي: العلم بوقوعها أو لا ; أي: اعتقاد أنَّها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة; سواء كان ذلك الاعتقاد جازماً أم لا، فيدخل : الظَّنُّ ، دون الشَّلِّ والوَهم; إذ لا اعتقاد فيهما . وهذا المعنى الَّذي فسَّر به التصديق هو معنى الحكم عند المناطقة، كما أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : «وهو مرادف للحكم ; أي: العلم بثبوت ... إلخ » هذا هو الحكم أيضاً عند المتكلمين . وحاصله : أنَّ التصديق مرادفٌ للحكم عند المناطقة، والحكم عند المناطقة يرادف الحكم عند المتكلمين، بل هو بعينه ، ثمَّ إِنَّ قولهم: وقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها» يُوهم - كما قال شيخنا سيدي الطَّيِّب - أن لا نسبة في السَّلب، وليس كذلك، ولكنَّهم أرادوا النِّسبة الثبوتية.
His saying: (19) 'Apprehension of a single [object] is known as conception, and perception of a relation is marked by 'assent'.' He divided the aforementioned knowledge into conception and assent. And he explained conception as: that it is the apprehension of a single [object]. And the single [object] is: whatever is other than the occurrence of complete relation or its non-occurrence. So it includes: the subject and predicate, like 'human' and 'writer' in your saying 'Human is a writer.' Both together, and sometimes the essence alone like 'hitter'. So he used the term 'known' here but intended the thing; because the word 'known' indicates a thing described by being-known, so he cancelled that attributive description which is being-known, and considered only the thing. His saying: (Apprehension of a single [object]) meaning: the intellect's apprehension of the single meaning; i.e., the soul's reaching the meaning in its completeness: like apprehension of the meaning of 'human' which is animality and rationality, called in terminology 'conception'. And it includes: the judgmental relation which is the locus of affirmation and negation without considering the judgment, as occurs from the doubter. And it also includes: the incomplete relation like the relation of the annexed to the annexer, and the adjective to the described, and the performative relation, and that about which there is equal doubt, and the unintended [relation] like the relation of the clause occurring as a link or as a predicate, so the apprehension of each of these things is conception. As for assent, he explained it as: that it is the apprehension of the relation, and he meant by it the judgment, to match the saying of the majority of philosophers: that assent is the apprehension of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence, and it is synonymous with judgment; i.e., knowledge of the establishment of a thing for a thing or the removal of a thing from a thing. His saying: (as occurs from the doubter) meaning: he conceives the subject and predicate and the meaning of the relation, and doubts its occurrence or non-occurrence; for if he did not conceive the relation, he could not doubt whether it occurs or not. His saying: (and the performative relation) meaning: because it does not admit truth or falsehood. His saying: (and that about which there is equal doubt) he followed al-Hilali in this, but there is consideration; because it is repeated with his saying before: 'and it includes the judgmental relation... as occurs from the doubter.' His saying: (and he meant by it the judgment) meaning: so it is a case of using the word for other than its original meaning, and his carrying it on this metaphorical usage is due to not finding a statement that the denotation of assent is only the relation. His saying: (it is the apprehension of the occurrence of the relation) the meaning of their saying 'apprehension of the occurrence of the relation... etc.' i.e., knowledge of its occurrence or not; i.e., belief that it occurs or does not occur; whether that belief is firm or not, so it includes conjecture, but not doubt and illusion, because there is no belief in them. And this meaning with which he explained assent is the meaning of judgment according to the logicians, as the commentator indicated by his saying: 'and it is synonymous with judgment; i.e., knowledge of the establishment... etc.' This is also judgment according to the theologians. The gist: that assent is synonymous with judgment according to the logicians, and judgment according to the logicians is synonymous with judgment according to the theologians, rather it is the same. Then their statement 'occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence' suggests - as our master al-Tayyib said - that there is no relation in negation, but it is not so, but they intended the positive relation.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage provides the definitions of the two types of knowledge: conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). Conception (tasawwur) is defined as the apprehension (idrak) of a single object (mufrad). The term 'mufrad' is defined negatively: it is whatever is not the occurrence or non-occurrence of a complete relation (nisba tamma). This includes the subject and predicate of a proposition (like 'human' and 'writer' in 'Human is a writer'), but also includes other types of relations: the judgmental relation considered without actual judgment (as when a doubter understands the proposition without affirming or denying), incomplete relations (like the construct 'book of Zaid'), performative relations (like commands, which have no truth value), and unintended relations (like relative clauses). The author also notes that the word 'known' in the original is used loosely to mean 'thing', disregarding the attribute of being known. For assent (tasdiq), it is defined as the apprehension of the relation (nisba) with the intention of judgment (hukm), matching the standard philosophical definition: apprehension of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence. This is synonymous with judgment, i.e., knowledge of the affirmation or negation of something. The commentator clarifies that this apprehension includes belief (i'tiqad), whether firm (like certainty) or not (like conjecture), but excludes doubt (shakk) and illusion (wahm) as they lack belief. He also notes that the term 'nisba' in the definition of assent is used metaphorically for judgment because the standard definition could not be found. Finally, he addresses an ambiguity: by 'occurrence or non-occurrence' they intend the positive relation (nisba thubutiyya) in both cases, not the absence of relation in negation.

Key Terms
التَّصَوُّر
التَّصْدِيق
المُفْرَد
النِّسْبَة
الحُكْمُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT included under the definition of tasawwur?
A) The apprehension of the subject and predicate in the proposition 'Human is a writer' without affirming it.
B) The apprehension of the relation 'book of Zaid' with understanding the possessive relationship.
C) The apprehension of the proposition 'The world is created' with the belief that it is true.
D) The apprehension of the command 'Pray!' understood as a performative utterance.

Key Takeaway
The foundation of all logical reasoning rests on the distinction between merely grasping meaning (tasawwur) and affirming or denying a proposition (tasdiq).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
