Defining Tasdiq: Majority vs. Imam al-Razi
Author defines tasdiq and contrasts the simple majority view with Razi's compound view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the majority definition of tasdiq from Imam al-Razi's compound definition and identify the four components in Razi's view.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is either simple perception or a compound of four perceptions—which view is more precise?

This lesson examines the foundational definition of tasdiq (assent), a core concept in Islamic logic. The passage presents two definitions: the majority view that tasdiq is the perception of the content of a proposition involving judgment, and Imam al-Razi's more analytical view that it is a compound of four distinct perceptions. Understanding this difference is crucial for later discussions on certainty, conjecture, and the structure of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined: it is 'tasdiq' (تصديق). The passage gives two definitions.
2
Extract the majority definition
The majority say tasdiq is the perception of the content of a proposition (including categorical and conditional) that involves a judgment (hukm), whether certain or not, corresponding to reality or not.
3
Extract Imam al-Razi's definition
Al-Razi says tasdiq is a collection of four perceptions: (1) perception of the subject, (2) perception of the predicate, (3) perception of the judgmental relation, (4) perception that the relation holds or not.
4
Compare the two definitions
The majority view is simpler: tasdiq is a single act of perceiving the proposition's content with judgment. Al-Razi breaks that act into four components, making tasdiq a compound.
5
Note key clarifications from the commentary
The commentator clarifies that 'connective or disjunctive' means conditional propositions, but the relation is the same as in categoricals. 'Or not' includes conjecture (zann) but not doubt or illusion, as those lack judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَوْ بِوُقُوعِ النِّسْبَةِ الاتِّصَالِيَّةِ وَالانْفِصَالِيَّةِ، فَإِدْرَاكُ مَضْمُونِ ذَلِكَ كُلُّهُ تَصْدِيقٌ؛ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ جَازِماً أَمْ لَا، مُطَابِقاً لِلْوَاقِعِ أَمْ لَا. وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ الرَّازِيِّ: التَّصْدِيقُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ مَجْمُوعِ أَرْبَعَةِ إِدْرَاكَاتٍ: إِدْرَاكِ المَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ، وَإِدْرَاكُ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ، وَإِدْرَاكِ النِّسْبَةِ الحُكْمِيَّةِ، وَإِدْرَاكِ أَنَّهَا وَاقِعَةٌ أَوْ لَيْسَتْ وَاقِعَةً. قوله: (الاتِّصَالِيَّةِ وَالِانْفِصَالِيَّةِ) على حذف موصوف؛ أي: في القضيَّة الاتصالية، أو في القضيَّة الانفصالية، لكن ليس فيه كبير فائدة؛ إذ النِّسبة لا تختلفُ ثبوتاً وانتفاء باعتبار الحمليّات والشَّرطيات. قوله: (أَمْ لَا) يدخل فيه - كما تقدَّم - الظَّنُّ فقط، دون الشَّلِّ والوهم؛ إذ لا حكم فيهما. قوله: (وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ الرَّازِيِّ) وهو الملقَّب بـ «الفخر»، وهو الإمام أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر بن الحسين البكري الطبرستاني الأصل الرَّازي المولد، المعروف بابن الخطيب.
Or by the occurrence of the connective or disjunctive relation, then the perception of the content of all that is assenting (tasdiq), whether it is certain or not, corresponding to reality or not. According to Imam al-Razi, tasdiq is an expression of a collection of four perceptions: perception of the subject of judgment, perception of the predicate of judgment, perception of the judgmental relation, and perception that it is or is not the case. He said: 'the connective and disjunctive' with an omitted described term; i.e., in the conditional conjunctive proposition or in the conditional disjunctive proposition, but there is no great benefit in that, since the relation does not differ in affirmation and negation with respect to categoricals and conditionals. He said: 'or not' includes in it – as previously – only conjecture, not doubt and illusion, since there is no judgment in them. He said: 'And according to Imam al-Razi' – he is laqabbed 'al-Fakhr', and he is Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar ibn al-Husayn al-Bakri al-Tabaristani by origin, al-Razi by birth, known as Ibn al-Khatib.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage defines tasdiq (assent) and presents two views. The majority define tasdiq as the perception of the content of a proposition (whether categorical or conditional) that involves a judgment, regardless of certainty or correspondence to reality. In contrast, Imam al-Razi defines tasdiq as a compound of four perceptions: the subject, the predicate, the judgmental relation, and the judgment of its truth or falsehood. The commentator then explains the matn: the phrase 'connective or disjunctive' refers to conditional propositions, but the distinction is not critical since the relation is the same. The phrase 'or not' includes only conjecture (zann), not doubt or illusion, because those lack judgment. He then identifies Imam al-Razi.

تصديق
حكم

D) Four

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is defined differently: the majority see it as a simple perception with judgment, while Imam al-Razi analyses it into four perceptions, highlighting its composite nature.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Tasdiq: Simple or Compound? The Methodological Argument
Author argues that the majority view of tasdiq as simple is preferable due to the distinct methods of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Sayyid al-Sharif preferred the majority view that tasdiq is simple, and identify the methodological basis for dividing knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
Tasdiq's uniqueness lies in its method: proof, not description.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary addresses a key dispute in mantiq: is tasdiq a simple act of judgment or composite of multiple perceptions? Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani argues that the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is based on the method (tariq) by which each is obtained. Since only the judgment part of tasdiq has a unique method (hujja), while the other supposed components share the method of tasawwur, there is no benefit in considering tasdiq compound. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to critically evaluate definitions in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the majority view (tasdiq is simple) and Imam al-Razi's view (compound of four parts: concepts of subject and predicate, relation, and judgment).
For the majority, the first three are conditions, not parts.
2
Focus on al-Sayyid's argument
Why does he favour the majority? Look for the key term 'tariq' (method). He argues that knowledge is divided because each type has a distinct method.
Al-Sayyid's argument is found in his glosses on Sharh al-Shamsiyya.
3
Trace the reasoning
Tasdiq's method is hujja (proof). Tasawwur's method is al-qawl al-sharih (descriptive statement). The three perceptions in al-Razi's compound tasdiq are obtained by the same method as tasawwur, not by hujja.
4
Apply the reasoning
Therefore, grouping those three perceptions with judgment under 'tasdiq' ignores the methodological distinction. There is no unique method for the entire compound.
5
Connect to the purpose of mantiq
The goal of mantiq is to elucidate the method leading to knowledge. The division must respect methodological uniqueness. This strengthens the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهُوَ عِنْدَ الجُمْهُورِ بَسِيطٌ، وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ مُرَكَّبٌ مِنْ أَرْبَعَةِ أَجْزَاءٍ، وَالإِدْرَاكَاتُ الثَّلَاثَةُ الأُولُ عِنْدَهُمْ: شُرُوطٌ لَهُ، وَعِنْدَهُ: أَجْزَاءٌ لَهُ. وَرَبَّحَ السَّيِّدُ مَذْهَبَ الجُمْهُورِ بِأَنَّ تَقْسِيمَ العِلْمِ إِلَى هَذَيْنِ القِسْمَيْنِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِامْتِيَازِ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا عَنِ الآخَرِ بِطَرِيقٍ يُسْتَحْصَلُ بِهِ، وَقَدِ اخْتُصَّ الإِدْرَاكُ المُسَمَّى بِالحُكْمِ بِطَرِيق وَاحِدٍ وَهُوَ الحُجَّةُ، وَمَا عَدَاهُ مِنْ سَائِرِ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ لَهُ طَرِيقٌ آخَرُ هُوَ القَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي ضَمِّ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِلَى الحُكْمِ مَعَ مُشَارَكَتِهَا لِسَائِرِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ فِي طَرِيقِهَا؛ إِذْ لَمْ يَجْعَلُوا لِهَذَا المَجْمُوعِ طَرِيقاً يَخُصُّهُ، فَمَنْ لَاحَظَ مَقْصُودَ هَذَا الفَنِّ وَهُوَ بَيَانُ الطَّرِيقِ المُوَصِّلِ إِلَى العِلْمِ لَمْ يَلْتَبِسْ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الوَاجِبَ فِي تَقْسِيمِهِ مُلَاحَظَةُ الامْتِيَازِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ. اهـ. قوله: (وَرَبَّحَ السَّيِّدُ) أي: في حواشي شرح الشَّمسيَّة للقطب الشيرازي. قوله: (إِذْ لَمْ يَجْعَلُوا لِهَذَا المَجْمُوعِ) أي: الَّذي هو التصديق والإدراكات الثلاث.
So it is, according to the majority, simple, and according to the Imam, composed of four parts, and the first three perceptions according to them are conditions for it, and according to him are parts of it. And al-Sayyid favored the doctrine of the majority because the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only to distinguish each from the other by a method by which it is obtained, and the perception called judgment (hukm) has been singled out by one method, which is the proof (hujja), and the rest of the other perceptions have another method, which is the descriptive statement (al-qawl al-sharih). So there is no benefit in joining the three perceptions to judgment while they share with the rest of the conceptions (tasawwurat) in their method, since they have not made for this totality a method particular to it. So whoever observes the purpose of this art – which is the elucidation of the method that leads to knowledge – will not be confused that the obligatory in its division is the observation of distinction in method. End. He said: 'And al-Sayyid favored' i.e., in his glosses on the Sharh al-Shamsiyya of Qutb al-Shirazi. He said: 'Since they have not made for this totality' i.e., which is tasdiq and the three perceptions.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage discusses the dispute over whether tasdiq is simple or compound. The majority consider it simple; Imam al-Razi considers it compounded of four perceptions. For the majority, the first three perceptions are conditions for tasdiq, not parts. Al-Sayyid al-Sharif favors the majority view. His reasoning: the division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq is based on the method (tariq) by which each type is obtained. Tasdiq (specifically the judgment component) has a unique method: proof (hujja). All other perceptions (including the three components of al-Razi's tasdiq) are obtained by the descriptive statement (al-qawl al-sharih), which is the method of tasawwur. Therefore, there is no benefit in grouping those three perceptions with judgment under one term because they share the method of tasawwur. The commentator clarifies that al-Sayyid's argument appears in his glosses on the Sharh al-Shamsiyya. The phrase 'this totality' refers to the combination of tasdiq and the three perceptions.

Key Terms
طريق
حجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Sayyid al-Sharif argue that the three perceptions (subject, predicate, relation) should not be considered parts of tasdiq?
A) Because they are too many to be included.
B) Because they are obtained by the same method as tasawwur (descriptive statement), not by proof.
C) Because Imam al-Razi did not include them.
D) Because the majority said so.

Key Takeaway
The division of knowledge into tasawwur and tasdiq must be based on a distinct method of acquisition; thus tasdiq is best considered simple because only judgment has a unique method.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition of 'ijtihad' in Usul al-Fiqh. Identify whether it is primarily a tasawwur (concept) or tasdiq (judgment). Then determine which method (descriptive statement or proof) would be appropriate to explain or prove it.
?
Explain why, according to al-Sayyid's reasoning, the act of 'prayer' (salat) should be classified as a tasawwur (concept) rather than a tasdiq, even though it involves multiple parts.

The Definitional Dispute over Hukm: Act or Passive State?
Author critiques the first definition of hukm as linguistically misleading.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two definitions of hukm and identify the linguistic fallacy that al-Ghazali warns against.

Core Idea
Hukm is not an act of the soul; language misleads us into thinking so.

This passage addresses a fundamental dispute in Islamic logic: What is the nature of judgment (hukm)? Two definitions are given: one defines it as an act of the soul, the other as a mental speech consequent upon knowledge. The author warns that the first definition arises from a dangerous linguistic fallacy, as al-Ghazali famously cautioned. By studying this critique, you will learn to distinguish between genuine logical analysis and mere verbal inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Find the two definitions of hukm in the Arabic. The first: 'It is an act of the soul additional to knowledge.' The second: 'It is a speech of the soul consequent upon knowledge.'
The second definition is said to be also an act, but the author questions this.
2
Understand why later scholars favored the first definition
Later scholars like al-Katibi inferred that hukm is an act because the verbs used to describe it (ascription, positing, abstraction) imply action. Note the linguistic reasoning.
This inference is based on verbal forms, not on the nature of hukm itself.
3
Apply al-Ghazali's critique
Al-Ghazali warns against seeking meanings from words, comparing it to facing west while looking for the sun. Reflect on why this is a logical error: the presence of action verbs does not prove the mental act is an action.
This is a classic fallacy of inferring ontology from language.
4
Evaluate the second definition and the passive state note
The author remarks that the second definition (mental speech) is more appropriate to being a passive state (infi‘al). Consider what this means for the nature of hukm.
This suggests that judgment may be a state that occurs to the soul, not something the soul actively does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي الحُكْمِ: فَقِيلَ: «هُوَ فِعْلٌ لِلنَّفْسِ زَائِدٌ عَلَى العِلْمِ». وَقِيلَ: «هُوَ حَدِيثُ النَّفْسِ التَّابِعُ لِلْعِلْمِ، وَهَذَا أَيْضاً فِعْلٌ»، فَلَا يُنَافِي الأَوَّلَ، وَقَدْ ذَكَرَ الإِمَامُ العِبَارَتَيْنِ. قوله: (فِعْلٌ لِلنَّفْسِ) أي: إيقاعها المحكوم به على المحكوم عليه، أو انتزاعها إيَّاه عنه. وَهَذَا القَوْلُ لِلْمُتَأَخِّرِينَ، وَمِنْهُمُ الكَاتِبِيُّ، تَوَهَّمُوا أَنَّ الحُكْمَ فِعْلٌ مِنْ جِهَةِ أَنَّ الأَلْفَاظَ الَّتِي يُعَبَّرُ بِهَا عَنْهُ كَالْإِسْنَادِ وَالْإِيقَاعِ وَالْإِنْتِزَاعِ وَالْإِيجَابِ وَالسَّلْبِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ، وَهُوَ غُرُورٌ، فَقَالَ الغَزَالِيُّ فِي المُسْتَصْفَى: «مَنْ طَلَبَ المَعَانِيَ مِنَ الأَلْفَاظِ ضَاعَ وَهَلَكَ، وَكَانَ كَمَنِ اسْتَدْبَرَ المَغْرِبَ وَهُوَ يَطْلُبُهُ». قوله: (وَهَذَا أَيْضاً فِعْلٌ) تَبِعَ فِي هَذَا الهِلَالِيُّ، وَفِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ فَإِنَّ هَذَا يُنَاسِبُ كَوْنَهُ انْفِعَالاً.
And know that there is disagreement regarding hukm (judgment). It is said: 'It is an act of the soul additional to knowledge.' And it is said: 'It is a speech of the soul consequent upon knowledge, and this also is an act,' so it does not contradict the first, and the Imam mentioned both expressions. He said: 'an act of the soul' i.e., its positing the predicate upon the subject, or its abstracting it from it. And this is the saying of the later scholars, among them al-Katibi; they imagined that judgment is an act because the words by which it is expressed, such as ascription, positing, abstraction, affirmation, and negation, indicate that. But it is delusion. For al-Ghazali said in al-Mustasfa: 'Whoever seeks meanings from words is lost and destroyed, and is like one who faces west while seeking the sun.' He said: 'and this also is an act' – al-Hilali followed him in this, and there is consideration in it; for this (the second definition) is more appropriate to being a passive state.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage addresses the nature of hukm (judgment). Two definitions are presented: (1) It is an act of the soul additional to knowledge (i.e., the soul actively posits or abstracts the predicate). (2) It is a mental speech consequent upon knowledge (which is also an act). The commentator notes that Imam (al-Razi?) mentioned both. He then critiques the first definition: later scholars like al-Katibi mistakenly inferred that hukm is an act because of the verbs used to describe it (e.g., ascribe, posit). Al-Ghazali warned that seeking meanings from mere words leads to error. The second definition (mental speech) is also claimed to be an act, but the commentator follows al-Hilali in considering it might instead be a passive state (infi'al). The passage ends mid-sentence but clearly favors critical refinement.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): Judgment: either an act of the soul beyond knowledge or a mental speech consequent upon knowledge. [Note: The debate on whether hukm is an act or a passive state continues in later hashiyas.]
فعل النفس (fi'l al-nafs): An act of the soul, such as positing or abstracting the predicate. [Note: Al-Ghazali criticizes inferring ontological status from linguistic expressions.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is the only reliable method.
B) It leads to loss and destruction.
C) It is praiseworthy.
D) It is acceptable for beginners.

Key Takeaway
Hukm is not an act of the soul but a mental speech consequent upon knowledge; inferring ontology from linguistic verbs is a delusion.

Priority of Tasawwur over Tasdiq: Positional and Natural
Author explains positional and natural priority of tasawwur over tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between positional and natural priority of conceptualization over assent, and explain why conceptualization is not a cause of assent using the doubter example.

Core Idea
Conceptualization is prior to assent in teaching and nature, but not causally.

In Islamic logic and epistemology, it is a foundational principle that conceptualization (tasawwur) is prior to assent (tasdiq). But what kind of priority? The commentator al-Bannani, building on al-Taftazani, distinguishes between positional priority — how we teach and write — and natural priority — how assent depends on prior concepts. However, he carefully clarifies that this dependence is not causal: having the concepts does not automatically produce assent, as the example of the doubter shows. In this lesson, we unpack this crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of priority
Locate the phrases 'al-taqdim bi-al-wad‘' (positional priority) and 'al-taqdim bi-al-tab‘' (natural priority) in the Arabic passage. Note that the commentator discusses each separately.
Positional priority concerns order in mention, writing, learning, and teaching.
2
Understand positional priority: teaching order
The author states that what leads to conceptualization (the definition) should come before what leads to assent (the proof). This is like beginning a lesson with definitions before arguments.
Example: In fiqh, defining 'riba' before proving its prohibition.
3
Understand natural priority: dependence without causation
Assent depends on three conceptualizations (subject, predicate, relational nexus). The dependence is not 'in terms of essence' but in some manner. Crucially, conceptualization is not a cause of assent, as shown by the doubter who has the concepts but does not assent.
The cause must always produce the effect, but concepts can exist without assent.
4
Apply the number one analogy
The author compares conceptualization to the number one, which exists without two. This illustrates that conceptualization can exist without assent, so it cannot be a cause.
A cause cannot exist without its effect; one exists without two, so one is not the cause of two.
5
Test with an Islamic example
Consider judging angels as honored servants. One must conceptualize 'angels', 'honored servants', and the relation. But conceptualizing these does not force the judgment—one could doubt. This shows natural priority without causality.
The example is taken directly from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال السعد : بدليل اتصافه هنا بأنه بديهي أو مكتسب . قوله : « وَقَدِّمِ الأَوَّلَ عِنْدَ الوَضْعِ لِأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّمُ بِال المُرَادُ بِـ تَقْدِيمِهِ عِنْدَ الوَضْعِ : بِاعْتِبَارِ الذِّكْرِ وَالكِتَابَةِ وَالتَّعَلُّمِ وَالتَّعْلِيمِ، وَكَذَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُقَدَّمَ مَا يُوَصِّلُ إِلَى التَّصَوُّرِ - وَهُوَ المُعَرِّفُ - عَلَى مَا يُوَصِّلُ إِلَى التَّصْدِيقِ - وَهُوَ الحُجَّةُ .. وَالمُرَادُ بِـ تَقْدِيمِهِ عَلَيْهِ بِالطَّبْعِ : كَوْنُ التَّصَوُّرِ يَحْتَاجُ إِلَيْهِ التَّصْدِيقُ ؛ لِامْتِنَاعِ الحُكْمِ بِدُونِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ ، لَكِنْ تَوَقُفُ التَّصْدِيقِ عَلَى التَّصَوُّرَاتِ لَيْسَ بِكُنْهِ الحَقِيقَةِ؛ أَيْ : بِالذَّاتِيَّاتِ، بَلْ يَكْفِي حُصُولُهَا بِوَجْهِ مَّا كَـ : الحُكْمِ عَلَى المَلَائِكَةِ مَثَلاً مَّا بِأَنَّهُمْ عِبَادٌ مُكْرَمُونَ. وقوله : (بِدَلِيلِ اتِّصَافِهِ) أي : هو إدراكاً؛ بدليل اتصافه بما ذكر ؛ إذ لو كان للنفس تأثير فيه لكان كلُّه مكتاً. وقوله : (وَقَدِّمِ الأَوَّلَ مراده : تقديم ما يفيد الأوَّل الذي هو التَّصور على ما يفيد التصديق؛ بدليل قول الشارح: «هُوَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الذِّكْرِ ... إلخ»؛ إذ الَّذي يذكر مفيد التصور لا نفسه. وقوله: (وَالتَّعَلُّمِ وَالتَّعْلِيمِ) الصَّوابُ: «عند التَّعلم والتعليم وغيرهما» ؛ لأنَّ التَّعلم والتعليم لا يخلوان عن ذكر وكتابة. وقوله : (وَالمُرَادُ بِـ تَقْدِيمِهِ عَلَيْهِ بِالطَّبْعِ : كَوْنُ ... إلخ) إِنَّما كان هذا هو المراد؛ لأنَّ التَّقديم الطَّبيعي هو أن يكون الشَّيء بحيث يحتاج إليه شيءٌ آخر، ولا يكون هو علَّةٌ للآخر، ولا شكّ أنَّ التَّصور بالنسبة للتصديق كذلك ؛ إذ ليس التَّصور علَّةٌ للتَّصديق ؛ إذ لا يلزمُ مِن وجود التصورات الثَّلاثة وجود التصديق كما في قضيَّة الشَّاكٌ، والتصديق يحتاج إلى التّصور . ونظير هذا : الواحد بالنسبة إلى الاثنين، فإنّه يوجد بدونهما ، والعلة لا توجد بدون المعلول. وقوله : ( بِوَجْهِ مَّا هو وإن كان كذلك، لكن لا بدَّ أن يتصور كلا من المحكوم عليه وبه والنسبة الحكميّة تصوراً بحسب ذلك التصديق، وعلى الوجه الذي يناسبه ويقتضيه، فإذا رأينا شبحاً من بعيد صح أن نحكم عليه بأنَّه شاغل فراغاً؛ لأنَّ هذه الصفة تثبت له بمجرد كونه جسماً من غير افتقار إلى شيء آخر، ولو أردنا أن نحكم عليه بالتَّحرُك لم نستطع حتَّى نتصوّر : أنَّه حَيَوَانٌ»، أو بالضحك لم نستطع حتَّى نتصوَّر: «أَنَّه إنسانُ».
Al-Sa'd said: By evidence of its being described here as intuitive or acquired. His statement: 'And give priority to the first in position because it is prior by...' What is meant by giving it priority in position is: in terms of mention, writing, learning, and teaching. Likewise, what leads to conceptualization – which is the definition – should be given priority over what leads to assent – which is the proof. What is meant by giving it priority over it by nature is: that conceptualization is needed by assent, because judgment is impossible without the three conceptualizations as previously mentioned. However, the dependence of assent on conceptualizations is not in terms of the essence of reality, i.e., by the essentials, rather it suffices that they be obtained in some manner, like the judgment about the angels, for example, that they are honored servants. And his statement: (By evidence of its being described) meaning: it is an apprehension; by evidence of its being described as mentioned; for if the soul had an effect in it, it would all be acquired. And his statement: (And give priority to the first) his meaning: giving priority to what benefits the first, which is conceptualization, over what benefits assent; by evidence of the commentator's statement: 'It is in terms of mention... etc.' since what is mentioned benefits conceptualization, not itself. And his statement: (learning and teaching) the correct [expression] is: 'during learning and teaching and other than them,' because learning and teaching are not free from mention and writing. And his statement: (And what is meant by giving it priority by nature: that...) is what is meant; because natural priority is that a thing is such that something else needs it, but it is not a cause for the other. There is no doubt that conceptualization in relation to assent is like that, since conceptualization is not a cause for assent, because the existence of the three conceptualizations does not necessitate the existence of assent, as in the case of the doubter, and assent needs conceptualization. An analogy for this is the one in relation to two, for it exists without them, while the cause does not exist without the effect. And his statement: (in some manner) – although it is so, it is necessary that each of the subject, predicate, and the relational nexus be conceptualized in accordance with that assent, and in the manner that suits and requires it. So if we see a form from afar, it is correct to judge it as occupying space, because this attribute is established for it simply by its being a body, without needing anything else. But if we wanted to judge it as moving, we could not until we conceptualize that it is an animal, or as laughing, we could not until we conceptualize that it is a human.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the priority of conceptualization (tasawwur) over assent (tasdiq). The author, al-Bannani, commenting on al-Sa'd (al-Taftazani), explains two types of priority. First, positional priority: in teaching and writing, the definition (which yields conceptualization) comes before the proof (which yields assent). Second, natural priority: assent depends on the prior conceptualization of the subject, predicate, and the relation between them. However, this dependence is not in terms of the essence (dhatiyyat) but only in terms of some manner of conceptualization, as illustrated by judging angels as honored servants. The author then clarifies that conceptualization is not a cause of assent, because one can have the concepts without assenting (e.g., a doubter). The analogy of the number one versus two shows that the cause must exist without the effect, but conceptualization exists without assent. Finally, the example of a distant form explains that to make a judgment like 'it moves', one needs to conceptualize 'animal', and for 'it laughs', one needs 'human'. This passage reinforces that while assent cannot occur without prior conceptualization, conceptualization alone does not guarantee assent.

Key Terms
التصور
التصديق
التقديم بالوضع
التقديم بالطبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Conceptualization is prior to assent in teaching (positional) and in dependence (natural), but it is not a cause of assent.

Defining Necessary and Theoretical Knowledge
Definition of necessary and theoretical knowledge with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any example of knowledge as necessary or theoretical in both conceptualization and assent, using the criteria from this passage.

Core Idea
Knowledge is divided by acquisition: some is attained without thought, some requires reflection.

In this passage, the author and commentator define the two fundamental categories of knowledge: necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari). This division is crucial in logic because it tells us which knowledge requires proof and which is self-evident. You will learn to apply this distinction to Islamic theological and legal examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Find the terms 'نظري' and 'ضروري' in the Arabic. Understand that they are categories of knowledge by method of acquisition.
2
Distinguish between tasawwur and tasdiq
Note that both types apply to conceptualizations and assents. Find examples for each in the passage.
3
Extract the defining condition for theoretical
The theoretical requires thought and reflection (فكر ونظر). Look for this condition in the passage.
4
Extract the defining condition for necessary
The necessary does not require thought after conceptualizing the subject and predicate. Identify this condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والنظري: ما احتاج للتأمل وعكسه هو الضروري) الجلي هذا تقسيم العلم بحسب طريقه الموصل إليه، وما قبله تقسيم له بحسب متعلقه. ويعني أن التصورات والتصديقات: منها ما هو نظري، وهو: "ما يحتاج في حصوله إلى فكر ونظر" كـ: "تصور معنى الروح والعقل" في التصورات، والحكم بأن العالم حادث، أو ليس بقديم في التصديقات. ومنها ما هو ضروري، وهو من التصورات: ما لا يحتاج إلى فكر ونظر: تصور معنى الحرارة والبرودة، ومن التصديقات: "ما لا يحتاج بعد تصور الطرفين إلى فكر ونظر، وسواء احتاج طرفاه إلى فكر أم لا كـ: الحكم بأن الإنسان مغاير للفرس، وأن الحلاوة مستلذة مثلا". ثم الضروري لا تحتاج النفس في حصوله لها إلى نظر كما مر، وقد تحتاج إلى حدس أو تجربة أو حس كما ستعرفه. قوله: (والنظري) قدم "النظري" على "الضروري"، وإن كان مقتضى الطبع عكسه؛ لكون قيوده وجودية، بخلاف الضروري، فإنها عدمية، والأعدام إنما تعرف بملكاتها؛ أي: بوجوداتها. وما درج عليه الناظم من تقسيم العلم الحادث إلى ضروري ونظري هو مذهب المحققين، وهو الأصح، وهناك أقوال أخر ضعيفة لا يلتفت لها.
His statement: (And the theoretical: that which requires reflection, and its opposite is the necessary). Al-Jaliyy: This is a division of knowledge according to the path leading to it, and what preceded it is a division according to its object. He means that conceptualizations and assents: among them are theoretical, and it is: 'that which requires in its acquisition thought and reflection' such as 'conceptualization of the meaning of spirit and intellect' in conceptualizations, and the judgment that the world is originated or not eternal in assents. And among them are necessary, and it is from conceptualizations: that which does not require thought and reflection: conceptualization of the meaning of heat and cold; and from assents: 'that which after conceptualizing the two extremes does not require thought and reflection, whether its extremes required thought or not' like 'the judgment that man is different from horse, and that sweetness is pleasurable' for example. Then the necessary: the soul does not need in its acquisition to [have] reflection as has passed, and it may need intuition or experience or sensation as you will know. His statement: (and the theoretical) he mentioned 'the theoretical' before 'the necessary', although the natural requirement is the opposite; because its conditions are existential, unlike the necessary, for its conditions are non-existential, and non-existences are only known through their positive counterparts; i.e., through their existences. What the poet followed in dividing contingent knowledge into necessary and theoretical is the doctrine of the verifiers, and it is the most correct, and there are other weak opinions that are not heeded.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the division of knowledge into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari) according to the method of acquisition. The author first states that the theoretical requires reflection (ta'amul) and the necessary is its opposite. The commentator explains that this division is by the path leading to knowledge, while a previous division was by the object of knowledge. He then clarifies that both tasawwurat and tasdiqat are divided into theoretical and necessary. For tasawwurat, the theoretical requires thought, like conceptualizing the meaning of spirit (ruh) and intellect (aql); for tasdiqat, it requires thought, like judging that the world is originated (hadith) or not eternal. The necessary does not require thought after conceptualizing the subject and predicate, like the judgment that man is different from horse. The commentator notes that the necessary may still require intuition (hads), experience (tajriba), or sensation (hiss), which will be explained later. Then he explains why the theoretical is mentioned first: because its conditions are positive (wujudiyya), while the necessary's conditions are negative ('adamiyya), and negatives are known through their positive counterparts. This division is the correct doctrine according to the verifiers.

Key Terms
نظري (nazari): What requires thought and reflection for its acquisition, whether in conceptualization or assent. [Note: Stable across the tradition.]
ضروري (daruri): What does not require thought and reflection after conceptualizing the subject and predicate (for assents) or without thought (for conceptualizations). [Note: Stable across the tradition.]
تصور (tasawwur): Simple apprehension or conceptualization of a meaning, without judgment. [Note: Standard definition.]
تصديق (tasdiq): Assent or judgment, combining two concepts with affirmation or negation. [Note: Standard definition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a necessary (daruri) conceptualization?
A) Conceptualization of spirit
B) Conceptualization of heat and cold
C) Judgment that the world is originated
D) Judgment that man is different from horse

Key Takeaway
The division of knowledge into necessary and theoretical depends on whether reflection is required for its acquisition.

The Order of Mention: Why Theoretical Precedes
Explanation of the order of mention of theoretical before necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the theoretical is mentioned before the necessary, and apply the principle that negatives are known through positives.

Core Idea
The theoretical is mentioned first because its conditions are positive, and we know the necessary through its opposite.

The author of the matn mentions theoretical knowledge before necessary knowledge, which seems counterintuitive. The commentator explains the wisdom: theoretical knowledge has positive conditions, while necessary knowledge is defined by the absence of those conditions. Since we understand absences only through their positive counterparts, the theoretical logically precedes.

Guided Path
1
Notice the order of mention
In the Arabic, the author says 'والنظري' (and the theoretical) before explaining the necessary. Why is the order reversed from what might be expected?
2
Identify the rationale given
The commentator explains that it is because theoretical's conditions are existential (وجودية) while necessary's are non-existential (عدمية).
3
Understand the epistemological principle
The principle is: 'Non-existences are known through their positive counterparts' (الأعدام إنما تعرف بملكاتها).
4
Evaluate the logical priority
This justifies mentioning theoretical first because it provides the basis for knowing the necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والنظري: ما احتاج للتأمل وعكسه هو الضروري) الجلي هذا تقسيم العلم بحسب طريقه الموصل إليه، وما قبله تقسيم له بحسب متعلقه. ويعني أن التصورات والتصديقات: منها ما هو نظري، وهو: "ما يحتاج في حصوله إلى فكر ونظر" كـ: "تصور معنى الروح والعقل" في التصورات، والحكم بأن العالم حادث، أو ليس بقديم في التصديقات. ومنها ما هو ضروري، وهو من التصورات: ما لا يحتاج إلى فكر ونظر: تصور معنى الحرارة والبرودة، ومن التصديقات: "ما لا يحتاج بعد تصور الطرفين إلى فكر ونظر، وسواء احتاج طرفاه إلى فكر أم لا كـ: الحكم بأن الإنسان مغاير للفرس، وأن الحلاوة مستلذة مثلا". ثم الضروري لا تحتاج النفس في حصوله لها إلى نظر كما مر، وقد تحتاج إلى حدس أو تجربة أو حس كما ستعرفه. قوله: (والنظري) قدم "النظري" على "الضروري"، وإن كان مقتضى الطبع عكسه؛ لكون قيوده وجودية، بخلاف الضروري، فإنها عدمية، والأعدام إنما تعرف بملكاتها؛ أي: بوجوداتها. وما درج عليه الناظم من تقسيم العلم الحادث إلى ضروري ونظري هو مذهب المحققين، وهو الأصح، وهناك أقوال أخر ضعيفة لا يلتفت لها.
His statement: (And the theoretical: that which requires reflection, and its opposite is the necessary). Al-Jaliyy: This is a division of knowledge according to the path leading to it, and what preceded it is a division according to its object. He means that conceptualizations and assents: among them are theoretical, and it is: 'that which requires in its acquisition thought and reflection' such as 'conceptualization of the meaning of spirit and intellect' in conceptualizations, and the judgment that the world is originated or not eternal in assents. And among them are necessary, and it is from conceptualizations: that which does not require thought and reflection: conceptualization of the meaning of heat and cold; and from assents: 'that which after conceptualizing the two extremes does not require thought and reflection, whether its extremes required thought or not' like 'the judgment that man is different from horse, and that sweetness is pleasurable' for example. Then the necessary: the soul does not need in its acquisition to [have] reflection as has passed, and it may need intuition or experience or sensation as you will know. His statement: (and the theoretical) he mentioned 'the theoretical' before 'the necessary', although the natural requirement is the opposite; because its conditions are existential, unlike the necessary, for its conditions are non-existential, and non-existences are only known through their positive counterparts; i.e., through their existences. What the poet followed in dividing contingent knowledge into necessary and theoretical is the doctrine of the verifiers, and it is the most correct, and there are other weak opinions that are not heeded.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage defines the division of knowledge into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari) according to the method of acquisition. The author first states that the theoretical requires reflection (ta'amul) and the necessary is its opposite. The commentator explains that this division is by the path leading to knowledge, while a previous division was by the object of knowledge. He then clarifies that both tasawwurat and tasdiqat are divided into theoretical and necessary. For tasawwurat, the theoretical requires thought, like conceptualizing the meaning of spirit (ruh) and intellect (aql); for tasdiqat, it requires thought, like judging that the world is originated (hadith) or not eternal. The necessary does not require thought after conceptualizing the subject and predicate, like the judgment that man is different from horse. The commentator notes that the necessary may still require intuition (hads), experience (tajriba), or sensation (hiss), which will be explained later. Then he explains why the theoretical is mentioned first: because its conditions are positive (wujudiyya), while the necessary's conditions are negative ('adamiyya), and negatives are known through their positive counterparts. This division is the correct doctrine according to the verifiers.

Key Terms
نظري (nazari): What requires thought and reflection for its acquisition. [Note: Stable.]
ضروري (daruri): What does not require thought and reflection. [Note: Stable.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the necessary is more important
B) Because theoretical knowledge is more common
C) Because the theoretical's conditions are existential and necessary's are non-existential
D) Because the poet made a mistake

Key Takeaway
The order of mention in definitions follows epistemic priority: positive conditions are defined before negative ones.

Necessary Knowledge: Types and Means of Acquisition
Author classifies necessary knowledge and its means of acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between necessary conceptual and necessary assumptive knowledge, and identify whether a given necessary item is acquired through intuition, experience, or sense.

Core Idea
Necessary knowledge requires no reflection, but still relies on intuition, experience, or the senses.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies what makes knowledge 'necessary' (daruri). It divides necessary knowledge into concepts (tasawwur) and assents (tasdiq), and explains that while such knowledge does not require systematic reflection (nazar), it may still depend on other cognitive means: intuition (hads), experience (tajriba), or sense perception (hiss). Understanding this classification helps you see why some truths are known immediately while others require a flash of insight or repeated observation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of necessary knowledge
Note that the author splits necessary knowledge into conceptual (tasawwuri) and assumptive (tasdiqi). The criterion for both is the lack of need for reflection (fikr wa nazar).
2
Examine the examples for each type
Conceptual: the idea of heat or cold. Assumptive: the judgment that man is not horse, or that sweetness is pleasurable. These are known immediately once the terms are understood.
3
Distinguish the three means of acquisition
The author lists intuition (hads), experience (tajriba), and sense (hiss). Although the soul does not need reflection, it may need one of these to obtain the knowledge.
4
Understand the definition of intuition (hads)
Intuition is defined as 'obtaining the middle terms at once' when turning to an objective. The example is knowing that the moon's light comes from the sun—a sudden grasp without ordered reasoning.
5
Differentiate intuition from reflection, experience, and sense
Reflection involves ordered reasoning from minor to major; intuition is instantaneous. Experience requires repeated observation (e.g., fire burns). Sense is direct perception via the five senses (e.g., fire is hot).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا مَا هُوَ ضَرُورِيٌّ ، وَهُوَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ : مَا لَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى فِكْرٍ وَنَظَرٍ : تَصَوُّرِ مَعْنَى الحَرَارَةِ وَالبُرُودَةِ، وَمِنَ التَّصْدِيقَاتِ: مَا لَا يَحْتَاجُ بَعْدَ تَصَوُّرِ الطَّرَفَيْنِ إِلَى فِكْرٍ وَنَظَرٍ، وَسَوَاءٌ احْتَاجَ طَرَفَاهُ إِلَى فِكْرٍ أَمْ لَا كَـ: الحُكْمِ بِأَنَّ الإِنْسَانَ مُغَايرٌ لِلْفَرَسِ، وَأَنَّ الحَلَاوَةَ مُسْتَلَذَّةٌ مَثَلاً. ثُمَّ الضَّرُورِيُّ لَا تَحْتَاجُ النَّفْسُ فِي حُصُولِهِ لَهَا إِلَى نَظَرٍ كَمَا مَرَّ، وَقَدْ تَحْتَاجُ إِلَى حَدَسٍ أَوْ تَجْرِبَةٍ أَوْ حِسٌ كَمَا سَتَعْرِفُهُ. بقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلِ الرُّوحُ مِنْ أَمْرِ رَبِّي ﴾ [الإسراء: ۸۵] ، وفي جمع الجوامع»: «حقيقة الرُّوح لم يتكلم فيها رسول الله ، فنمسك عنها (۲) . ٢ - وفرقة خاضت فيها ، وتأوَّلوا الآية بأنَّ اليهود قالوا : إن أجاب عنها فليس بنبي، وإن لم يجب فنبي، فلم يأذن الله تعالى له في الجواب تأكيداً لمعجزته ، لا لعدم إمكان الكلام فيه . ثم اختلف هؤلاء في حقيقته على أقوال كثيرة، قال الشيخ زروق في «شرح الرسالة»: يحكى أنَّ في مسألة الرُّوح سبع مئة ،قول والمحتمل من ذلك لأهل السُّنَّة ثلاثة أقوال؛ أحسنها وهو قول المحققين كإمام الحرمين ونقل عن الأشعري: أنَّ الرُّوح جسم نوراني لطيف سار في البدن كسريان النار في الفحم، والماء في العود الأخضر، أجرى الله تعالى العادة باستمرار حياة الأجسام ما استمرَّت مُشابِكَةٌ لها». ثم قوله : (إِلَى حَدَسٍ أَوْ تَجْرِبَةٍ أَوْ حِسٌ) الحدس : «التَّخمين»، وسيأتي أنَّ التحقيق: «أَنَّه عبارةٌ الظَّفَر عند الالتفات إلى المطالب بالحدود الوسطى دفعة واحدة». ومثال ذلك : الحكم على نور القمر بكونه مستفاداً من نور الشَّمس، فالانتقال في الحدس دفعي ؛ لأنَّه من الحد الوسط إلى المطلوب، وليس فيه ترتيب فى الدليل، بخلاف النظر، ففيه انتقال مِنَ الصُّغرى إلى الكبرى، فمهما احتاج إدراكك إلى ترتيب في الدليل فهو نظر، وإلا فهو حدس؛ كما ننظر إلى اختلاف تشكلات نور القمر بحسب اختلاف أوضاعه مِنَ الشَّمس قُرباً وبعداً؛ لأنَّه كلَّما قرب مِنَ الشَّمس قل نوره، وكلَّما بَعُد منها كَثُر نوره فتصل إلى المطلوب من غير احتياج ترتيب . ومثال ما احتاج إلى التّجربة : الحكم على النَّار بأنَّها محرقة. ومثال الحسّ : الحكم بأنَّ النَّار حارةٌ، ويشمل الحسُّ الحواس الخمس، وهي المشاعر، ومنه قول الشاعر : وَالرَّأسُ مُرْتَفِعٌ فِيهِ مَشَاعِرُهُ تَهْدِي السَّبِيلَ لَهُ سَمْعَ وَعَيْنَانِ.
Among them is what is necessary, and it is from conceptualizations: what does not need thought and reflection: conceptualization of the meaning of heat and cold. And from assents: what does not need, after conceptualization of the two extremes, thought and reflection, whether its two extremes need thought or not, like the judgment that man is different from horse, and that sweetness is pleasurable, for example. Then the necessary: the soul does not need for its acquisition reflection as previously mentioned, and it may need intuition or experience or sense as you will know. By His saying the Exalted: 'Say: The soul is from the command of my Lord' [al-Isra 85], and in Jam' al-Jawami': 'The reality of the soul the Messenger of God did not speak about, so we refrain from it.' And a group delved into it, and interpreted the verse that the Jews said: If he answers it, he is not a prophet, and if he does not answer, he is a prophet. So God the Exalted did not permit him to answer to strengthen his miracle, not because it is impossible to speak about it. Then these differed about its reality in many opinions. Sheikh Zaruq said in Sharh al-Risala: It is narrated that there are seven hundred opinions on the matter of the soul. What is probable from that for the People of the Sunnah are three opinions: the best of which is the saying of the verifiers like Imam al-Haramayn and transmitted from al-Ash'ari: that the soul is a subtle luminous body flowing in the body like the flow of fire in coal and water in green wood; God the Exalted made it customary for the life of bodies to continue as long as they are interwoven with it. Then his saying: (to intuition or experience or sense): Intuition is 'conjecture', and it will come that the verification is 'that it is an expression for obtaining the middle terms at once when turning to the objectives.' An example of that is the judgment that the light of the moon is derived from the light of the sun. So the transition in intuition is instantaneous because it is from the middle term to the objective, and there is no order in the proof, unlike reflection, for in it there is transition from the minor premise to the major premise. So whenever your perception needs order in the proof it is reflection, otherwise it is intuition; as we look at the variation of the phases of the moon's light according to its different positions relative to the sun in proximity and distance; because the closer it is to the sun the less its light, and the farther from it the more its light, so you reach the objective without needing order. An example of what needs experience: the judgment that fire burns. An example of sense: the judgment that fire is hot, and sense includes the five senses, which are the faculties, and from it is the saying of the poet: 'And the head is elevated, in it are his faculties guiding the way for him: hearing and two eyes.'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage defines necessary knowledge (daruri) and its two types: conceptual (tasawwuri) and assensual (tasdiqi). The author gives examples: conceptualization of heat and cold does not require thought; the judgment that man is not horse or that sweetness is pleasant are assents that are self-evident after understanding the terms. Then he notes that necessary knowledge does not require reflection (nazar) but may require intuition (hads), experience (tajriba), or sense (hiss). He then inserts a long digression about the soul, citing Quran and scholars, arguing that its reality is not known by necessary means but by revelation. He then returns to explain intuition: it is a sudden grasp of the middle term without ordered reasoning, exemplified by knowing the moon's light comes from the sun. He distinguishes intuition from reflection: reflection involves ordered steps from minor to major. He then gives examples for experience (fire burns) and sense (fire is hot), noting sense includes the five senses.

تصور
تصديق
حدس
تجربة

Necessary knowledge can be either a simple concept or an immediate judgment; it never requires systematic proof, but may be triggered by intuition, repeated experience, or direct sensation.

Qawl Sharh and Hujja: The Two Direct Means to Knowledge
Author defines the two types of logical premises: qawl sharh for concepts and hujja for assent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qawl sharh and hujja as the two direct means to attain tasawwur and tasdiq, and identify their respective subcategories.

Core Idea
Knowledge is attained via two direct routes: definition (qawl sharh) for concepts, and proof (hujja) for assent.

This passage from al-Bannani's commentary on the logic text lays the foundation for all logical reasoning by distinguishing the two tools that directly lead to knowledge: clarifying statements for concepts and proofs for assent. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing how to properly define terms and construct arguments in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of unknown knowledge
The passage distinguishes between unknown concept (tasawwur) and unknown assent (tasdiq). Each has a direct means: qawl sharh for the former, hujja for the latter. Mark these in the Arabic.
The verse: 'وَمَا بِهِ إِلَى تَصَوُّرٍ وُصِلْ يُدْعَى بِـ: «قَوْلِ شَارِحٍ' and 'وَمَا لِتَصْدِيقِ بِهِ تُوُصِّلَا بِـ: «حُجَّةٍ'.
2
Define qawl sharh and its subtypes
The commentary explains that qawl sharh includes complete definition (hadd tamm), incomplete definition, complete description (rasm tamm), and incomplete description. Write these four and note that they directly give the concept.
The author specifies 'mubasharatan' meaning directly, excluding indirect means like the universal alone.
3
Define hujja and its subtypes
The commentary says hujja includes demonstration (burhan), dialectic (jadal), rhetoric (khataba), poetry (shi'r), and sophistry (safsata). These all directly lead to assent. The term hujja indicates overcoming the opponent.
Hujja is also called 'qiyas' (syllogism) in a broad sense.
4
Understand the qualifier 'directly' for both
For both tools, the passage stresses they lead directly without intermediary. For qawl sharh, it excludes the universal by itself; for hujja, it excludes the proposition by itself. Discuss why these indirect forms do not suffice.
The directness is essential: the tools themselves are sufficient to produce the knowledge.
5
Apply the distinction
Given an example from fiqh, determine whether it is a qawl sharh (definition) or a hujja (argument). For instance, 'Wine is an intoxicating liquid' is a definition; 'Wine is forbidden because it is intoxicating' is an argument.
Practice with examples from Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَمَا بِهِ إِلَى تَصَوُّرٍ وُصِلْ يُدْعَى بِـ: «قَوْلِ شَارِحٍ فَلْتَبْتَهِلْ (۲۳) وَمَا لِتَصْدِيقِ بِهِ تُوُصِّلَا بِـ: «حُجَّةٍ يُعْرَفُ عِنْدَ العُقَلَا يَعْنِي : أَنَّ المَعْلُومَ الَّذِي يُلاحَظُ لِلتَّوَصُّلِ بِهِ إِلَى مَا جُهِلَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرِ مُبَاشَرَةٌ يُسَمَّى : قَوْلاً شَارِحاً، كَمَا يُسَمَّى : مُعَرِّفاً - بِالكَسْرِ ، وَالَّذِي يُلاحَظُ لِلتَّوَصُّلِ بِهِ إِلَى مَا جُهِلَ مِنَ التَّصْدِيقِ مُبَاشَرَةٌ يُسَمَّى : «حُجَّةً) وَ: «قياساً". قوله : (مُبَاشَرَةٌ) أي : مِن حدّ تام أو ناقص، أو رسم تام، أو ناقص. واحترز به عن : الموصل بواسطة كالكلِّي مِن حيث إنَّه كلّيّ، أو مِن حيث إنَّه جنس أو فصل أو خاصَّةٌ؛ لتوقف ذلك على التّركيب والنسبة إلى المعرف. قوله : (يُسَمَّى قَوْلاً شَارِحاً يعني في الاصطلاح؛ لأنَّه يشرح الماهية ويميزها عما يشاركها : : في الجنسية. قوله : (مُبَاشَرَةٌ) أي : من برهان أو جدل أو خطابة، أو شعر، أو سفسطة. احترز به عن القضيَّة من حيث إنَّها قضيَّةٌ، ونحو ذلك . قوله : (يُسَمَّى : «حُجَّةٌ)) أي : لأنَّ مَن تمسَّك به يحج خصمه؛ أي: يغلبه .
His saying: 'And that by which to a concept one arrives is called "a clarifying statement", then you should strive. And that for assent by which one arrives is called "a proof", known among the rational.' He means: the known thing which is observed for arriving by it to what was unknown of concept directly is called 'a clarifying statement', just as it is called 'a definer' (with kasr of the ra). And what is observed for arriving by it to what was unknown of assent directly is called 'a proof' and 'a syllogism'. His saying 'directly' means: from a complete definition, or incomplete, or a complete description, or incomplete. And he excluded by it the intermediary such as the universal inasmuch as it is universal, or inasmuch as it is genus or differentia or property, because that depends on composition and relation to the definiendum. His saying 'it is called a clarifying statement' means in terminology, because it explains the essence and distinguishes it from what shares with it in genus. His saying 'directly' means: from a demonstration, or dialectic, or rhetoric, or poetry, or sophistry. He excluded by it the proposition inasmuch as it is a proposition and the like. His saying 'it is called a proof' means: because whoever adheres to it overcomes his opponent, i.e., defeats him.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage clarifies the two fundamental tools of logic: the 'qawl sharh' (clarifying statement) for attaining concept (tasawwur) and the 'hujja' (proof) for attaining assent (tasdiq). The verse from the matn presents the distinction, and the sharh expands on it. The author explains that 'directly' means these tools lead to knowledge immediately, without intermediary, and they are subdivided into complete or incomplete definitions and descriptions for concepts, and into the five arts (demonstration, dialectic, rhetoric, poetry, sophistry) for proofs. He also excludes indirect means like the universal itself without composition. Finally, he justifies the term 'hujja' as that which defeats the opponent in debate, emphasizing its dialectical function.

Key Terms

Key Takeaway
The logical path to knowledge splits into two: qawl sharh (definition/description) for concepts and hujja (proof) for assent, each with distinct subcategories.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
10 min
Definition of Dalala and Reconciliation of Views
Definition of dalala and resolution of a theological objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the earlier and later logicians' definitions of dalala are actually the same, and analyze the theological objection regarding the eternity of Allah's speech using the distinction between a real attribute and an accidental relation.

Core Idea
Dalala is a relation, not an act of understanding, reconciling definitions.

This passage dives into the definition of dalala (indication), a foundational concept in Islamic logic. You will see how the later logicians defined it as a relation (haythiyya), and how the earlier definition as understanding (fahm) actually points to the same idea. We'll also tackle a key theological objection: if dalala were an act of understanding, then Allah's eternal speech would have a temporally originated attribute, which is impossible. The answer lies in distinguishing real attributes from accidental relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Find the definitions of dalala given by the earlier logicians (al-aqdamun) and the later logicians (al-muta'akhkhirun). Earlier: 'fahm' (understanding). Later: 'al-haythiyya' (being such that from one thing another is known).
2
Examine the supposed contradiction
The objection states that if dalala is fahm, then Allah's speech (qadim) would have a hadith (temporally originated) dalala because there was no human understander in pre-eternity. This would make the speech itself hadith, which is false.
Notice the implicit syllogism: if dalala is fahm, then its existence depends on a fahim; in azal, no fahim; so dalala is hadith; if dalala is an attribute, its haduth implies haduth of the subject.
3
Understand the reconciliation
The author argues that the earlier logicians meant by 'fahm' the property of the word that meaning is understood from it, not the act itself. The later logicians, with 'haythiyya', meant the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding. Both are the same: a relation of the sign to being such that it yields knowledge.
This is not a real disagreement but a verbal one.
4
Analyze the response to the objection
The response distinguishes real attributes (sifa haqiqiyya) from accidental relations (nisba 'arida). Dalala is a relation, not a real attribute. A relation can be temporally originated without its subject being originated, like the specific attachment (ta'alluq tanjizi) of God's power (qadim) to a particular act (hadith).
The hashia adds that the attachment of speech to its meanings is eternal (nafsi), so the analogy is only partial.
5
Apply the distinction
The key is to note that dalala itself need not be hadith; the objection assumes it is an attribute inhering in the speech. But as a relation, it can be eternal if the terms (sign and meaning) are eternal. Thus, Allah's speech eternally indicates all things.
The proof: if dalala is eternal, no haduth of speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَذَهَبَ المُتَأخّرُونَ إِلَى أَنَّ الدَّلَالَةَ هِيَ الحَيثِيَّةُ؛ أَيْ: كَوْنُ أَمْرٍ بِحَيْثُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يُفْهَمَ مِنْهُ أَمْرٌ آخَرُ؛ سَوَاءٌ فُهِمَ أَوْ لَمْ يُفْهَمْ، وَبِعِبَارَةٍ أُخْرَى: كَوْنُ أَمْرٍ بِحَيْثُ يَلْزَمُ مِنَ العِلْمِ بِهِ العِلْمُ بِأَمْرٍ آخَرَ، وَعَلَيْهِ: يَكُونُ وَصْفُ الدَّالِّ بِالدَّلَالَةِ قَبْلَ الفَهْمِ حَقِيقَةً. فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: يَلْزَمُ عَلَى مَذْهَبِ الأَقْدَمِينَ حُدُوثُ دَلَالَةِ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى القَدِيمِ؛ لِعَدَمِ الفَاهِمِ فِي الأَزَلِ، وَيَلْزَمُ مِنْ حُدُوثِهَا حُدُوثُ مَوْصُوفِهَا، وَذَلِكَ بَاطِلٌ. قَالَ المُحَشِّي: قَوْلُهُ: (سَوَاءٌ فُهِمَ أَوْ لَمْ يُفْهَمْ) هَذِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ وَقَعَتْ لِلشَّيْخِ السَّنُوسِيِّ، وَتَبِعَهُ عَلَيْهَا جَمْعٌ، وَلَيْسَتْ فِي كَلَامِ المُتَأَخِّرِينَ، فَهَذِهِ زِيَادَةٌ مِنْ عِنْدِهِ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى فَهْمِهِ—كَجَمَاعَةٍ—الخِلَافَ بَيْنَ الفَرِيقَيْنِ. وَالحَقُّ: أَنَّهُ لَا خِلَافَ بَيْنَهُمَا، فَالمُتَأَخِّرُونَ قَائِلُونَ بِأَنَّ الدَّالَّ لَا يُوصَفُ بِالدَّلَالَةِ حَقِيقَةً إِلَّا بَعْدَ الفَهْمِ، وَلَمْ يُرِيدُوا بِالحَيْثِيَّةِ مُجَرَّدَ المُصَاحَبَةِ لِلْفَهْمِ، وَإِنَّمَا أَرَادُوا: أَنَّ الدَّلَالَةَ هِيَ كَوْنُ اللَّفْظِ مَحَلًّا لِتَعَلُّقِ الفَهْمِ بِهِ. وَحَاصِلُهُ: أَنَّ الأَقْدَمِينَ وَإِنْ عَرَّفُوا الدَّلَالَةَ بِالفَهْمِ، فَمُرَادُهُمْ: مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مِمَّا هُوَ صِفَةٌ لِلَّفْظِ؛ أَعْنِي: كَوْنُهُ بِحَيْثُ يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ المَعْنَى، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ عَنِ السَّيِّدِ، وَالمُتَأَخِّرُونَ لَمْ يَقْصِدُوا بِقَوْلِهِمْ: "كَوْنُ أَمْرٍ بِحَيْثُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يُفْهَمَ... إِلَخْ" مُجَرَّدَ الصَّلَاحِيَّةِ لِلْفَهْمِ، بَلْ قَصَدُوا كَوْنَ اللَّفْظِ مَحَلًّا لِتَعَلُّقِ الفَهْمِ بِهِ، وَهَذَا هُوَ مَعْنَى كَلَامِ المُتَقَدِّمِينَ، فَرَجَعَ الخِلَافُ إِلَى وِفَاقٍ وَلَمْ يَبْقَ بَيْنَ الفَرِيقَيْنِ شِقَاقٌ. وَتَوَهَّمَ جَمَاعَةٌ الخِلَافَ مَبْنِيًّا عَلَى تَحْكِيمِ الأَلْفَاظِ، مَعَ الغَفْلَةِ عَنِ المُرَادِ، وَتَقَدَّمَ قَوْلُ الغَزَالِيِّ: "مَنْ طَلَبَ المَعَانِيَ... إِلَخْ". قَوْلُهُ: (وَبِعِبَارَةٍ أُخْرَى) أَشَارَ بِهَذَا لِرَفْعِ تَوَهُمِ مُبَايَنَةِ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفِ لِمَا قَبْلَهُ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَعَلَيْهِ: يَكُونُ) أَيْ: عَلَى مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ المُتَأَخِّرُونَ، وَهُوَ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى فَهْمِهِ مُخَالَفَةَ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفِ لِتَعْرِيفِ الأَقْدَمِينَ، وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ مَا فِيهِ. قَوْلُهُ: (فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: يَلْزَمُ) تَبِعَ فِي هَذَا السُّؤَالِ الهِلَالِيَّ، وَهُوَ مُعْتَرِضٌ مِنْ وُجُوهٍ: الأَوَّلُ: أَنَّهُ كَانَ مِنْ حَقِّهِ أَنْ لَوْ أَتَى بِهِ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ الاعْتِرَاضَاتِ وَيُجِيبَ عَنْهُ، لَكِنَّ الهِلَالِيَّ أَتَى بِهِ سُؤَالًا فَتَبِعَهُ. الثَّانِي: أَنَّهُ بَنَاهُ عَلَى الخِلَافِ بَيْنَ الأَقْدَمِينَ وَالمُتَأَخِّرِينَ، وَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ مَا فِيهِ. الثَّالِثُ: أَنَّهُ مَبْنِيٌّ أَيْضًا عَلَى أَنَّ الفَاهِمَ هُوَ المُخَاطَبُ، وَالتَّحْقِيقُ خِلَافُهُ كَمَا حَقَّقَهُ خَاتِمَةُ المُحَقِّقِينَ شَيْخُنَا سَيِّدِي الطَّيِّبُ، فَقَوْلُ هَذَا الشَّارِحِ: "لِعَدَمِ الفَاهِمِ" فِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّ الفَاهِمَ هُوَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى العَالِمُ بِمَدْلُولَاتِ كَلَامِهِ فِي أَزَلِهِ، وَلَيْسَ المُرَادُ بِالفَاهِمِ: المُخَاطَبَ؛ لِمَا يَلْزَمُ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ عَدَمِ دَلَالَةِ كَلَامِهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى جَمِيعِ مَعْلُومَاتِهِ حَتَّى فِيمَا لَا يَزَالُ؛ لِعَدَمِ الفَاهِمِ المُخَاطَبِ، كَيْفَ وَالعَقْلُ وَالنَّقْلُ مُطَبِّقَانِ عَلَى دَلَالَةِ الكَلَامِ عَلَى جَمِيعِ المَعْلُومَاتِ؛ أَيْ: تَعَلُّقِهَا بِهَا؟! وَمَعْنَى الفَهْمِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَيْهِ مَجَازٌ لَيْسَ مَقْصُودًا عَلَى حَقِيقَتِهِ، بَلِ المُرَادُ بِهِ عِلْمُ المَدْلُولِ مِنَ الدَّالِّ. لَا يُقَالُ: عِلْمُهُ تَعَالَى المَعْلُومَاتِ مِنَ الكَلَامِ الدَّالِّ عَلَيْهَا يَقْتَضِي حُدُوثَ عِلْمِهِ مَعَ أَنَّهُ قَدِيمٌ. لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ: إِذَا كَانَتِ الدَّلَالَةُ قَدِيمَةً فَلَا يَلْزَمُ ذَلِكَ، وَبِذَلِكَ يَتَعَيَّنُ أَنْ تَكُونَ "مِنْ" فِي قَوْلِهِمْ: "فَهْمُ أَمْرٍ مِنْ أَمْرٍ" ابْتِدَائِيَّةً، لَا تَعْلِيلِيَّةً. قَوْلُهُ: (وَذَلِكَ بَاطِلٌ) أَيْ: فَيَكُونَ قَوْلُ الأَقْدَمِينَ المُؤَدِّي إِلَى هَذَا المَحْذُورِ بَاطِلًا. قُلْتُ: أُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ الصِّفَةَ الَّتِي يَلْزَمُ مِنْ حُدُوثِهَا حُدُوثُ مَوْصُوفِهَا هِيَ الصِّفَةُ الحَقِيقِيَّةُ، وَالدَّلَالَةُ إِنَّمَا هِيَ مُجَرَّدُ نِسْبَةٍ عَارِضَةٍ لِلدَّالِّ، فَلَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ حُدُوثِهَا حُدُوثُهُ، كَمَا أَنَّ التَّعَلُّقَ التَّنْجِيزِيَّ لِلْقُدْرَةِ حَادِثٌ، وَهِيَ قَدِيمَةٌ بِلَا مَرْيَةٍ. قَوْلُهُ: (فَلَا يَلْزَمُ مِنْ حُدُوثِهَا حُدُوثُهُ) تَسْلِيمُ حُدُوثِ الدَّلَالَةِ بَاطِلٌ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَاهَا التَّعَلُّقُ؛ أَي: تَعَلُّقُ الكَلَامِ القَدِيمِ بِجَمِيعِ المَعْلُومَاتِ، وَهُوَ نَفْسِيٌّ، وَالنَّفْسِيُّ لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَلَا يَخْتَلِفُ، فَلَا يُمْكِنُ حُدُوثُهُ، وَسَيَأْتِي لِهَذَا الشَّارِحِ قَرِيبًا أَنَّ تَعَلُّقَ الكَلَامِ الَّذِي هُوَ الدَّلَالَةُ قَدِيمٌ كَالكَلَامِ، وَالتَّنْظِيرُ بِالتَّعَلُّقِ التَّنْجِيزِيِّ لَا يَصِحُّ لِحُدُوثِهِ وَقِدَمِ الدَّلَالَةِ.
The later logicians held that indication (dalala) is the consideration (haythiyya); i.e., a thing being such that it is valid for another thing to be understood from it, whether or not it is actually understood. In other words: a thing being such that from knowledge of it, knowledge of another thing necessarily follows. According to this, describing the sign as having indication before understanding is real (not metaphorical). So if you say: 'It necessarily follows, according to the school of the earlier logicians, that the indication of the speech of Allah—exalted is He—which is eternal, is temporally originated, due to the absence of an understander in pre-eternity, and it necessarily follows from its temporal origination the temporal origination of its described thing (i.e., the speech), and that is false.' The commentator said: His statement: '(whether understood or not understood)' this addition was made by Shaykh al-Sanusi, and a group followed him in it, but it is not in the words of the later logicians. So this is an addition from him, based on his understanding—like a group—of the disagreement between the two groups. The truth is that there is no disagreement between them. The later logicians are saying that the sign is not described with indication as a real description except after understanding, and they did not intend by 'haythiyya' mere accompaniment of understanding; rather they intended that indication is the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding to it. The summary: the earlier logicians, even though they defined indication by understanding, their intended meaning is 'what is understood from it' which is a description of the word; i.e., its being such that meaning is understood from it, as previously mentioned from al-Sayyid. The later logicians did not intend by their saying 'a thing being such that it is valid to be understood, etc.' mere suitability for understanding, but rather they intended the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding to it. And this is the meaning of the words of the earlier logicians. So the disagreement returns to agreement, and there remains no discord between the two groups. And a group's imagining of disagreement is based on making the wording decisive, while being heedless of the intended meaning. And the saying of al-Ghazali has preceded: 'Whoever seeks the meanings... etc.' His statement: '(and in another expression)' he indicated by this a removal of the imagination that this definition is different from what preceded it. His statement: '(and according to this: it is)' i.e., according to what the later logicians held, and it is based on his understanding that this definition opposes the definition of the earlier logicians, and you have known what is in it. His statement: '(so if you say: it necessarily follows)' he followed in this question al-Hilali, and he is an objector in several respects: First, it was his right to have brought it as part of the objections and answered it, but al-Hilali brought it as a question, so he followed him. Second, that he built it on the disagreement between the earlier and later logicians, and you have known what is in it. Third, that it is also built on the understanding (fahm) being the addressee, while the verification is otherwise, as verified by the seal of the verifiers, our master al-Tayyib. So the statement of this commentator: 'due to the absence of an understander' contains a consideration; because the understander is Allah—exalted is He—who knows the meanings of His speech in His pre-eternity, and the intended meaning of 'fahm' is not the addressee; because of what would follow from that of the non-indication of His speech—exalted is He—on all His knowledge even in what is yet to come, due to the absence of an addressee understander. How can the intellect and transmission both agree on the indication of speech on all information? i.e., its attachment to them? And the meaning of 'fahm' with respect to Him is metaphorical, not intended in its true sense; rather the intended meaning is knowledge of the signified from the sign. It cannot be said: 'His knowledge—exalted is He—of information from the speech indicating them requires the temporal origination of His knowledge while it is eternal.' For we say: 'If the indication is eternal, that does not follow.' And by that it is determined that 'min' in their saying 'fahm amr min amr' is a min of beginning (ibdtida'iyya), not of explanation (taliliyya). His statement: '(and that is false)' i.e., then the saying of the earlier logicians that leads to this problematic result is false. I say: It is answered that the attribute from whose temporal origination the temporal origination of its described thing necessarily follows is the real attribute, whereas indication is merely an accidental relation to the sign, so from its temporal origination the temporal origination of the sign does not follow, just as the specific attachment (ta'alluq tanziziyy) of power is temporally originated, while power is eternal without doubt. His statement: '(so from its temporal origination the temporal origination of the sign does not follow)' the admission of the temporal origination of indication is false; because its meaning is attachment (ta'alluq); i.e., the attachment of the eternal speech to all known things, and it is a mental/essential (nafsi) attribute, and the mental does not change or differ, so its temporal origination is not possible. And it will come shortly from this commentator that the attachment of speech which is indication is eternal like the speech, and the analogy with the specific attachment (ta'alluq tanziziyy) is invalid because of its temporal origination and the eternity of indication.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the later logicians' definition of 'indication' (dalala). The author begins by stating that the later logicians define dalala as 'al-haythiyya'—the property of being such that from one thing another can be understood, whether or not it is actually understood. Another expression: the property of being such that knowledge of one thing necessitates knowledge of another. According to this, describing the sign (al-dal) with indication before actual understanding is a real description, not metaphorical. The author then presents an objection: the earlier logicians defined dalala as 'understanding itself' (fahm). If that were the case, then the speech of Allah, which is eternal (qadim), would have no indication before the existence of a human understander; and if indication were temporally originated (hadith), its subject (the speech) would also be temporally originated, which is false because Allah's speech is eternal. The author resolves this by explaining that the earlier and later definitions are actually in agreement. The earlier logicians, when they said 'understanding', meant the property of the word that it is such that meaning is understood from it, not the act of understanding itself. The later logicians, with their definition of 'haythiyya', mean exactly this property—the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding. So the supposed conflict is only verbal. The objection based on Allah's speech is then answered: indication is not a real attribute (sifa haqiqiyya) inhering in the sign; it is merely a relation (nisba 'arida). The temporal origination of a relation does not entail the temporal origination of its subject. For example, the specific volitional attachment (ta'alluq tanziziyy) of God's power (qudra) is temporally originated, but the power itself is eternal. The hashia then adds a refinement: the correct understanding is that the attachment of speech to its meanings is eternal (nafsi), not temporally originated, so the analogy with power is imperfect. Thus, the definition of dalala as a relation is consistent with the eternity of Allah's speech and its eternal indication of all things known.

الحَيْثِيَّة
الدَّال

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the temporal origination of dalala not imply the temporal origination of the sign (e.g., Allah's speech)?
A) Because the sign is eternal and cannot be affected.
B) Because dalala is a real attribute that inheres separately.
C) Because dalala is an accidental relation, not a real attribute inhering in the sign.
D) Because the earlier definition was incorrect.

Key Takeaway
Indication (dalala) is an accidental relation, not a real attribute; this allows it to be temporally originated (or eternal) without affecting the eternity of its subject, reconciling the definitions and defending the eternity of Allah's speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Identify the genus and differentia in the definition of 'wahi' (revelation) given by a mutakallim of your choice. Does it fit the structure of hadd or rasm? Use the definition dissector tool above.
?
Task 2: An objector says: 'If Allah's speech is eternal, then it must indicate everything eternally, but new events occur; so either new indications arise (making it temporal) or the speech changes.' Analyze this objection using the conditional reasoning form: state the antecedent, consequent, and the valid form of response (modus tollens or affirming antecedent?).

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
5 min
Ibn 'Aradun on Rational Indication: The Quran's Words Point to Eternal Speech
Ibn 'Aradun argues that the indication of Quranic words to the internal speech is rational, not conventional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish rational indication (dalala 'aqliyya) from conventional indication (dalala wad'iyya) using the example of a request and apply this distinction to the Quranic words and eternal divine speech.

Core Idea
The Quran's words to eternal speech: rational inference, not linguistic convention.

How do we know that the Quran's words point to an eternal speech in God's essence? Ibn 'Aradun argues that this is not a matter of linguistic convention (wad'), but a rational inference based on our experience of how speech works. When someone says 'Give me water,' we understand not only the external command but also that the speaker has an internal desire for water. Similarly, the Quran's words rationally indicate an eternal divine speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of indication
Conventional indication (dalala wad'iyya) is the original assignment of words to meanings by the language setter. Rational indication (dalala 'aqliyya) is an inference made by reason beyond the conventional meaning, based on experience.
Keep this distinction clear: wad' is fixed by language; 'aql is based on reason and common experience.
2
Analyse the example: 'Give me water to drink'
The words conventionally indicate the external act of giving water. Rationally, we infer that the speaker desires water and has that speech in his conscience (qiyam al-talab bi-nafsihi). This inference is not from the language setter but from reason via inner awareness (wijdan).
The text emphasizes that the language setter only placed words for external referents, not for inner states.
3
Apply to the Quran and eternal speech
The Quranic words have conventional meanings (rules, stories). But they also rationally indicate that there is an eternal speech in God's essence, because speech typically arises from an internal state of the speaker. This rational inference is based on the same principle as the water example.
This is a key theological argument in Ash'ari kalam: the Quran's created words point to an uncreated divine attribute.
4
Note the clarification about logical entailment
Al-Qismatini explains that this rational indication is not a logical necessity (luzum 'aqli) but a judgment based on inner awareness (wijdan). It is an experiential inference, not a purely deductive one.
This prevents the critique that rational indication requires strict proof; it is a reasonable inference from common experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاخْتَارَ ابْنُ عَرَضُونَ فِي شَرْحِ الحَفِيدَةِ : أَنَّ دَلَالَةَ القُرْآنِ عَلَى الكَلَامِ القَدِيمِ عَقْلِيَّةٌ ؛ قَالَ: كَدَلَالَةِ اسْقِنِي المَاءَ» ؛ عَلَى أَنَّ المُتَكَلَّمَ بِهِ مُقْتَضِ فِي نَفْسِهِ لِلْمَاءِ، وَأَنَّهُ مُتَحَدِّثُ فِي ضَمِيرِهِ بِذَلِكَ. قوله : (فِي شَرْحِ الحَفِيدَةِ) هي للسنوسي . وجزم العلامة القسمْطِيني بأنَّها عقليَّةٌ كما عند ابن عرضون، ووجهه : بأن قول القائل: «اسقني الماء» يدلُّ على قيام الطَّلب بنفسه، وليست دلالته عليه بالوضع؛ لأنَّ الواضع إنَّما وضع الألفاظ لتدلَّ على المسمَّيات الكائنة في الخارج، وأمَّا أنَّ من تكلَّم بها قد قامت معان بباطنه، فهذا القدر لا تعرّض للواضع إليه ، وإِنَّما هو أمرٌ يحكم به العقل من جهة الوجدان، وهذا المراد بالدلالة العقلية، وليس المراد بها أنَّ الألفاظ ملزومةٌ عقلاً ؛ لقيام معان بنفس المتكلم بها . اهـ .
And Ibn 'Aradun chose in his commentary on al-Hafida (or al-'Aqida) that the indication of the Quran to the eternal speech is rational; he said: like the indication of 'Give me water to drink' on the fact that the speaker desires water in his soul and is speaking about it in his conscience. His saying: (in the commentary on al-Hafida) it is by al-Sanusi. And the distinguished scholar al-Qismatini affirmed that it is rational as according to Ibn 'Aradun, and its explanation: that the saying of the speaker 'Give me water to drink' indicates the existence of a request in his soul, and its indication is not by convention (wad'); because the setter of language only placed words to indicate the external referents. As for the fact that one who speaks these words has meanings in his inner self, this aspect the setter of language did not address; it is rather something that the reason judges through inner awareness. This is what is meant by rational indication. It is not meant that the words are entailed by reason because meanings subsist in the speaker's soul. End.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the relationship between the Quranic words and the eternal divine speech. Ibn 'Aradun and al-Qismatini hold that this indication is rational ('aqliyya), not conventional (wad'iyya). The example given is the command 'Give me water to drink' (isqini al-ma'). When someone says this, we rationally infer that the speaker has a desire for water in his soul, even though the words themselves conventionally refer to the external act of giving. The conventional meaning is the external act, but the additional inference that the speaker has an internal desire is made by reason, not by language. Similarly, when we hear the Quran, we rationally infer that there is an eternal speech in the Divine Essence that corresponds to these words. This rational inference is based on experienced knowledge (wijdan) that speech typically indicates a speaker's internal state. The commentator clarifies that 'rational indication' here does not mean a logical entailment (luzum 'aqli) but rather a rational judgment based on common experience.

Key Terms
دلالة عقلية (dalala 'aqliyya): Rational indication; a relation between a sign and its meaning that is known by reason, not by linguistic convention. [Note: In later logic, 'aqliyya can also refer to entailment relations; here it is based on experiential reason.]
الوضع (al-wad'): Linguistic convention; the original assignment of words to meanings by the language setter. [Note: Stable in usul and logic.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Aradun, what kind of indication does the Quran have to the eternal speech?
A) Conventional indication (wad'iyya)
B) Rational indication ('aqliyya)
C) Both conventional and rational
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Ibn 'Aradun argues that the Quran's words rationally indicate God's eternal speech, not by linguistic convention, but by a rational inference based on the experienced relationship between speech and inner states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take another example from Islamic theology: the indication of a miracle (like the splitting of the moon) to the truthfulness of the Prophet. Is that indication conventional or rational? Explain using the criteria of Ibn 'Aradun.
?
Suppose someone says 'I want you to give me water' in a language you do not know. How would you rationally infer that they desire water? How does this analogy apply to the Quran and eternal speech?
